Crawford v. Fisher


NO. 2014-CA-01606-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


213 So. 3d 44; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 522



December 15, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Crawford v. Fisher, 2017 Miss. LEXIS 84 (Miss., Mar. 2, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CIRCUIT COURT OF THE FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HINDS COUNTY. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/29/2014. TRIAL JUDGE: JAMES W. CRAIG. TRIAL COURT ATTORNEYS: JAMES W. CRAIG, VANESSA JUDITH CARROLL, WILSON DOUGLAS MINOR.

COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CIRCUIT COURT OF THE FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HINDS COUNTY. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/29/2014. TRIAL JUDGE: JAMES W. CRAIG.
Crawford v. State, 716 So. 2d 1028, 1998 Miss. LEXIS 100 (Miss., 1998)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The circuit court erred in finding that an inmate had the same or similar claims pending before the supreme court at the time his 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 lawsuit was filed because in his motion for leave to file a successive petition for post-conviction relief, the inmate presented no argument relating in any manner to the method-of-execution issue that was pleaded in his § 1983 suit; [3]-The circuit court erroneously dismissed the inmate's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 lawsuit on the basis of a factual misapprehension because the inmate could proceed with his § 1983 claim in state court; [2]-The United States Supreme Court had held that method-of-execution claims could be brought pursuant to § 1983.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

3 of 603 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Hood v. Louisville Tire Center, Inc.


NO. 2015-CA-01175-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2009-CA-00052-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


204 So. 3d 1250; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 504



December 8, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WINSTON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/02/2015. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOSEPH KILGORE.
State ex rel. Hood v. Louisville Tire Center, Inc., 55 So. 3d 1068, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 141 (Miss., 2011)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether a chancery court properly granted a business corporation's motion to dismiss a suit by the State of Mississippi, through the Office of the Attorney General of Mississippi, for want of prosecution under Miss. R. Civ. P. 41(b). HOLDINGS: [1]-The court did not abuse its discretion in determining that the delay was inexcusable because, following the remand of the case, the case was stagnant on the court docket for approximately three years and staffing issues and settlement negotiations did not provide a legitimate excuse for the delay. Furthermore, substantial evidence supported the court's determination that the corporation was prejudiced by the passage of time due to the death of an individual who was of central importance to the corporation's defense of the action; [2]-The chancery court did not abuse its discretion in determining that lesser sanctions were not sufficient.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

4 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Walters v. State


NO. 2015-KA-01332-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


206 So. 3d 524; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 503



December 1, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Walters v. State, 2017 Miss. LEXIS 136 (Miss., Apr. 6, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/11/2015. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN HUEY EMFINGER. TRIAL COURT ATTORNEYS: DEWEY ARTHUR, LEE WILKINS, EDWARD RAINER, GARY WILLIAMS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Since the amendment to Miss. Code Ann. § 97-17-41, that occurred between the time of the alleged larceny and trial did not specifically provide that the Legislature intended it to apply retroactively, under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-1 (2015), the trial court did not err in instructing the jury on the elements of grand larceny as they existed at the time the crime was committed; [2]-The trial court did not err in quashing the subpoena of codefendant, who was being tried separately, because, on the advice of counsel, codefendant indicated an intent to invoke his Fifth Amendment privilege as to all questions defense counsel would have asked him; [3]-The trial court did not err in admitting Google Earth images of defendant's property, because the State made a prima facie showing that the photographs accurately depicted his property on the dates at issue.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

5 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Carson v. State


NO. 2013-KA-02011-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


212 So. 3d 22; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 473



November 17, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Carson v. State, 2017 Miss. LEXIS 62 (Miss., Feb. 16, 2017)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Carson v. Mississippi, 2017 U.S. LEXIS 7069 (U.S., Nov. 27, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MADISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/07/2013. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN HUEY EMFINGER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-While trial counsel was deficient for failing to request an accomplice-testimony instruction, as the State used such testimony to identify defendant as the shooter, the deficient performance did not prejudice the defense, as the jury heard testimony from a nonaccomplice witness that defendant admitted his involvement in the robbery and could have deduced from accomplice's testimony that he had an incentive to lie; [2]-The trial court did not err in failing to give two proposed jury instructions, because the instructions given fairly announced the law, covering the presumption of innocence and the necessity of ignoring unfounded suspicion and speculation during deliberations; [3]-The omission of the name of the victim did not render the indictment fatally flawed, as it was not an element of the crimes charged.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

6 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Miss. Dep't of Revenue v. AT&T Corp.


NO. 2015-CA-00600-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


202 So. 3d 1207; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 448



October 27, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CHANCERY COURT OF THE FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HINDS COUNTY. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/19/2015. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM H. SINGLETARY. TRIAL COURT ATTORNEYS: LAURA HUDDLESTON CARTER, BRIDGETTE TRENETTE THOMAS, GARY WOOD STRINGER, JOHN FLOYD FLETCHER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Miss. Code Ann. § 27-7-15(4)(i) (2013) violated the dormant commerce clause under the internal consistency test because appellee taxpayer's dividend income from in-state subsidiaries was excluded from income, while such income from out-of-state subsidiaries was not, as it had not already borne a tax under the statute, resulting in malapportionment; [2]-The appropriate remedy was to delete the phrase "under the provisions of this article" from the statute because this preserved legislative intent to include dividend income in the definition of income, while allowing an exemption to taxpayers who already had borne a tax in Mississippi or another state.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

7 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Wells v. State


NO. 2015-KA-01483-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


202 So. 3d 1230; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 445



October 27, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CIRCUIT COURT OF THE FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARRISON COUNTY. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/09/2015. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROGER T. CLARK. TRIAL COURT ATTORNEYS: MITCHELL LANCE OWEN JAMES LLOYD DAVIS, III.
Wells v. State, 160 So. 3d 1136, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 85 (Miss., 2015)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant as an habitual offender under Miss. Code Ann. 99-19-81 (2007) to thirty years without the possibility of probation or parole for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(a)(1) (2005), because it was the maximum prison penalty at the time of his original sentence pursuant to § 41-29-139(b)(1)(A); [2]-Defendant's original sentence was imposed when the maximum sentence prescribed for the crime of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute was thirty years, and the statute that lowered the maximum penalty did not take effect until more than five years after he received his initial sentence; [3]-The supreme court limited the trial court's consideration on remand to whether it would apply a subsequent drug offender enhancement.


OUTCOME: Sentence affirmed.

 

8 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Pascagoula- Gautier Sch. Dist. v. Bd. of Supervisors


NO. 2014-CA-01774-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


212 So. 3d 742; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 437



October 20, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by, in part, Motion granted by, in part Pascagoula-Gautier Sch. Dist. v. Bd. of Supervisors, 2017 Miss. LEXIS 109 (Miss., Mar. 23, 2017)
Rehearing denied by Pascagoula-Gautier Sch. Dist. v. Bd. of Supervisors, 2017 Miss. LEXIS 116 (Miss., Mar. 23, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/19/2014. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. SAMAC S. RICHARDSON.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A school district and a city had standing to sue a county board of supervisors to challenge its approval of tax assessments on a company's leasehold interest in property it leased from the county because they experienced an adverse effect from the board's conduct, and that adverse effect was different from that experienced by the general public; [2]-The district was the direct beneficiary of the school district taxes assessed on the property, the city was the taxing authority for the school district taxes on the property, both the district and the city had statutory duties associated with the taxes, Miss. Code Ann. § 37-57-104(1) (Rev. 2014), and their funding was reduced by any allegedly improperly low tax assessment; [3]-The trial court erred by failing to join the company as a party under Miss. R. Civ. P. 19(2) because it had claimed an interest in the subject matter.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.

 

9 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Smith


NO. 2015-CA-00213-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


206 So. 3d 502; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 423



October 13, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Smith v. Smith, 2017 Miss. LEXIS 15 (Miss., Jan. 12, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/11/2014. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. SANFORD R. STECKLER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A chancellor's award of physical and legal custody of the children to the father was not a rejection of the GAL's visitation recommendation, and the error in rejecting the recommendation for a neutral counselor without saying why was harmless given that years had passed since the initial custody award; [2]-Ample evidence existed for the chancellor to make a custody decision where the GAL had investigated the sexual-abuse allegations and secured and coordinated with experts to assess the claims, and the evidence included forensic interviews and extensive testimony; [3]-The chancellor's Albright analysis was affirmed where it was clear that the mother's credibility, judgment, and behavior were weighed against her, contributing to the chancellor finding it was in the children's best interests that the father have custody.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

10 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Carr v. State


NO. 2014-CA-00726-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


196 So. 3d 926; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 324



August 11, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: QUITMAN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/17/2013 TRIAL JUDGE: HON. CHARLES E. WEBSTER. TRIAL COURT ATTORNEYS: GLENN S. SWARTZFAGER. LOUWLYNN VANZETTA WILLIAMS, JASON L. DAVIS.
Carr v. State, 655 So. 2d 824, 1995 Miss. LEXIS 56 (Miss., 1995)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court held that it was not unconstitutional for defendant to bear the burden of proving that he was intellectually disabled for capital sentencing purposes; [2]-The trial court erred by holding that defendant was not intellectually disabled where it applied an incorrect legal standard by treating defendant's IQ score of between 70 and 75 alone as dispositive of the case and by failing to balance and analyze his adaptive functioning deficits with his IQ score, even though the trial court found that defendant had proved the existence of two adaptive functioning deficits. The case was remanded for the trial court to consider whether defendant's adaptive functioning deficits were so severe that he should be ruled intellectually disabled.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case remanded.

 

11 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Colburn v. State


NO. 2014-KA-01368-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


201 So. 3d 462; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 323



August 11, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Colburn v. State, 2016 Miss. LEXIS 440 (Miss., Oct. 20, 2016)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Colburn v. Mississippi, 2017 U.S. LEXIS 1470 (U.S., Feb. 27, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/19/2014. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM E. CHAPMAN, III. TRIAL COURT ATTORNEYS: LARRY BAKER, JAMES GIDDY, KELLY G. WILLIAMS, CATHY CRONIN COUGHLIN.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Mississippi Vulnerable Persons Act, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 43-47-1 to 43-47-39 (Rev. 2015), was not unconstitutionally vague, because, while the Legislature defined "vulnerable person" broadly, it defined the criminal offense with sufficient definiteness that ordinary people could understand what conduct was prohibited and in a manner that did not encourage arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement; [2]-The indictment satisfied Miss. Unif. Crim. R. Cir. Ct. Prac. 7.06, in that it fully notified defendant of the nature and cause of the accusation, as he the date ranges, the transactions, the banks, the account numbers, and the alleged victim of the crimes charged; [3]-The trial court did not err in excluding the victim's will and a letter, because evidence the victim left her estate to defendant would not have assisted the jury in determining if he took money before she died.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

12 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. State


NO. 2015-KA-00066-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


194 So. 3d 855; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 262



June 23, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WARREN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/25/2014. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ISADORE W. PATRICK, JR.
Wilson v. State, 198 So. 3d 408, 2016 Miss. App. LEXIS 149 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 22, 2016)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a receiving stolen property case, defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel was without merit; [2]-The trial court properly allowed a jury instruction which informed the jury that proof defendant stole the property in question was prima facie evidence that defendant knew that the property was stolen property; [3]-The trial court properly allowed a jury instruction which informed the jury that the State was not required to disprove defendant's alibi but rather that the State had to prove defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt; [4]-The trial court properly sentenced defendant to serve 10 years in prison; [5]-Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-1 (Rev. 2015) required the trial court to sentence defendant under the sentencing statute in place at the time of the crime.


OUTCOME: Conviction and sentence affirmed.

 

13 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Bester v. State


NO. 2013-CT-00058-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


188 So. 3d 526; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 153



April 14, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bester v. Mississippi, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 5029 (U.S., Oct. 3, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JONES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/26/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BILLY JOE LANDRUM.
Bester v. State, 188 So. 3d 576, 2014 Miss. App. LEXIS 410 (Miss. Ct. App., 2014)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the trial court had the authority to sentence petitioner to life imprisonment, absent a recommendation from the jury. HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court had authority under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-65(4)(a) (Rev. 2014) to sentence petitioner to life imprisonment, absent a recommendation from the jury, because the plain language of the statute authorized a trial court to sentence a defendant to imprisonment for any term as the court, in its discretion, it could determine; [2]-It was pernicious, i.e., harmful, for the supreme court to continue to exceed its constitutional authority by judicially amending § 97-3-65(4)(a) and limiting a judge's sentencing authority as established by the Legislature.


OUTCOME: Judgments affirmed.

 

14 of 603 DOCUMENTS


City of Gulfport v. Dedeaux Util. Co.


NO. 2014-CA-00556-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


187 So. 3d 139; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 130



March 24, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by, En banc City of Gulfport v. Dedeaux Util. Co., 2016 Miss. LEXIS 134 (Miss., Mar. 24, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY SPECIAL COURT OF EMINENT DOMAIN. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/14/2014. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM R. BARNETT. TRIAL COURT ATTORNEYS: GARY WHITE, HARRY M. ALLEN, PETER C. ABIDE.
Dedeaux Util. Co. v. City of Gulfport, 63 So. 3d 514, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 191 (Miss., 2011)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-When appellant city condemned appellee utility, it was no error to use of different valuation dates for different assets because the court was so instructed on remand, and this did not fail to value the utility as a "going concern"; [2]-It was no error to limit the city's setoff to revenues produced by assets added after a certain date because this was the Mississippi Supreme Court's intent; [3]-The city was properly required to pay interest from the date of filing the petition instead of the date of taking possession because there were two valuation dates; [4]-It was error to make the city pay interest under Miss. Code Ann. § 75-17-1(1) (2009) because Miss. Code Ann. § 75-17-7 (2009) was the applicable statute; [5]-It was no error to decline to order a new trial due to a compromise verdict because nothing showed the jury reached such a verdict.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part.

High v. Kuhn


NO. 2015-IA-00072-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


191 So. 3d 113; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 121



March 17, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by High v. Kuhn, 2016 Miss. LEXIS 215 (Miss., May 26, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY SPECIAL COURT OF EMINENT DOMAIN. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/08/2015. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL H. WARD.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A special court of eminent domain erred as a matter of law when it granted a petition for private road access under Miss. Code Ann. § 65-7-201 because Miss. Const. art. 4, § 110 provided that such rights of way were not permissible in incorporated cities and towns; [2]-There was no waiver under Miss. Code Ann. § 11-27-15 because none of the enumerated grounds for dismissal applied to this case; [3]-There was no violation of the Equal Protection Clause under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and there were other available remedies besides Miss. Code Ann. § 65-7-201; [4]-There was no separate action for expenses brought, as required by Miss. Code Ann. § 11-27-37.


OUTCOME: Reversed and rendered.

 

16 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Hale v. State


NO. 2014-KA-01778-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


191 So. 3d 719; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 58



February 4, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified and rehearing denied by Hale v. State, 2016 Miss. LEXIS 205 (Miss., May 19, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/09/2014. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROGER T. CLARK. TRIAL COURT ATTORNEY: ROBERT C. STEWART.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the trial court erred at defendant's trial for sale or transfer of a controlled substance, under Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(a)(1) (2013), by denying defendant's proffered jury instructions on the defenses of involuntary intoxication and entrapment. HOLDINGS: [1]-Although defendant contended that an unforeseen interaction between his prescription medication and the grapefruit juice which he drank on the night in question caused him to become involuntarily intoxicated, and incapable of controlling his own actions, defendant failed to provide a sufficient evidentiary basis to support his proffered instruction on involuntary intoxication and other instructions covered his theory of the case. The court did not err in denying defendant's entrapment instruction because no rational jury could have found that defendant was induced by law-enforcement officers to commit a crime.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Green v. State


NO. 2013-CT-01228-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


183 So. 3d 28; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 43



January 28, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: ADAMS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/07/2013. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FORREST A. JOHNSON, JR.
Green v. State, 183 So. 3d 78, 2015 Miss. App. LEXIS 29 (Miss. Ct. App., Jan. 20, 2015)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a case involving multiple counts of being a felon in possession of a firearm under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-5(1), because defendant did not raise an objection on the basis of double jeopardy or raise the issue on appeal, the only avenue for review was the plain error doctrine under Miss. R. App. P. 28(a)(3) and Miss. R. Evid. 103(d); [2]-The trial court did not deviate from or misapply a legal rule in a plain, clear, or obvious way because the double jeopardy rule had not been raised or discussed in prior cases involving multiple counts of this offense; [3]-Using plain error in this specific instance would have been inappropriate.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

18 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Bradley v. Jordan


NO. 2014-CA-01710-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


182 So. 3d 439; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 28



January 21, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAUDERDALE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/12/2014. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LESTER F. WILLIAMSON, JR. TRIAL COURT ATTORNEYS: DONALD W. BOYKIN, CHRISTOPHER MICHAEL FALGOUT.
Bradley v. State, 934 So. 2d 1018, 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 1015 (Miss. Ct. App., 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the statute of limitations had run on any claims that a client may have had as to his court appointed attorney's negligence or professional malpractice, when the client alleged that his attorney failed to investigate whether the client had served one year or more on the two sentences used to support the client's habitual-offender status and failed to raise this defense at the client's sentencing hearing. HOLDINGS: [1]-The client knew that his attorney had acted negligently when the client was sentenced as a habitual offender because the client admitted that, at the time of his sentencing, he informed his attorney that he had not served a full year on one of his convictions. As such, the client's suit was time-barred, under Miss. Code § 15-1-49, because the three-year statute of limitations began to run from the date of his sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

19 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Atwood v. State


NO. 2015-CA-00190-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


183 So. 3d 843; 2016 Miss. LEXIS 18



January 14, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WAYNE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/21/2015. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT WALTER BAILEY. TRIAL COURT ATTORNEYS: LISA HOWELL, PHILLIP WEINBERG, ANDY DAVIS.
Atwood v. State, 2016 Miss. LEXIS 21 (Miss., Jan. 14, 2016)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-It was error to determine that Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-37(5)(a) (Rev. 2015), which provided for graduated penalties for technical violations for probation and supervised release, was unconstitutional as violative of separation of powers because there was nothing in the amendments to this statute that impinged upon a trial court's ability to enforce its orders; [2]-The trial court retained its authority to determine whether there was a violation of a condition of supervised release, as well as the power to revoke the term of supervision and to impose a period of imprisonment; [3]-The Mississippi Legislature merely altered the term and place of imprisonment for certain violations; [4]-Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-29 could not have been relied upon as authority to revoke post-release supervision since it addressed suspended sentences and conditional pardons.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

 

20 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Vaughn v. Public Emples. Ret. Sys. of Miss.


NO. 2013-CT-01179-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


182 So. 3d 433; 2015 Miss. LEXIS 559



November 12, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Vaughn v. Pub. Employees' Ret. Sys., 2016 Miss. LEXIS 59 (Miss., Feb. 4, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/21/2013. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WINSTON L. KIDD.
Vaughn v. Public Emples. Ret. Sys. of Miss., 182 So. 3d 446, 2015 Miss. App. LEXIS 62 (Miss. Ct. App., Feb. 10, 2015)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-While it was error for the Public Employees' Retirement System (PERS) and the lower courts to use Miss. Code Ann. §§ 25-11-115 and 25-11-117.1 (Rev. 2010) to determine who received a retiree's benefits after her death and the death of her named beneficiary, where all involved should have looked to Miss. Code Ann. § 25-11-115(1) (Rev. 1999) as part and parcel of the contract between the retiree and PERS, the application of § 25-11-117.1(1) was harmless error where the end result was substantially similar to that for which the retiree contracted.


OUTCOME: Decisions affirmed.

Czekala-Chathamfiled v. State ex rel. Hood


NO. 2014-CA-00008-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


195 So. 3d 187; 2015 Miss. LEXIS 638

November 5, 2015, Filed

22 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Parish v. State


NO. 2014-KM-01401-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


176 So. 3d 781; 2015 Miss. LEXIS 529



October 22, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/29/2014. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN HUEY EMFINGER. TRIAL COURT ATTORNEYS: KEVIN D. CAMP, JARED K. TOMLINSON, WHITNEY M. ADAMS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The prosecution presented sufficient evidence that defendant was driving under the influence of marijuana in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30(1)(d) (Rev. 2013) because a police observed that defendant had dilated pupils, reddened eyes, and slurred speech, and defendant exhibited eyelid and leg tremors while performing a sobriety test; [2]-Defendant's blood tests revealed the presence of active metabolites for marijuana, meaning he was still experiencing the pharmacological effects of the drug even after he was arrested, and he admitted to smoking marijuana twenty minutes prior to encountering the officer; [4]-The evidence was sufficient to prove not only that defendant had ingested marijuana before driving but that he was driving in a state of intoxication that lessened a person's normal ability for clarity and control.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed.

SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


212 So. 3d 804; 2015 Miss. LEXIS 496



October 1, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Williams v. Clark Sand Co., 2016 Miss. LEXIS 10 (Miss., Jan. 7, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/27/2014. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT P. KREBS. TRIAL COURT ATTORNEYS: FRED KRUTZ, III, DANIEL J. MULHOLLAND, COLLEEN S. WELCH, JOHN T. GIVENS, R. ALLEN SMITH, JR., TIMOTHY W. PORTER, PATRICK MALOUF, EDWIN S. GAULT, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The circuit court properly granted a corporation summary judgment because an individual's claims were barred; [2]-The Florida corporate-dissolution and survival statute, Fla. Stat. § 607.1407, applied, and the individual failed to file suit prior to the corporation's dissolution; [3]-Corporate-survival statutes, specifically § 607.1407, were not statutes of limitation; [4]-Section 607.1407 was not in conflict with the Mississippi corporate-survival statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 79-4-14.07 (Rev. 2013), thus, there was no conflict requiring application of the center-of-gravity test; [4]-Pursuant to the Full Faith and Credit Clause, U.S. Const. art. IV, § 1, the Florida organization and dissolution laws were entitled to enforcement in Mississippi.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MISSISSIPPI PUBLIC SERVICE COMMISSION. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/22/2012. TRIAL COURT ATTORNEYS: BEN HARRY STONE, RICKY J. COX, MICHAEL ADELMAN, CHRISTA R. BISHOP, C. STEPHEN STACK, SHAWN S. SHURDEN.

DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Appellee Public Service Commission's (Commission) approval of appellee utility's rate increase for "mirror construction work in progress" (mirror CWIP) costs was not an illegal tax because the rate was not paid to or used for government support; [2]-It was error to approve the increase because the Commission did not find costs were "prudently incurred," under Miss. DISPOSITION: VACATED IN PART AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether a sheriff or a circuit court was to oversee and compensate bailiffs. HOLDINGS: [1]-Under Miss. OUTCOME: Judgment vacated in part and rendered.

Parker v. Benoist


NO. 2012-CA-02010-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


160 So. 3d 198; 2015 Miss. LEXIS 113



February 19, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: YALOBUSHA COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/20, 2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. PERCY L. LYNCHARD, JR.
Parker v. Benoist, 2014 Miss. LEXIS 431 (Miss., Aug. 28, 2014)



DISPOSITION: ON DIRECT APPEAL: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART. ON CROSS-APPEAL: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether Mississippi law was to recognize a good-faith and probable-cause exception to a forfeiture in terrorem clause in a will. HOLDINGS: [1]-Forfeiture provisions in wills in Mississippi were enforceable unless a will contest was founded upon probable cause and made in good faith; [2]-The forfeiture provision in the decedent's will was unenforceable against the complainant because her will contest was based upon probable cause and was brought in good faith. Thus, she was entitled to her inheritance as provided in the will; [3]-The trial court did not abuse its discretion in permitting the executor to remove estate assets to pay attorneys to represent the estate during the will contest. However, the chancellor erred in refusing to remove the executor under the will upon finding that the complainant's evidence in support of the executor's removal was not uncontested.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed and rendered in part, and reversed and case remanded in part.

Chunn v. State ex rel. Miss. Dep't of Ins.

SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


156 So. 3d 884; 2015 Miss. LEXIS 36



January 22, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/05/2013. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM A. GOWAN, JR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The licensing requirement, Miss. Code Ann. § 83-39-3(2) (Rev. 2011), violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution where the State failed to articulate any rationale basis for precluding all felons, regardless of the nature or age of the felony, from holding bail-agent licenses; [2]-Because Miss. OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; case remanded.

Sallie v. State


NO. 2012-CT-01280-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


155 So. 3d 760; 2015 Miss. LEXIS 38



January 22, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by Sallie v. State, 2016 Miss. App. LEXIS 776 (Miss. Ct. App., Dec. 6, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MADISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/25/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN HUEY EMFINGER.
Sallie v. State, 155 So. 3d 872, 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 833 (Miss. Ct. App., 2013)



DISPOSITION: THE JUDGMENTS OF THE COURT OF APPEALS AND THE MADISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT ARE AFFIRMED IN PART AND VACATED IN PART, AND THIS CASE IS REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The jury was required find the elements of the firearm enhancement, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-37(2) (Rev. 2014), beyond a reasonable doubt under Apprendi before a trial court was allowed to apply the enhancement; [2]-Given the elements of the crimes as listed in the jury instructions, the jury in the instant case found the elements of the firearm enhancement beyond a reasonable doubt; [3]-Defendant failed to receive fair notice that the firearm sentence enhancement was being sought where his indictment did not indicate that the State would seek any sentence enhancement, the State in no way indicated pretrial that it would seek the firearm enhancement, and only after the jury convicted defendant did he receive any indication that the trial court might have considered the enhancement at trial.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; sentence vacated; case remanded.

Hotboxxx, LLC v. City of Gulfport


NO. 2013-CA-00939-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


154 So. 3d 21; 2015 Miss. LEXIS 1



January 8, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/28/2013. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. SANFORD R. STECKLER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The chancery court erred in dismissing, on res judicata grounds, the LLC's action challenging a city ordinance restricting the areas in which adult businesses could be located where a federal court's dismissal on the grounds that the LLC lacked standing was not an adjudication on the merits, and the issue of standing in Mississippi courts was based on a different standard than in federal court; [2]-Under Mississippi law, the LLC lacked standing where the LLC's business license application was incomplete, and its lease for a building in which it planned to run an adult entertainment business was pendent on obtaining the appropriate license, and thus, was void and did not confer standing.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Cowart v. State


NO. 2012-KA-02051-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


178 So. 3d 651; 2015 Miss. LEXIS 2



January 8, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PIKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/05/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DAVID H. STRONG, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The four photographs depicting the injuries that caused the victim's death, while likely prejudicial, especially in light of the fact that the victim was connected to life support machines in three of them, were not so gruesome and inflammatory that the trial court abused its discretion in determining that their probative value outweighed their prejudicial effect; [2]-Since defendant was acquitted of manslaughter and murder, his challenge to the jury instruction on manslaughter was moot; [3]-Defendant's challenge the voluntariness of his statements was procedurally barred, as he pointed to nothing in the record to support his argument that the waiver of his rights and his statements were not knowing, intelligent, and voluntary; [4]-The sentence imposed, which did not exceed the statutory maximum, was not constitutionally infirm.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

44 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Bell v. State


NO. 2013-KA-00389-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


160 So. 3d 188; 2015 Miss. LEXIS 4



January 8, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Bell v. State, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 167 (Miss., Apr. 9, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GRENADA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/22/2013. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOSEPH H. LOPER, JR.
Bell v. State, 725 So. 2d 836, 1998 Miss. LEXIS 305 (Miss., 1998)



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-107 (Rev. 2007) did not apply when an individual's death sentence was rendered unconstitutional, but did apply if, and only if, the United States Supreme Court or the Mississippi Supreme Court rendered a wholesale declaration that the death penalty as a sentence to anyone was unconstitutional; [2]-Since defendant's sentence of death was unconstitutional because he had been determined to be mentally retarded, but the entire statute had not been declared unconstitutional, the circuit court erred in applying § 99-19-107 to his case.


OUTCOME: Sentence vacated; case remanded for resentencing to life imprisonment.

Trinity Yachts, LLC v. Mike & Jerry's Paint & Supply (In re Lien)


NO. 2012-IA-01667-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2013-CA-01155-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


152 So. 3d 286; 2014 Miss. LEXIS 602



December 11, 2014, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/18/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN C. GARGIULO.

COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/11/2013. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN C. GARGIULO.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED. AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a case in which the owner of two multimillion-dollar yachts under construction at the owner's shipyard challenged a lien the unpaid paint supplier established and enforced on the yachts under Miss. Code Ann § 85-7-31 (Rev. 2011) of the Water Craft Seizure Act, the trial court did not err in granting summary judgment in favor of the owner because privity did not exist between the owner and the paint supplier; the specification of the brand of paint and the painter supplier in the contract between the owner and the independent contractor did not establish privity between the owner and the paint supplier as it did not confer rights or impose obligations on the paint supplier; and the amendment to the master service agreement did not operate retroactively to create privity between the owner and the paint supplier sufficient to create a lien in the paint supplier's favor.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; interlocutory appeal dismissed.

Foster v. State, 148 So. 3d 1045, 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 135 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 26, 2013)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.

OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant failed to preserve for appellate review his contention that his 40-year sentence for armed robbery should be vacated as it equated to a life sentence because in arguing that his sentence exceeded his estimated life expectancy defendant went outside the record, as neither the websites he referred to in his brief nor the arguments first presented on appeal were presented to the trial court; [2]-The trial court did not abuse its discretion by sentencing defendant to 40 years because it conformed to Miss. Polk v. State


NO. 2013-CA-00701-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


150 So. 3d 967; 2014 Miss. LEXIS 497



October 9, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 15, 2014.
Rehearing denied by Polk v. State, 2014 Miss. LEXIS 588 (Miss., Dec. 4, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: OKTIBBEHA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/26/2013. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES T. KITCHENS, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether a petitioner was entitled to have all records expunged relating to his earlier arrest and indictment when he pleaded guilty to one count and the district attorney retired to files the remaining two counts, based upon the petitioner's entering a plea of guilty as to the one count, and the petitioner subsequently received a full, complete, and unconditional pardon from the Governor of Mississippi. HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court correctly denied the petitioner's petition to expunge the record(s) pertaining to his criminal conviction because there was no statutory basis for expungement of the record of the criminal conviction for which the petitioner was pardoned; [2]-As to the petitioner's criminal records pertaining to the counts which were remanded to file based on his guilty plea, those records were eligible for expungement pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-15-26(5).


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part. Case remanded for further proceedings.

McCoy v. State


NO. 2013-KA-00390-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


147 So. 3d 333; 2014 Miss. LEXIS 470



September 18, 2014, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: UNION COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/01/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW K. HOWORTH.
McCoy v. State, 47 So. 3d 1197, 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 619 (Miss. Ct. App., 2010)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's sentences were not constitutionally disproportionate because they fit well within the limits of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-79; [2]-The fact that defendant was a first-time offender did not preclude the trial court from imposing up to the maximum sentence; [3]-The trial court did not err by failing to declare a mistrial sue sponte based on statements by the prosecutor because the statements, when taken into context, did not ask the jurors to put themselves in the victims' place to determine defendant's guilt; [4]-Even assuming that the prosecutor's isolated statement could constitute a golden-rule argument, there was no evidence suggesting that defendant was unduly prejudiced by the statement; [5]-The trial court's denial of defendant's Batson challenge was not clearly erroneous because the reasons offered by the State were race-neutral and supported by the record.


OUTCOME: Convictions and sentences affirmed.

Parker v. Benoist


NO. 2012-CA-02010-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


2014 Miss. LEXIS 431



August 28, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Remanded by, in part Parker v. Benoist, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 113 (Miss., Feb. 19, 2015)
Rehearing denied by Parker v. Benoist, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 111 (Miss., Feb. 19, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: YALOBUSHA COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/20/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. PERCY L. LYNCHARD, JR.



DISPOSITION: ON DIRECT APPEAL: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART. ON CROSS APPEAL: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether Mississippi law recognized a good faith and probable cause exception to a forfeiture in terrorem clause in a will. HOLDINGS: [1]-The chancery court erred in excluding a daughter from a testator's will because the daughter sufficiently showed that her suit alleging that her brother unduly influenced the testator was brought in good faith and was founded upon probable cause; [2]-To allow the enforcement of a forfeiture clause, regardless of a good faith challenge based upon probable cause, would be unconstitutional under Miss. Const. art. 3 § 24 and against public policy; [3]-Forfeiture provisions in wills were enforceable unless a contest was brought in good faith and based on probable cause; [4]-The daughter's claim was based upon the fact that she understood her parents' intentions in mutual reciprocal wills to be that she and her brother "share and share alike."


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

Rehearing denied by Gillett v. State, 2014 Miss. LEXIS 471 (Miss., Sept. 18, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/05/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT B. HELFRICH.
Gillett v. State, 56 So. 3d 469, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 337 (Miss., 2010)



DISPOSITION: POST-CONVICTION COLLATERAL RELIEF IS GRANTED IN PART AND DENIED IN PART. THE SENTENCES OF DEATH ARE VACATED, AND THE CASE IS REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT OF FORREST COUNTY FOR A NEW SENTENCING HEARING.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-An inmate's due-process rights were violated when the jury was allowed to consider an invalid aggravator supported by evidence that was not otherwise admissible, and this error was compounded when the Supreme Court of Mississippi affirmed his sentence; [2]-Because the Supreme Court did not find that the constitutional error at the trial-court level was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt, and because the Court declined to reweigh the aggravators and mitigating evidence, the inmate's sentences of death were vacated.


OUTCOME: Postconviction relief granted; case remanded for resentencing.

Rice v. State

134 So. 3d 292; 2014 Miss. LEXIS 160



March 20, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Rice v. State, 2014 Miss. LEXIS 277 (Miss., June 5, 2014)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Rice v. Miss., 2014 U.S. LEXIS 6230 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SUNFLOWER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/11/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. ASHLEY HINES. TRIAL COURT ATTORNEYS: DAVID LEE RICE, PRO SE. JACQUELINE SMITH.
Rice v. State, 723 So. 2d 1239, 1998 Miss. App. LEXIS 961 (Miss. Ct. App., 1998)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court correctly counted petitioner's pre-conviction jail time as time served in a third cause under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-83 (Rev. 2007) and found that petitioner had served more than one year of his sentence in that cause because the time he served toward his sentence in a second cause while awaiting trial in the third cause began to count as time served in the third cause when the two sentences were ordered to run concurrently; [2]-Each day served on petitioner's sentence in the second cause would also count as time served in the third cause, and because petitioner's sentence in the third cause was ordered to run concurrently with his sentence in the second cause, which he was already serving, the Mississippi Department of Corrections began calculating his sentences for both causes the day his probation was revoked and he was first incarcerated.


OUTCOME: Denial of petition for post-conviction relief affirmed.

Earthgrains Bakery Group, Inc. v. Miss. Dep't of Empl. Sec.


NO. 2012-CC-01522-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


131 So. 3d 1163; 2014 Miss. LEXIS 99; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P8370



February 13, 2014, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/04/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. TOMIE T. GREEN.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether a corporation's distributors were employees of the corporation, specifically, agent drivers or commission drivers under the Mississippi Employment Security Law, Miss. Code Ann. § 71-5-11(J)(2)(a) (Rev. 2011), for the purpose of receiving unemployment benefits. HOLDINGS: [1]-The administrative law judge's (ALJ) decision that the independent operator distributors were agent and commissioned drivers for the corporation was erroneous because the ALJ failed to apply the law correctly, and the decision was not supported by substantial evidence; [2]-The distributors did not receive remuneration for services from the corporation because they were not being paid a salary, wages, or commission by the corporation, and they did not have personal service contracts with the corporation, so they did not satisfy the requirements for classification as employees under § 71-5-11(J)(2).


OUTCOME: Order reversed and judgment rendered in favor of corporation.

Keller v. State

February 6, 2014, Decided

Noone v. Noone


NO. 2012-CA-01849-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


127 So. 3d 193; 2013 Miss. LEXIS 647



December 12, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: COPIAH COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/22/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. EDWARD E. PATTEN, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A spouse was not entitled to a partition of property owned as joint tenants with rights of survivorship by a chancery court decree based on Miss. Code Ann. § 11-21-1 (Supp. 2013); [2]-The Mississippi Legislature's decision to use the phrase ""homestead property exempt from execution" in other statutes identified the specific type of property that the Legislature wanted to protect; [3]-The phrase did not intend to bring the specific limitations on creditors' rights to other, unrelated statutes; [4]-The power of judicial review did not extend to invalidating statutes as against public policy.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Hall v. State


NO. 2012-KA-01282-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


127 So. 3d 202; 2013 Miss. LEXIS 649



December 12, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Hall v. State, 2016 Miss. LEXIS 123 (Miss., Mar. 17, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/10/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT B. HELFRICH.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the trial court erred in granting the State's requested instruction on accessory after the fact to burglary. HOLDINGS: [1]-Only a defendant, not the State could request a lesser-included offense instruction; [2]-The State was not entitled to instructions which allowed the jury to convict defendant of the lesser offense of accessory after the fact; [3]-Notwithstanding defendant's inartful objection, the trial court committed plain error when it granted the two supplementary instructions; [4]-Accessory after the fact was a lesser nonincluded offense of the principal offense; [5]-The trial erred in denying defendant's motion for JNOV, which requested that the jury verdict of guilty for accessory after the fact be set aside.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed, and his sentence was vacated.

Dees v. State


NO. 2012-KA-01128-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


126 So. 3d 21; 2013 Miss. LEXIS 593



November 21, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TIPPAH COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/09/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT WILLIAM ELLIOTT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The circumstantial evidence presented by the State was sufficient to sustain defendant's arson conviction; [2]-Reasonable jurors could have rejected a defense expert's testimony in favor of the testimony of the State's witnesses and found beyond a reasonable doubt that the fire to defendant's home did not have an electrical cause and was incendiary; [3]-A rational jury could have concluded from defendant's financial situation and the strong evidence supporting her prior commission of insurance fraud that defendant had the motive to burn down her house and recover the insurance proceeds; [4]-Evidence that defendant defrauded an insurance plan was sufficient to sustain her insurance fraud conviction.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court did not err in finding that defendant's Miranda rights waiver was knowing, intelligent, and voluntary; [2]-Because the four-fold warning inherently incorporated the right of a suspect to stop answering questions and to cease the interrogation at anytime he or she wished, the absence of an explicit warning of that right did not affect whether defendant's waiver was knowing, intelligent, and voluntary; [3]-Defendant went voluntarily to the police station to be interrogated, he was adequately informed of his Miranda rights before he signed the waiver, the interrogating officer thought he was very intelligent, and he voluntarily handwrote his own statement for the police; [4]-His learning disability did not rise to the level of mental disability required to have interfered with his ability to waive his rights since he possessed the capacity to waive his rights.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:

HOLDINGS: [1]-Although the trial court based appellee's recovery on an oral contract rather than on quantum meruit, prejudgment interest was not justified because there was a bona fide dispute as to the amount of damages, and prejudgment interest was unavailable under Miss. Code Ann. § 85-7-151 in an action to enforce a contractor's lien.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed. The judgment of the trial court was affirmed in part and reversed in part.

Borne v. Estate of Carraway, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 552 (Miss., Nov. 1, 2012)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART, AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether lake owners, a homeowners association (HOA), and a city were properly found liable for repairs to a homeowner's property caused by a sinkhole formed after a culvert system failed. HOLDINGS: [1]-As the chancellor found that the homeowner's widow first learned of the sinkhole less than three years before suit was filed, she did not clearly err in finding that the complaint was timely filed under the discovery rule; [2]-The chancellor erred by imposing joint and several liability on the city, lake owners, and HOA; as she did not find that they had colluded to commit a tortious act, joint and several liability was not permitted under Miss. Code Ann. § 85-5-7(2); [3]-As the HOA had the right to control water overflowing from a lake onto downstream properties, the chancellor properly found, on riparian principles, that the HOA had a duty of reasonable care to control the water.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part.

Galloway v. State


NO. 2010-DP-01927-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


122 So. 3d 614; 2013 Miss. LEXIS 328



June 6, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Galloway v. State, 2013 Miss. LEXIS 509 (Miss., Sept. 26, 2013)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Galloway v. Mississippi, 134 S. Ct. 2661, 189 L. Ed. 2d 209, 2014 U.S. LEXIS 3685 (U.S., May 27, 2014)
Motion granted by, Request denied by, Motion denied by Galloway v. State, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 168 (Miss., Apr. 9, 2015)
Later proceeding at Galloway v. State, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 292 (Miss., May 21, 2015)
Motion dismissed by, Without prejudice, En banc Galloway v. State, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 534 (Miss., Oct. 22, 2015)
Later proceeding at Galloway v. State, 2017 Miss. LEXIS 142 (Miss., Apr. 13, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/24/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROGER T. CLARK.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of capital murder and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court committed reversible error by allowing the admission of DNA test results without providing defendant the opportunity to confront the DNA analyst who did the testing in violation of his confrontation rights under U.S. Const. amend. VI. The supreme court disagreed. The record illustrated that the witness, as the technical reviewer assigned to the case, was familiar with each step of the complex testing process conducted by the analyst, and the witness performed her own analysis of the data. The witness personally analyzed the data generated by each test conducted by the analyst and signed the report. Given the witness's knowledge about the underlying testing process and the report itself, any questions regarding the accuracy of the report due to possible contamination of the DNA samples could have been asked of the witness. Consistent with the holding in Grim, no Confrontation Clause violation occurred in the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed. Sentence vacated. Case remanded for resentencing.

Post-conviction proceeding at, Motion granted by, Stay granted by Batiste v. State, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 86 (Miss., Feb. 12, 2015)
Post-conviction proceeding at Batiste v. State, 2016 Miss. LEXIS 27 (Miss., Jan. 21, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: OKTIBBEHA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/31/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES T. KITCHENS, JR.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant in the Oktibbeha County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of capital murder with the underlying felony of robbery, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(e) (2006). The jury determined that defendant was to suffer the death penalty. Accordingly, the circuit court sentenced defendant to suffer death by lethal injection until death was pronounced. The circuit court denied defendant's post-trial motions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stated in his confession that he killed the victim during a fight, left the apartment for approximately an hour and a half, and then returned and began a clean-up effort when he was discovered by a sheriff's deputy. OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Grayson v. State


NO. 2012-DR-00059-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


118 So. 3d 118; 2013 Miss. LEXIS 163



April 18, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Grayson v. State, 2013 Miss. LEXIS 411 (Miss., Aug. 8, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GEORGE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/08/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KATHY KING JACKSON.
Grayson v. State, 806 So. 2d 241, 2001 Miss. LEXIS 303 (Miss., 2001)



DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR LEAVE TO FILE SUCCESSOR PETITION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF IS DISMISSED AS PROCEDURALLY BARRED. LEAVE TO PROCEED IN THE CIRCUIT COURT WITH A MOTION FOR ACCESS IS GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate, who had been sentenced to death, filed a motion for leave to file a successor petition for postconviction relief (PCR) and for leave to proceed in the circuit court with a motion for access.


OVERVIEW: In his motion for leave to file a successor petition for PCR, petitioner argued that counsel in his first PCR action had been ineffective under U.S. Const. amend. VI. The court first stated that because PCR proceedings were a critical stage of the death-penalty appeal process at the state level, PCR petitioners who were under a sentence of death did have a right to the effective assistance of PCR counsel. It held that PCR counsel had been deficient. Because none of petitioner's present claims for relief were meritorious, however, petitioner had not suffered prejudice. He had failed to show that his claims met any exceptions to the procedural bars. Next, petitioner sought access to his experts for the purpose of evaluation, testing, and any other purpose reasonably believed by counsel to be necessary for the full litigation of his postconviction claims. The court stated that as a matter of due process, prisoners sentenced to death should be granted access to their experts so long as the access complied with the rules and regulations of the Mississippi Department of Corrections and so long as those rules and regulations did not violate due process.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the motion for leave to file a successor petition. It granted petitioner's motion for leave to proceed in the circuit court with a motion for access.

 

79 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth Brands v. Morgan


NO. 2011-CA-01274-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


110 So. 3d 752; 2013 Miss. LEXIS 141



April 4, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/18/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. PATRICIA D. WISE.



DISPOSITION: ON DIRECT APPEAL: REVERSED AND REMANDED. ON CROSS-APPEAL: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a nonsettling manufacturer (NSM) and two distributors (appellants), appealed an order entered by the Hinds County Chancery Court, Mississippi, which denied them a permanent injunction or a declaration that the NSM fee on cigarettes for sale outside Mississippi under the NSM law, Miss. Code Ann. § 27-70-5 (2010), violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, or the Due Process Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Appellee Commissioner of Revenue cross-appealed. The state's highest court held that if another state enacted a statute identical to the NSM law and a Mississippi distributor obtained cigarettes for sale outside of Mississippi, then Mississippi would impose a fee on a transaction and the other state would impose a fee on a transaction. If the cigarettes acquired by the Mississippi distributor were sold intrastate, they would be subject to only one fee. If another state enacted an identical statute, interstate commerce would bear a burden that intrastate commerce would not. Section 27-70-5 was not internally consistent and violated the Commerce Clause. The constitutionality of a state tax could not be challenged under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 in state court if an adequate remedy was available under state law. To the extent that Marx v. Truck Renting and Leasing Association Inc., 520 So. 2d 1333 (Miss. 1987), and Burrell v. Mississippi State Tax Commission, 536 So. 2d 848 (Miss. 1988) conflicted with National Private Truck, they were overruled. Appellants were not entitled to attorney's fees under § 1988 as they had an adequate remedy, which they invoked--declaratory relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court for the entry of a judgment consistent with the opinion.

 

80 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Falkner v. Stubbs


NO. 2010-CT-01664-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


2013 Miss. LEXIS 65



March 7, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, On rehearing at, Remanded by Falkner v. Stubbs, 2013 Miss. LEXIS 431 (Miss., Aug. 22, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CHICKASAW COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/01/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. HENRY L. LACKEY.
Falkner v. Stubbs, 2012 Miss. App. LEXIS 126 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 6, 2012)



DISPOSITION: THE JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF APPEALS IS AFFIRMED. THE JUDGMENT OF THE CHICKASAW COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT IS REVERSED AND THE CASE IS REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor sued appellee owners of a home, seeking damages for breach of contract based on work done on the home and a construction lien on the home. The trial court entered judgment for the contractor. The Court of Appeals of Mississippi affirmed the judgment, but reversed the award of attorney's fees and prejudgment interest. The contractor appealed.


OVERVIEW: There was no written contract for the work, but the trial court found that the contractor's recovery was based in quantum meruit. The appellate court found that there was no applicable statutory basis for the award of attorney's fees or prejudgment interest even if the contractor's recovery was based solely on an express contract rather than quantum meruit. No award of prejudgment interest may have been made where the principal amount was not fixed before judgment. An award of prejudgment interest under Miss. Code Ann. § 75-17-1 was improper where a claim for damages was unliquidated. The same considerations which precluded a recovery of prejudgment interest for unliquidated amounts owed under § 75-17-1 applied to Miss. Code Ann. § 87-7-3. Here, the amount of the contractor's claim was clearly in dispute, and the trial court resorted to quantum meruit to fix the exact amount of damages. There was no finding that the owners disputed the amount owed in bad faith. Attorney's fees were available only when expressly provided for in either a statute or contract, or when there was sufficient proof to award punitive damages. Miss. Code § 85-7-181 was inapplicable to this case.


OUTCOME: The decision of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed and the case was remanded to the trial court for a final determination of the contractor's award without prejudgment interest or attorney's fees.

Jones County Sch. Dist. v. Miss. Dep't of Revenue


NO. 2011-CA-00712-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


111 So. 3d 588; 2013 Miss. LEXIS 71; 180 Oil & Gas Rep. 689



March 7, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Jones County Sch. Dist. v. Miss. Dep't of Revenue, 2013 Miss. LEXIS 260 (Miss., May 2, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JONES COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/02/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FRANKLIN C. MCKENZIE, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A school district sought a refund of oil and gas severance taxes paid on its royalty interests derived from oil and gas production on sixteenth-section land. The Jones County Chancery Court (Mississippi) ruled that the school district was not liable for severance taxes and that a three-year statute of limitations applied to the school district's refund claim. The Mississippi Department of Revenue and the school district appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the oil and gas severance taxes levied under Miss. Code Ann. §§ 27-25-501 to 27-25-525 and 27-25-701 to 27-25-723 did not apply to the school district because the school district did not meet the definition of a "person" subject to the taxes and there was no indication that the school district was subject to the taxes by necessary implication. A statute of limitations did not apply to the school district's refund claim because Miss. Const. art. IV, § 104 provided that statutes of limitation in civil causes did not run against the state or its subdivisions. It was necessary to remand the case so that the chancery court could determine whether the doctrines of waiver or estoppel applied. Under Miss. Code Ann. §§ 53-1-73 and 53-1-75, the school district was liable for administrative expense taxes on its royalty interests derived from oil and gas production on sixteenth-section land because the assessments were fees rather than taxes, Miss. Code Ann. § 53-1-71 expressly made the state and its subdivisions subject to the fees, and no constitutional provision or other law was violated by requiring school districts to pay the fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the chancery court's judgment insofar as it held that the school district was not liable for severance taxes and that the school district was liable for administrative expense taxes. The court reversed the chancery court's judgment to the extent that the chancery court held that a statute of limitations applied. The court remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

82 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Kee Brown v. State


NO. 2010-CT-00352-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


102 So. 3d 1087; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 610



December 13, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/02/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROGER T. CLARK.
Brown v. State, 2012 Miss. App. LEXIS 156 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 27, 2012)



DISPOSITION: THE JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF APPEALS IS REVERSED. THE JUDGMENT OF THE HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT IS AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Mississippi), which affirmed an order granting the State's motion to amend the grand jury's indictment to charge defendant as a habitual offender under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-83 (Rev. 2007) and convicting him of felony escape.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled that a prior conviction for burglary satisfied the violent-crime requirement for habitual-offender status, even though the State had produced no evidence that the burglary involved violence. On appeal, defendant contended that burglary of a dwelling was not a "crime of violence" within the meaning of § 99-19-83. The supreme court held that burglary of a dwelling was not a per se "crime of violence" under § 99-19-83. The Legislature was free to enact a statute that makes burglary of a dwelling a per se crime of violence, but it had not chosen to do so, and the supreme court declined to assume that the legislature intended to do so. Absent such a statute, or proof of an actual act of violence during the commission of a burglary, burglary of a dwelling was not a violent crime for purposes of § 99-19-83. The fact that the Legislature did not choose to provide a list of "crimes of violence" that applied under § 99-19-83 did not render the statute ineffective.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for sentencing.

Knight v. Public Emples. Ret. Sys. of Miss.


NO. 2010-CT-01586-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


108 So. 3d 912; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 611



December 13, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Knight v. Public Emples. Ret. Sys. of Miss., 2013 Miss. LEXIS 82 (Miss., Mar. 21, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/30/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. SWAN YERGER.
Knight v. Public Emples. Ret. Sys. of Miss., 108 So. 3d 941, 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 749 (Miss. Ct. App., Dec. 6, 2011)



DISPOSITION: THE JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF APPEALS IS REVERSED. THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT OF HINDS COUNTY IS REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The circuit court affirmed the decision of the Mississippi Public Employees Retirement System (PERS) to deny disability benefits to a former state employee. She appealed; the Mississippi Court of Appeals affirmed. She sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed an application for retirement benefits with PERS, seeking non-duty-related disability benefits. She claimed to be disabled by severe foot pain, numbness, and swelling. She resigned from her job, which required her to be on her feet most of the day, because of the increasing severity of the pain. PERS denied her claim for disability benefits, finding that as she presented no objective medical evidence of the cause of her pain, there was no proof it was caused by illness. The high court disagreed. Two physicians opined that her objective symptoms were likely caused by peripheral neuropathy. With a doctor's statements that she could not continue the tasks required of her job (walking long distances) and that she was at a maximum medical improvement, she presented enough medical evidence under Miss. Code Ann. § 25-11-113(1)(a) (Supp. 2012) to show that she was physically incapacitated for the job she was employed to do, that it was likely permanent, and that she should be retired.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed and the judgment of the circuit court was reversed and rendered.

Patton v. State


NO. 2011-KP-00106-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI

December 13, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended February 12, 2013.

Motion denied by Patton v. State, 2013 Miss. LEXIS 135 (Miss., Mar. 28, 2013)
Motion to strike denied by Patton v. State, 2013 Miss. LEXIS 138 (Miss., Mar. 28, 2013)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Patton v. Mississippi, 134 S. Ct. 687, 187 L. Ed. 2d 556, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 8618 (U.S., 2013)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied Patton v. Mississippi, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 125753 (N.D. Miss., Sept. 14, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WINSTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/07/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FRANK G. VOLLOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Winston County (Mississippi), which convicted him of false pretence in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-19-39 (Rev. 2006) and fraudulent use of identity in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-19-85 (Rev. 2006).


OVERVIEW: The supreme court held that the circuit judge did not abuse his discretion in denying defendant's motion for recusal. Defendant made no showing that the judge engaged in any improper ex parte communications or "earwigging" or that he had any personal knowledge of the disputed facts of defendant's case prior to trial. Pretrial, the circuit judge read the case files, read the indictments, spoke with the supreme court concerning his appointment, and spoke with his nephew as to whether the nephew had been involved in defendant's case. The circuit judge also made clear that his communication pretrial was for administrative purposes only, and he was not discussing the merits of the case. The communications did not violate Miss. Unif. Cir. & Cty. R. 1.10 and were not improper. The amendment to the indictment charging defendant with false pretense did not prejudice defendant, and the circuit court did not err in allowing the amendment under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-5(1) (Rev. 2007) to change the charge to attempt to commit false pretense. Defendant was on notice that he could be convicted of attempt to commit any of the offenses with which he was charged in the indictment.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment.

Coleman & Coleman Enters. v. Waller Funeral Home


NO. 2011-CA-00697-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


106 So. 3d 309; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 570



November 15, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Coleman & Coleman Enters. v. Waller Funeral Home, 2013 Miss. LEXIS 43 (Miss., Feb. 7, 2013)
Rehearing denied by Coleman & Coleman Enters., Inc. v. Waller Funeral Home, 2013 Miss. LEXIS 45 (Miss., Feb. 7, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAFAYETTE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/13/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT WILLIAM ELLIOTT.
Estate of Parham v. Waller Funeral Home, Inc., 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 99223 (N.D. Miss., Sept. 28, 2006)



DISPOSITION: ON DIRECT APPEAL: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED. ON CROSS-APPEAL: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a funeral home and customer, sought a declaration that appellee funeral home's prepaid funeral services contracts were transferable by its customers. Appellee filed counterclaims alleging tortious interference with contract and false advertising. The Lafayette County Circuit Court (Mississippi) granted appellee partial summary judgment, finding its contracts were nontransferable. The jury found for appellee; both sides appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant home advertised it would perform funeral services for persons who had preneed contracts with other providers. Appellee denied the customer's request to transfer his contract to appellant home; this suit followed. The high court held that as appellee's contracts lacked a revocation clause, the trial court properly held they were irrevocable under former Miss. Code Ann. § 75-63-63 and were not unilaterally transferable by its customers. Appellee's claims of tortious interference with the contracts of customers still living at the time of trial failed; it could not prove any actual damages, since those customers had irrevocable, nontransferable contracts with appellee to be performed after they died. As the jury found this to be an exceptional case of false advertising, appellee was properly awarded attorney's fees under 15 U.S.C.S. § 1117(a) of the Lanham Act. Pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 11-1-65(3)(a)(iv), the trial court properly reduced the punitive damage award to $ 0 based on appellant home's negative net worth; appellee having failed to adduce proof of appellant home's net worth during the punitive phase, it could not complain of the reduced verdict on appeal.


OUTCOME: The damage award to appellee on its tortious interference claim was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial on damages. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.


 

86 of 603 DOCUMENTS



Allcock v. Bannister


NO. 2011-CA-00289-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


106 So. 3d 790; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 549



November 1, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Allcock v. Bannister, 2013 Miss. LEXIS 107 (Miss., Feb. 21, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/20/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN C. GARGIULO.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a judgment entered in favor of appellees, a doctor and the doctor's clinic, in the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi) in her wrongful death action. She argued that the trial court erred in denying her motion to amend the pretrial order and in granting the doctor and clinic a new trial because of a faulty jury instruction.


OVERVIEW: The mother's son died as a result of calcium chloride in his IV bag. The mother argued that she did not have her expert witness testify to rebut the testimony of the expert of the doctor and clinic. The supreme court held that the trial court did not err by denying the mother's motion to amend the pretrial order. The mother did not move to add her witness as an expert until six months after the discovery deadline. The doctor and clinic disclosed their expert's testimony before the mother's disclosure deadline. They maintained at trial that the doctor did not order any amount of calcium chloride. Thus, their disclosure placed the mother on sufficient notice that their expert would testify to the contents of the IV bag. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by granting a new trial. The jury instruction stated an incorrect rule of law. It required the jury to find the doctor at fault if the nursing staff improperly administered an IV bag. It imposed liability on the doctor for the nurse's actions that were not committed under the direction or control of the physician. Therefore, the instruction incorrectly imposed vicarious liability on the doctor for the nurse's actions.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment.
