Borne v. Estate of Carraway


NO. 2011-CA-00267-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


2012 Miss. LEXIS 552



November 1, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at Borne v. Estate of T. L. Carraway, 2013 Miss. LEXIS 373 (Miss., July 18, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/21/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DENISE OWENS.
Borne v. Estate of T. L. Carraway, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 557 (Miss., Nov. 1, 2012)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner (for whom plaintiff estate and trust were substituted after his death) sued defendants, his neighbors and a homeowners association, alleging their negligence caused a sinkhole to develop on his land. Defendants sued third-party defendant city for indemnity. The Hinds County Chancery Court (Mississippi) found defendants and the city jointly and severally liable for the costs of repairs; they appealed.


OVERVIEW: A culvert system that caused a sinkhole on plaintiff's land drained a lake owned by the neighbors and maintained by the association. The trial court found that 1) the city's sewer-line repairs, along with defendants' failure to repair and maintain the culvert system, caused the sinkhole; 2) the neighbors had an easement by necessity, and the association had an easement by implication, in the culvert system; 3) defendants breached their duty of reasonable care in repairing and maintaining the easement; and 4) their indemnity claim against the city failed since they also participated in the wrongdoing. The appellate court held that as the trial court found that plaintiff had first learned of the sinkhole less than three years before filing suit, it properly found the complaint was timely under the discovery rule, Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-49(2) (2003). As the trial court did not find that defendants and the city had colluded to commit a tortious act, its imposition of joint and several liability on them was not permitted under Miss Code Ann. § 85-5-7(4) (2011). After properly dismissing defendants' indemnity claim, the trial court erred by not rendering judgment for the city.


OUTCOME: The portion of the trial court's judgment ordering joint and several liability and awarding damages against the city was reversed, judgment was rendered in favor of the city, and the case was remanded for apportionment of liability between the neighbors and association in direct proportion to percentage of their fault, in accordance with § 85-5-7(5). The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Diamond Grove Ctr., LLC v. Miss. State Dep't of Health


NO. 2011-SA-01128-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


98 So. 3d 1068; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 506



October 11, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/25/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. J. DEWAYNE THOMAS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Mississippi Department of Health (DOH) approved a certificate of need (CON) application filed by appellee, a behavioral health center in Warren County, to add twenty adolescent psychiatric beds in Warren County, Miss. Code Ann. § 41-7-191(4)(a)(iii) (Rev. 2009). Appellant, a behavioral health center in Winston County, appealed from the judgment of the Hinds County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which affirmed the DOH's decision.


OVERVIEW: In 1995, the DOH had approved a CON for twenty adolescent psychiatric beds in Warren County but the CON was never acted upon; the CON was the property of a sister company of the Winston County center. Upon filing the application, the Warren County center acknowledged the existence of a legislatively imposed state-wide moratorium on such beds, but relied as the basis for its application on § 41-7-191(4)(a)(iii), which the Warren County center asserted provided an exception to the moratorium by expressly authorizing twenty such beds to be put into service in Warren County. The Winston County center argued the Legislature enacted § 41-7-191(4)(a)(iii) simply to authorize a one-time grant of a CON for Warren County, and did not intend for the CON grant to "remain valid indefinitely." However, the DOH properly determined that because no beds had ever been established in Warren County under § 41-7-191(4)(a)(iii), the exception to the moratorium on adolescent psychiatric beds remained available to the DOH. The Winston County center's "one-time grant" argument undermined the purpose of the exception.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

89 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Rowland v. State


NO. 2011-CA-00813-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


98 So. 3d 1032; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 484



October 4, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended October 12, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WASHINGTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/26/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. ASHLEY HINES.
Rowland v. State, 42 So. 3d 503, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 386 (Miss., 2010)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Washington County Circuit Court (Mississippi) to two counts of capital murder and two counts of armed robbery. He filed a post-conviction-relief petition, claiming that the trial court had placed him in double jeopardy by convicting him of capital murder and the underlying felony of armed robbery. The circuit court denied the motion; after an appeal and remand, it again denied the motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and two others robbed a poker game in progress, killing two of the poker players. The capital murder indictments charged the armed robberies of the two murder victims, naming them, and also included the words "and others." The trial court held that the jury could have found that the murder victims were not victims of armed robbery and still found defendant guilty of the capital murders based on the armed robbery of the other victims. The court rejected this conclusion. The identity of the victim of the underlying felony was an element of the offense of capital murder that was required to be stated in the capital-murder indictment. Accordingly, defendant could not have been convicted on an indictment of capital-murder based on the "armed robbery of others;" his capital-murder convictions had to have been based on the armed robberies of the named victims. Because he was convicted of capital-murder for killing during the commission of the armed robberies of the named murder victims, and then separately for the armed robberies of these same named victims, he was placed in double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's separate armed-robbery convictions and sentences and reverse the judgment of the circuit court denying his petition for post-conviction relief.

Miss. Dep't of Revenue v. AT&T Corp.


NO. 2010-SA-02013-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


101 So. 3d 1139; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 433



September 6, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Miss. Dep't of Revenue v. At&T Corp., 2012 Miss. LEXIS 603 (Miss., Dec. 6, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/16/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM H. SINGLETARY.
Miss. Dep't of Revenue v. AT&T Corp., 2012 Miss. LEXIS 440 (Miss., Sept. 6, 2012)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 11-13-11 (Rev. 2004) and former Miss. Code Ann. § 27-7-73 (1993), a taxpayer sued the Mississippi Department of Revenue, challenging the constitutionality of tax statutes. The Hinds County Chancery Court (Mississippi) held that former Miss. Code Ann. §§ 27-7-37(2)(a)(i) and 27-7-15(4)(i) violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, and awarded the taxpayer damages. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: After unsuccessful administrative appeals before the Department (formerly known as the Mississippi State Tax Commission), the taxpayer filed the instant suit. Instead of instituting a pre-deprivation lawsuit under § 11-13-11, challenging the lawfulness of tax collection via a Commerce Clause challenge to the statutes, the taxpayer paid the challenged income taxes and assessment. For this reason, held the high court, § 11-13-11 did not afford the trial court jurisdiction over the taxpayer's appeal. Further, the Department ordered that the taxpayer, pursuant to former § 27-7-73, had to pay the assessment within 30 days or file a petition and bond in the trial court requesting a hearing. By not paying the bond as required by § 27-7-73, the taxpayer failed to perfect its appeal; that the parties stipulated to the trial court's jurisdiction under § 27-7-73 was immaterial, as jurisdiction could not be conferred by consent. Therefore, the trial court did not have jurisdiction over the taxpayer's appeal, and the Department's findings became final.


OUTCOME: The trial court's orders were vacated and the order of the Department remained in effect.

Sears v. Learmonth


NO. 2011-FC-00143-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


95 So. 3d 633; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 422



August 23, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Learmonth v. Sears, Roebuck & Co., 631 F.3d 724, 2011 U.S. App. LEXIS 967 (5th Cir. Miss., 2011)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] CERTIFIED QUESTION DECLINED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motorist sued appellee, a truck driver's employer, for negligence. A jury awarded appellant damages, which were remitted by the federal district court pursuant to Miss. Code Ann 11-1-60(2)(b). Both parties appealed. The United States Court of Appeals for the Fifth Circuit certified this question: Was § 11-1-60(2), which generally limited noneconomic damages to $ 1 million in civil cases, constitutional?


OVERVIEW: The jury returned a unanimous general verdict for appellant in the amount of $ 4 million. The special interrogatory and jury verdict did not instruct the jury to itemize the compensatory damages into separate categories. The district court remitted the portion of the verdict that it deemed to represent noneconomic damages to $ 1 million. The high court noted that there was no evidence the parties ever entered into a binding stipulation as to what portion of the verdict represented economic damages and what portion represented noneconomic damages. Thus, the high court could not know with any degree of assurance that the jury awarded appellant more than $ 1 million for noneconomic damages. Accordingly, to rule on the constitutionality of § 11-1-60(2)(b) would require engaging in speculation and guesswork as to what amount the jury might have awarded in economic damages and what amount it might have awarded in noneconomic damages. Therefore, the high court declined to answer the certified constitutional question which, had the case arisen on direct appeal, it would not have reached under the facts presented.


OUTCOME: The request to answer the certified question was declined.

Rogers v. State


NO. 2010-KA-01191-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


95 So. 3d 623; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 399



August 16, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SCOTT COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/11/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MARCUS D. GORDON.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the Scott County Circuit Court (Mississippi), defendant was convicted of two counts of child sexual abuse; he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual battery against an eight-year-old boy (count one) and of fondling the boy's 11-year-old brother (count two). He argued that the trial court erred by overruling his hearsay objection to statements the younger boy made to a forensic psychologist. The high court agreed. The trial court erred in allowing the psychologist to testify about the younger boy's statement that defendant had put his mouth on the boy's penis, as the trial court made no finding as to the reliability of the statement and did not conduct a hearing outside the presence of the jury as required by Miss. R. Evid. 803(25). That defendant had confessed did not render the error harmless, as the boy's statement was the only evidence corroborating the confession. The older boy testified that defendant sodomized him while they were in a chicken house in Lena, Mississippi, which the boy believed was in Scott County. As Lena was in fact in Leake County, and the jury was never instructed that it had to find beyond a reasonable doubt that the crime had occurred in Scott County--an essential element of the offense--defendant's conviction of count two could not stand.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

93 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Hardison v. State


NO. 2009-KP-00233-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


94 So. 3d 1092; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 383



August 9, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/24/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. SWAN YERGER.
Hardison v. State, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 180 (Miss., Mar. 31, 2011)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of armed robbery. He argued that his right to a speedy trial under Sixth Amendment of the United States Constitution was violated and that the trial court denied his constitutional right to a jury of his peers when it sustained the State's objections to his peremptory challenges.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court held that defendant was not denied his Sixth Amendment right to a speedy trial. Not a single Barker factor weighed in defendant's favor, and one, reason for the delay, weighed heavily against him. The delay in bringing defendant to trial was more than three times the presumptively prejudicial eight-month mark. However, of the 833 days between indictment and trial, 701 were attributable to defendant. The denial of defendant's peremptory challenge without a proper Batson analysis constituted reversible error. The trial could erroneously denied defendant a peremptory strike by holding that a juror's previous service on a jury in a criminal case was not a race-neutral reason for the strike. During voir dire, the juror had expressed regret that the jury was unable to reach a verdict. Defendant's reason for the peremptory challenge, that the juror's responses about a prior jury experience indicated he could be pro-prosecution, qualified as race-neutral. The trial could never addressed the issue of pretext but simply held that the stated reason was not race-neutral. Under Miss. Unif. Cir. & Cty. R. 10.01, defendant had a right to twelve peremptory strikes.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial.

 

94 of 603 DOCUMENTS



Dialysis Solutions, LLC v. Miss. State Dep't of Health


NO. 2011-SA-01041-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


96 So. 3d 713; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 307



June 21, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Dialysis Solutions, LLC v. Miss. State Dep't of Health, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 461 (Miss., Sept. 20, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MISSISSIPPI STATE DEPARTMENT OF HEALTH - CERTIFICATE OF NEED. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/30/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: MARY CURRIER - EXECUTIVE DIRECTOR, MISSISSIPPI STATE DEPARTMENT OF HEALTH, STATE HEALTH OFFICER.
Dialysis Solutions, LLC v. State Dep't of Health, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 377 (Miss., Aug. 4, 2011)



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant health care provider sought a certificate of need from appellee Mississippi State Department of Health (MDH), and the MDH denied the application. Pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 41-7-201 (Supp. 2011), the provider sought judicial review in the Mississippi Supreme Court. The Court ordered briefing regarding whether Miss. Code Ann. § 41-7-201 (Supp. 2011) was constitutional under Miss. Const. art. VI, § 146.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court held Miss. Code Ann. § 41-7-201 (Supp. 2011), purporting to allow the provider to appeal directly to the supreme court, violated Miss. Const. art. VI, § 146 because it impermissibly conferred original jurisdiction on the supreme court, as, (1) under Miss. Const. art. I, §§ 1 - 2, the legislature could not confer jurisdiction on courts not given or authorized to be given by the Mississippi Constitution, (2) the "revisory" appellate jurisdiction conferred on the supreme court in Miss. Const. art. VI, § 146 applied only to judicial decisions rendered by a tribunal clothed with judicial power, (3) no certificate of need procedure existed at common law, (4) the nature of a certificate of need proceeding was permit-like and often nonadversarial, and (5) the final order of the MDH was issued by the State Health Officer, who was not statutorily required to be an attorney, under Miss. Code Ann. § 41-3-5.1 (2009), so the MDH lacked the indicia to be considered a tribunal of the character from which the legislature was authorized to grant appeals directly to the supreme court.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Hma v. Miss. State Dep't of Health


NO. 2011-IA-00196-SCT, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2011-IA-00211-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


98 So. 3d 980; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 294



June 14, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Jackson HMA, LLC v. Miss. State Dep't of Health, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 511 (Miss., Oct. 18, 2012)
Rehearing denied by Bd. of Trs. of State Insts. of Higher Learning v. Jackson HMA, LLC, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 514 (Miss., Oct. 18, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/19/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. PATRICIA D. WISE.
Jackson HMA, LLC v. Miss. State Dep't of Health, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 297 (Miss., June 14, 2012)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED. REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Three hospitals filed suit against the Mississippi Department of Health (MSDH) and the University of Mississippi Medical Center (UMMC), requesting declaratory and injunctive relief. The Hinds County Chancery Court (Mississippi) denied cross-motions for summary judgment, finding that genuine issues of material fact existed as to whether the Certificate of Need (CON) statutes, Miss. Code Ann. § 41-7-171 et seq., applied to UMMC.


OVERVIEW: UMMC filed an application for a CON with MSDH. When certain hospitals requested a public hearing in response to the application, MSDH sought two official opinions of the Attorney General (AG). In response to the second AG opinion, UMMC withdrew its application and requested a determination by MSDH of reviewability. MSDH granted the request, finding that UMMC was not required to obtain a CON for the proposed project under the State Health Plan. The hospitals then filed the instant action. The CON statutes applied to UMMC because it was included within the statute's definition of a "person" under Miss. Code Ann. § 41-7-173(p) (Rev. 2009). Furthermore, Miss. Code Ann. § 41-7-191(4)(a)(vi) demonstrated that the legislature intended the CON statutes to apply to UMMC. Finally, there was no conflict between the CON statutes and UMMC's creation statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 37-115-25 (Rev. 2007). However, Miss. Code Ann. § 41-7-191(1)(f) did not diminish the power of MSDH, delegated to it under Miss. Code Ann. § 41-7-187, to adopt rules and regulations to determine when a CON was required. Thus, MSDH had the authority to determine that UMMC did not require a CON for the proposed project.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that denied the medical center's motion for summary judgment, and rendered judgment granted the order. It affirmed the denial of the hospitals' motion for summary judgment.


 

96 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Pickering v. Langston


NO. 2010-CA-00362-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


88 So. 3d 1269; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 249



May 24, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Companion case at Pickering v. Hood ex rel. State, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 247 (Miss., May 24, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/24/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WINSTON L. KIDD.
Langston Law Firm v. Mississippi, 410 B.R. 150, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 95675 (S.D.N.Y., 2008)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state auditor filed an action against appellees, a law firm and its attorneys, seeking funds paid to the law firm as part of a settlement for a delinquent state tax liability. The Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) granted summary judgment to the law firm. The state auditor appealed.


OVERVIEW: A corporation settled its delinquent tax liability by paying sums to the State, a private charity, and the law firm, which was hired by the attorney general to pursue the claim. The state auditor demanded that the money paid to the charity and the law firm be turned over to the State because it constituted public funds. The charity complied, but the law firm refused, claiming that the payment of its fees was not made with public funds. First, the money paid to the law firm was part of the corporation's tax liability and, as such, constituted public funds under Miss. Code Ann. § 7-7-1 (Rev. 2002). Next, distribution of the public settlement funds to the law firm violated Miss. Const. art. 4, § 100, which required the tax liability to be paid into the state treasury. Furthermore, the attorney general failed to comply with Miss. Code Ann. § 7-5-7 (Rev. 2002), which required that any special assistants, such as the law firm, be paid from the attorney general's contingent fund or from other funds appropriated to the attorney general's office by the Legislature. Finally, the state auditor did not waive his right to proceed under Miss. Code Ann. § 7-7-211(g).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, and remanded the matter for disposition consistent with its opinion.

5K Farms, Inc. v. Miss. Dep't of Revenue


NO. 2009-CT-01787-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


94 So. 3d 221; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 233



May 10, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 16, 2012.
Rehearing denied by 5k Farms, Inc. v. Miss. Dep't of Revenue, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 407 (Miss., Aug. 16, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/21/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM H. SINGLETARY.
5K Farms, Inc. v. Miss. State Tax Comm'n, 94 So. 3d 291, 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 141 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 15, 2011)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Mississippi Department of Revenue (MDR) upheld the assessment of fees against appellant farm. The farm appealed and filed a motion for relief from the requirement to post a pretrial bond. The MDR objected to the motion and moved to dismiss; the trial court dismissed the case. The farm appealed; the Court of Appeals of Mississippi affirmed. The farm petitioned for a writ of certiorari, which was granted.


OVERVIEW: The farm filed a pauper's affidavit and a motion for an order allowing it to proceed without posting a pretrial bond. The trial court denied that motion, as it had no discretion to waive the bond requirement imposed by former Miss. Code Ann. §§ 27-77-5(7) and 27-77-7 (Rev. 2005). Since the farm had neither paid the bond nor paid the tax under protest, the trial court held that it lacked jurisdiction. The intermediate appellate court declined to consider the farm's constitutional challenge to §§ 27-77-5 and 27-77-7, because the farm had not raised that issue in the trial court. The high court granted certiorari solely to review whether the pretrial bond requirement derived from former §§ 27-77-5 and 27-77-7 related to appellate jurisdiction and was constitutional, or was procedural and unconstitutional. If procedural, it would have constituted an intrusion by the legislature into the assigned powers of the high court and of the judicial branch, and a violation of Miss. Const. art. VI, §§ 144 and 146. The high court found that the requirement of a pretrial bond related to appellate jurisdiction and therefore was within the powers of the legislature.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the lower courts were affirmed.


 

98 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Wilson


NO. 2010-CA-02002-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


90 So. 3d 51; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 219



May 3, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Smith v. Wilson, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 337 (Miss., June 28, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LOWNDES COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/29/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. H. J. DAVIDSON, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After their daughter's death, appellee grandparents filed an action requesting visitation with their grandchildren. The Lowndes County Chancery Court (Mississippi) granted the request pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 93-16-3(1) (Rev. 2004). Appellants, the children's father and his wife, sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellants argued that the grandparent-visitation statutes, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 93-16-3 and 93-16-5, and the Martin v. Coop factors were unconstitutional in light of Troxel v. Granville and violated their due process rights. The high court disagreed. Section 93-16-3 was narrower than the visitation statute the U.S. Supreme Court invalidated in Troxel, and the Martin factors prohibited chancellors from granting any visitation that would interfere with a parent's substantive due-process rights. The chancellor duly considered the father's wishes but was not required to defer to them, and found that visitation with the grandparents within the children's best interest. A finding of the father's unfitness was not a prerequisite to awarding the grandparents visitation. The chancellor's finding that appellants permanently intended to deny the grandparents visitation was supported by substantial evidence. The chancellor properly weighed and applied the Martin factors. The chancellor's award of visitation during the Thanksgiving and Christmas holidays in alternate years, two weeks in the summer, and phone calls once per week was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

99 of 603 DOCUMENTS



Johnson v. Sysco Food Servs.


NO. 2011-WC-01086-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


86 So. 3d 242; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 220



May 3, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by Johnson v. Sysco Food Servs., 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 628 (Miss. Ct. App., Sept. 24, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WORKERS' COMPENSATION COMMISSION. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/01/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LILES B. WILLIAMS.
Johnson v. Sysco Food Servs., 2011 Miss. LEXIS 383 (Miss., Aug. 11, 2011)



DISPOSITION: DIRECT APPEAL ASSIGNED TO THE COURT OF APPEALS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 71-3-51 (Rev. 2011), a claimant challenged the decision of the Mississippi Workers' Compensation Commission to deny his claim for benefits. A threshold issue was whether the amendment to § 71-3-51 that allowed direct appeals from the Commission to the state's high court was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Before the amendment to § 71-3-51, appeals from decisions of the Commission had to be filed in the circuit court. The high court directed the parties to brief the issue of whether the amendment to § 71-3-51 violated Miss. Const. art. VI, § 146, which delineated the limits of the high court's jurisdiction. The high court noted that Miss. Const. art. VI, § 146 granted it such jurisdiction as properly belonged to a court of appeal, which meant appeals of decisions rendered by a tribunal clothed with judicial power. The Commission was such a tribunal, as the legislature gave it the power and authority to make decisions that were conclusive and binding. Further, Miss. Const. art. VI, § 146 allowed the high court to exercise jurisdiction on matters provided by "general law, " and § 71-3-51 was a general law. Therefore, pursuant to Miss. Const. art. VI, § 146, the legislature was constitutionally empowered to confer appellate jurisdiction on the high court over direct appeals from the Commission.


OUTCOME: The high court held that it had jurisdiction over the appeal. As with all workers' compensation cases appealed to the high court, it assigned the case to the intermediate appellate court for decision.


 

100 of 603 DOCUMENTS



Estate of Gibson v. Magnolia Healthcare, Inc.


NO. 2010-CA-00741-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


91 So. 3d 616; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 186



April 12, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified July 19, 2012
Rehearing denied by, En banc, Modified by Estate of Gibson ex rel. Estate of Gibson v. Magnolia Healthcare, Inc., 2012 Miss. LEXIS 350 (Miss., July 19, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/09/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BETTY W. SANDERS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WASHINGTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DISPOSITION: ON DIRECT APPEAL: AFFIRMED. ON CROSS-APPEAL: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED - 04/12/2012. MOTION FOR REHEARING FILED: 05/15/2012.



DISPOSITION: DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant estate filed a wrongful death suit against appellees, a nursing home and its management company. The Washington County Circuit Court (Mississippi) denied the home's motions for a mistrial, did not allow the jury to consider appellant's request for punitive damages, reduced the compensatory damages award pursuant to Miss. Code § 11-1-60, and denied appellees' motions for judgment notwithstanding the verdict (JNOV). Both sides appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant alleged that the home negligently allowed the decedent to fall out of bed by failing to keep his bed rails upright, which caused injuries that contributed to his death. The trial court reduced the jury's compensatory damages award due to § 11-1-60's $ 500,000 cap on noneconomic damages in medical malpractice cases. The high court held that as the company's contractual duties were similar to those imposed under Mississippi law for a nursing home administrator and licensee, and there was no evidence it committed an individual wrong, it had been entitled to JNOV. As appellant submitted sufficient evidence that the home's negligence caused the decedent's injuries and that those injuries led to his death, the home was not entitled to JNOV. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the home's motions for a mistrial. The trial court properly declined to submit the punitive damages issue to the jury as it found there was no clear and convincing evidence that the home acted with willful, wanton, or reckless disregard for others' safety or committed fraud. Appellant's challenge to § 11-1-60's constitutionality, raised for the first time on appeal, was not reviewable.


OUTCOME: The high court reversed that part of the trial court's order denying the company's motions for directed verdict and judgment notwithstanding the verdict, and remand the matter to the trial court to dismiss with prejudice and strike the company's name from the final judgment. It affirmed as to all other issues.


 

101 of 603 DOCUMENTS



Pascagoula Sch. Dist. v. Tucker


NO. 2010-CA-00955-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


91 So. 3d 598; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 189



April 12, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Pascagoula Sch. Dist. v. Tucker, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 346 (Miss., July 19, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/13/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FRANKLIN C. MCKENZIE, JR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a school district and others, sued defendants, the State of Mississippi and county officials, challenging Miss. Code Ann. § 19-9-171 (2011), requiring the district to share ad valorem tax revenue it collected from gas terminals and oil refineries with other districts in the county where the terminals and refineries were located. The Jackson County, Mississippi, Chancery Court, found § 19-9-171 constitutional. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, three other school districts in the same county as plaintiff district, were allowed to intervene in the action. Plaintiffs argued that § 19-9-171 violated Miss. Const. art. VIII, § 206, which authorized a school district to levy an additional tax to maintain its schools, by forcing plaintiff district to divide its maintenance tax levy with other districts. The high court agreed. The plain language of art. VII, § 206 granted a district the authority to levy an ad valorem tax and mandated that the revenue collected be used to maintain only its schools. Conversely, no such authority was given for a district to levy an ad valorem tax to maintain schools outside its district. While Miss. Const. art. VIII, § 201 granted the Mississippi Legislature broad power to regulate school finance, the Legislature had no authority to mandate how the funds were distributed, as art. VIII, § 206 clearly stated that the purpose of the tax was to maintain the levying school district's schools. Thus, the plain language of art. VIII, § 206 that granted a school district the right to levy taxes to maintain its schools defined the limits of power granted to the Legislature by art. VIII, § 201.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.


 

102 of 603 DOCUMENTS



In re Hooker


NO. 2012-IA-00166-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


87 So. 3d 401; 2012 Miss. LEXIS 120; 101 A.L.R.6th 695



March 8, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition denied by, As moot In re Hooker, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 130 (Miss., Mar. 8, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/24/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. TOMIE T. GREEN.
In re Hooker, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 125 (Miss., Mar. 8, 2012)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the Attorney General of Mississippi, filed suit to void pardons the Governor of Mississippi had issued to appellant pardonees pursuant to Miss. Const. art. V, § 124. The Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) issued a temporary restraining order (TRO) requiring appellants to provide proof of publication complying with art. V, § 124 and barring the Mississippi Department of Corrections from releasing them. Appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: During his last days in office, the Governor granted executive clemency to appellants pursuant to Miss. Const. art. V, § 124. The Attorney General filed suit on behalf of the State of Mississippi, contending that appellants failed to publish notice of the petitions for pardons as required by art. V, § 124; he did not challenge the pardons' facial validity. The trial court issued a TRO prohibiting the Mississippi Department of Corrections from releasing appellants until it provided the trial court with sufficient proof of acceptable publication under art. V, § 124. The high court noted that compliance with constitutional provisions that were procedural in nature and committed solely to another branch of government was not justiciable. The exercise of the pardon power, vested solely with the Governor, was of a purely political nature. Under the separation-of-powers doctrine, a facially valid pardon issued by the Governor, who was the head of the coequal executive branch of government, could not be set aside or voided by the judicial branch, based solely on a claim that the procedural publication requirement of art. V, § 124 was not met, or that the publication was insufficient.


OUTCOME: The high court reversed and rendered the decision of the trial court, vacated the TRO, and rendered judgment dismissing the Attorney General's complaint and the action as barred by the doctrine of separation of powers.

Knox v. State


NO. 2010-CA-00814-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


75 So. 3d 1030; 2011 Miss. LEXIS 576



December 1, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/14/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM H. SINGLETARY.
Brawner v. State, 872 So. 2d 1, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 458 (Miss., 2004)
Puckett v. State, 737 So. 2d 322, 1999 Miss. LEXIS 122 (Miss., 1999)
Knox v. State, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 263 (Miss., May 20, 2010)
Walker v. State, 671 So. 2d 581, 1995 Miss. LEXIS 494 (Miss., 1995)
Stevens v. State, 806 So. 2d 1031, 2001 Miss. LEXIS 234 (Miss., 2001)
Simmons v. State, 869 So. 2d 995, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 49 (Miss., 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Sixteen death-sentenced inmates filed a complaint in the Chancery Court for the First Judicial District of Hinds County (Mississippi), alleging that they were deprived of their right to obtain meaningful state postconviction and federal habeas corpus review of their convictions and death sentences. The chancery court dismissed the complaint for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The inmates appealed.


OVERVIEW: The essence of the inmates' complaint was that there were defects in both the statutory structure and the performance of the Mississippi Office of Capital Post-Conviction Counsel (MOCPCC), and that the deficient performance of MOCPCC violated their right to the effective assistance of postconviction counsel in their death-penalty cases. The chancery court properly held that the inmates' attack on the death sentences and postconviction judicial reviews of their convictions was cognizable under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5 (Supp. 2011), a provision of the Uniform Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act (UPCCRA), Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-1 et seq. (2011), and, therefore, the chancery court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. Under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-7 (Supp. 2011), the Supreme Court of Mississippi was fully capable of considering the inmates' claims in individual applications to file a motion for postconviction relief. Furthermore, under the UPCCRA, the Supreme Court of Mississippi was the only state court with jurisdiction over the claims, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-27 (Supp. 2011).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Compere v. St. Dominic Jackson Mem. Hosp.


NO. 2010-CA-00490-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


71 So. 3d 607; 2011 Miss. LEXIS 472



September 29, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/11/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. SWAN YERGER.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient filed a second malpractice suit against appellees, a doctor and hospital. The prior suit, in which appellees had sought summary judgment due to his non-compliance with Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-36(15), was still pending. The Hinds County Circuit Court dismissed the first suit without prejudice, dismissed the second suit with prejudice, and imposed monetary sanctions on appellant's counsel for filing it. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mailed notice as required by Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-36(15) (2003) to appellees of his intent to file a malpractice action; however, he failed to wait the 60 days required by § 15-1-36(15) before he filed the first complaint. Due to that failure, appellants moved for summary judgment. Before the trial court ruled on that motion, appellant filed the instant suit. The trial court dismissed both suits and assessed monetary sanctions against appellant's counsel under Miss. R. Civ. P. 11 and Mississippi's Litigation Accountability Act of 1988, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-55-5, finding the second complaint was "frivolous." The high court held that the trial court erred in dismissing the second complaint with prejudice and in sanctioning counsel because appellant waited the 60 days required by § 15-1-36(15) before filing the second lawsuit. The trial court erred in relying on the doctrine of priority jurisdiction to support its ruling, as that doctrine presupposed a pending action that the plaintiff could proceed upon and obtain "adequate relief," which was not the case with appellant's first action, since he had failed to wait the required 60 days.


OUTCOME: The orders were reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Akins v. Miss. Dep't of Revenue


NO. 2010-CA-00599-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


70 So. 3d 204; 2011 Miss. LEXIS 464



September 22, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/09/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. PATRICIA D. WISE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged an order of the Chancery Court for the First Judicial District of Hinds County (Mississippi), which dismissed his complaint against appellee, the Mississippi Tax Commission, for lack of subject matter jurisdiction due to his failure to pay contractor's taxes under protest or to post bond pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 27-77-7 (Rev. 2005). He argued that he was deprived his right to due process.


OVERVIEW: The Commission assessed a contractor's tax against the taxpayer. The taxpayer alleged that the appeal provisions of § 27-77-7 were unconstitutional. The supreme court held that the statute met constitutional standards, and the taxpayer failed to pay the tax or post a bond in order to grant jurisdiction to the chancery court. The taxpayer was afforded due process. Miss. Code Ann. §§ 27-77-5 and 27-77-7 (Rev. 2005) provided him two full administrative hearings and an opportunity for judicial review in order to contest the validity of the tax assessment. The taxpayer was provided a pre-deprivation process pursuant to § 27-77-5 to contest the validity of the tax. He was heard by the Board of Review and the full Commission. The taxpayer was provided a post-deprivation process. He had fair opportunity to challenge the tax and the ability to receive a refund if successful. Section 27-77-7 provided the taxpayer with the process for seeking a refund or credit for an alleged overpayment of tax or for taxes paid in protest. Its requirement to pay the tax before seeking judicial review provided taxpayers with a fair opportunity to challenge the validity of the tax.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the decision.


 

107 of 603 DOCUMENTS



Hughes v. Hosemann


NO. 2010-CA-01949-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


68 So. 3d 1260; 2011 Miss. LEXIS 436



September 8, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/09/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. S. MALCOLM O. HARRISON.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens filed an action against defendant, the Secretary of State, challenging an initiate filed by intervenors, an organization and a member, that the Secretary qualified to be placed on the general election ballot. The citizens contended that the initiative violated Miss. Const. art. 15, § 273(5)(a). They sought review of a judgment entered in favor of the Secretary and intervenors in the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi).


OVERVIEW: The supreme court held that the initiative was not ripe for review. Even though one could allege that the initiative violated § 273(5)(a), that determination was premature because the supreme court would have to review the substantive constitutionality of the proposal prior to its enactment. Additionally, the supreme court would have to decide issues on appeal that were not clearly or properly addressed by the trial court. Neither the Secretary nor intervenors proffered a motion or counterclaim requesting any relief or judgment. The supreme court was without power to determine the constitutionality of a proposed statute, amendment, or initiative prior to its approval by the legislature or electorate. The wisdom and merit of proposed initiatives were best left to the purview of the voters. Nothing in the Constitution gave the supreme court the authority to review the validity of a proposal prior to its enactment. The supreme court could not invade the territory of the legislature or the electorate to review the substantive validity of a proposed initiative. It would honor the maxim embodied in the constitutional mandate of separation of powers, Miss Const. art. 1, §§ 1 and 2.


OUTCOME: The supreme court vacated the trial court's final judgment and rendered judgment dismissing the complaint and the action without prejudice.


 

108 of 603 DOCUMENTS



Speed v. Hosemann


NO. 2011-CA-01106-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


68 So. 3d 1278; 2011 Miss. LEXIS 429



September 8, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/29/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WINSTON L. KIDD.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen filed an action against appellee Secretary of State, seeking a declaration that a ballot initiative violated Miss. Const. art. 15, § 273(5)(a), and seeking an injunction against the Secretary from placing the initiative on the ballot. The Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) denied the citizen's motion for judgment on the pleadings, and held that the initiative was appropriate for ballot placement. The citizen appealed.


OVERVIEW: The initiative attempted to restrict the State's power to transfer certain property to certain parties after taking it by eminent domain. The constitutionality of proposed initiative was not ripe for adjudication, such that any opinion thereon would have been improperly advisory. The case was rushed through the trial court and efficiently punted to the appellate court for expedited review. However, there was no good reason for the frenetic, fast-paced atmosphere surrounding the case. While minimum constitutional and statutory requirements had to be met before a measure was placed on the ballot, a pre-election review of an initiative was limited to matters of form, and not substantive constitutionality. Therefore, the citizen's challenge to the substantive validity of the initiative was not ripe for consideration. Thus, the appellate court declined to consider the issues raised in the appeal, and it intimated no opinion whatever upon the merits of the important questions attempted to be submitted for its decision.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's judgment, and dismissed the complaint and the action without prejudice.


 

109 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Decker v. State


NO. 2008-CT-01621-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


66 So. 3d 654; 2011 Miss. LEXIS 379



August 4, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CLAY COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/01/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LEE J. HOWARD.
Decker v. State, 66 So. 3d 659, 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 459 (Miss. Ct. App., Aug. 31, 2010)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Court of Appeals (Mississippi) that upheld her conviction for violating the Mississippi Vulnerable Adults Act of 1986, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 43-47-1 to 43-47-39 (Rev. 2009); defendant claimed, among other things, reversible error in the discrepancy between the indictment and the trial court's jury instructions.


OVERVIEW: A grand jury indicted defendant for using her mother's money "without her consent." When the evidence at trial established that defendant had obtained her mother's consent to use the money, the State requested--and the trial judge granted--a jury instruction that allowed the jury to find defendant guilty, even if her mother had given her permission to use the money. The state supreme court found, inter alia, that the wording of the indictment led defendant to believe that having her mother's permission was a complete defense to the charges. Therefore, the jury instructions expanded, beyond the charges in the indictment, the bases on which defendant could be convicted. The discrepancy between the indictment and the jury instructions was material because it prejudiced defendant's ability to defend. Because the error was not cleared up in other instructions, the jury instructions, when taken as a whole, created injustice by expanding, beyond the charges in the indictment, the bases on which defendant could be convicted. A citation to § 43-47-19(1), (2)(b), as its terms were defined in Miss. Code Ann. § 43-47-5, was insufficient to correct the error.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and judgment was rendered.

Jackson v. State


NO. 2008-CT-00074-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


67 So. 3d 725; 2011 Miss. LEXIS 368



July 28, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Jackson v. State, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 351 (Miss., July 28, 2011)
Rehearing dismissed by, As moot Jackson v. State, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 347 (Miss., July 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WARREN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/04/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ISADORE W. PATRICK, JR. MOTION FOR REHEARING FILED: 04/15/2010.
Jackson v. State, 67 So. 3d 781, 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 99 (Miss. Ct. App., Feb. 24, 2009)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner was convicted of capital murder. He filed numerous petitions for post-conviction relief (PCR), all of which had been denied. The trial court dismissed his most recent PCR motion as a successive writ. The Court of Appeals (Mississippi) affirmed the trial court's dismissal. In its original opinion, the court reversed the prisoner's capital-murder conviction. The State filed a motion for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: The court found that it had been without jurisdiction to decide the prisoner's 1999, 2002, and 2004 applications for leave to proceed with PCR motions. Because there was no direct appeal of his conviction or sentence, the prisoner was required to file his PCR motions in the trial court pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-7 (Rev. 2007). The court found that while Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-25 gave the court jurisdiction to address the prisoner's dismissed 2007 PCR motion, the circuit court should exercise initial jurisdiction over the PCR proceedings pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. §§ 99-39-25(1), 99-39-7 (Rev. 2007). Because the court had vacated its denials of the 2002 and 2004 applications -- the denials that prompted the trial court to apply the successive-writ bar, the court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the prisoner's latest motion under the successive-writ bar, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-23(6) (Rev. 2007).


OUTCOME: The court vacated and set aside its denials of the prisoner's 1999, 2002, and 2004 applications for post-conviction relief. The court reversed the decision of the Court of Appeals and the trial court's dismissal of the petition and remanded the case to the trial court for further post-conviction-relief proceedings.

Putnam v. Epps


NO. 2010-CP-00708-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


63 So. 3d 547; 2011 Miss. LEXIS 205



April 14, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by Putnam v. Epps, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 201 (Miss., Apr. 14, 2011)
Rehearing denied by Putnam v. Epps, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 330 (Miss., June 30, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: YAZOO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/26/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JANNIE M. LEWIS.
Putnam v. Epps, 963 So. 2d 1232, 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 421 (Miss. Ct. App., 2007)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of dismissal by the Yazoo County Circuit Court of his complaint pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-807 challenging the computation by the Mississippi Department of Corrections of his earned-time allowance. Appellee State argued that the inmate's complaint was a motion for post-conviction relief that should have been filed in the county of conviction.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court dismissed the inmate's complaint upon a finding of improper venue. The court on appeal held that the inmate's complaint was brought pursuant to statutes governing administrative review procedure in Miss. Code Ann. §§ 47-5-801 through 47-5-807 (2004) rather than a motion for post-conviction relief subject to dismissal for improper venue. The court explained that earned time was not a reduction of sentence because any inmate released before the expiration of his term of sentence was placed under earned-release supervision until the expiration of sentence. The inmate remained under the jurisdiction of the Department under Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-138(6) (2004). The inmate's complaint, filed after he exhausted administrative remedies, named the Commissioner of the Department as the only defendant and venue was proper in the county where his office was located. Miss. R. Civ. P. 82(d) provided for transfer to the proper venue rather than dismissal of the inmate's action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the case for transfer to a proper venue.

Dedeaux Util. Co. v. City of Gulfport


NO. 2008-CA-02105-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2010-CA-00290-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


63 So. 3d 514; 2011 Miss. LEXIS 191



April 7, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Dedeaux Util. Co. v. City of Gulfport Miss., 2011 Miss. LEXIS 321 (Miss., June 30, 2011)
Rehearing denied by Dedeaux Util. Co. v. City of Gulfport, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 331 (Miss., June 30, 2011)
Rehearing denied by Dedeaux Util. Co. v. City of Gulfport, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 320 (Miss., June 30, 2011)
Rehearing denied by Dedeaux Util. Co. v. City of Gulfport, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 332 (Miss., June 30, 2011)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by City of Gulfport v. Dedeaux Util. Co., 2016 Miss. LEXIS 130 (Miss., Mar. 24, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY SPECIAL COURT OF EMINENT DOMAIN. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/25/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. T. LARRY WILSON. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/21/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES H.C. THOMAS, JR.
Dedeaux Util. Co. v. City of Gulfport, 938 So. 2d 838, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 529 (Miss., 2006)



DISPOSITION: ON DIRECT APPEAL: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED. ON CROSS-APPEAL: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED. AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals from judgments of the Harrison County Special Court of Eminent Domain (Mississippi) and the Harrison County Chancery Court (Mississippi), appellant and cross-appellant privately-owned public utility sought review of an award for a taking by appellee and cross-appellant City of Gulfport, Mississippi, when the City took over ownership and operation of the utility.


OVERVIEW: The utility provided water and sewer services in an area annexed by the City. About three years after the annexation, the City filed a complaint of eminent domain against the utility. The utility continued to be privately operated until a jury award of compensation to the utility's owners eight years later after which the City took over the assets and operation of the utility. On appeal of a second, higher jury verdict for the utility after remand, the court held that in cases involving privately-owned public utility companies, the applicable date for determining due compensation through the jury's consideration of fair-market value was the actual date the property was transferred rather than the date that the complaint of eminent domain was filed. Miss. Code Ann. § 11-27-19 (2004), which fixed such value as of the date of the complaint, was unconstitutional as applied to a utility which was obligated to continue to provide service until the taking of its property was completed. The court ordered a new trial on the amount of damages related to post-complaint improvements to the utility's property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed chancery court dismissal of the case before it for lack of jurisdiction under the doctrine of priority of jurisdiction. As to the case before the Special Court of Eminent Domain, the court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for further consideration of damages related to post-complaint improvements to the utility's property and with instructions to the trial court on proper jury instructions and closing argument.


 

113 of 603 DOCUMENTS



State ex rel. Hood v. Louisville Tire Center, Inc.


NO. 2009-CA-00052-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


55 So. 3d 1068; 2011 Miss. LEXIS 141



March 10, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended March 11, 2011.
Decision reached on appeal by State ex rel. Hood v. Louisville Tire Center, Inc., 2016 Miss. LEXIS 504 (Miss., Dec. 8, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WINSTON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/25/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. J. MAX KILPATRICK.
State ex rel. Hood v. Louisville Tire Ctr., Inc., 2011 Miss. LEXIS 151 (Miss., Mar. 10, 2011)



DISPOSITION: ON DIRECT APPEAL: REVERSED AND REMANDED; ON CROSS-APPEAL: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Mississippi sought review of a decision of the Winston County Chancery Court (Mississippi) granting the motion by appellee gasoline and diesel fuel retailer for summary judgment that Mississippi's Price-Gouging Statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 75-24-25(2009), was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Mississippi's Price-Gouging Statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 75-24-25 (2009), penalized businesses that raised the price of their goods from the price charged in the same market area at or immediately before a proclamation of a state of emergency. Using an average of the weekly prices of the retailer before the declaration of a state-wide declaration of emergency due to an approaching hurricane, the State alleged price-gouging by the retailer. The retailer contended the statute was vague in its use of the phrases "same market area" and "at or immediately before." The court held that the language of the Price-Gouging Statute provided adequate notice on its face of what was prohibited when a state of emergency was declared. The alleged conduct being prosecuted was the raising of prices after the declaration of a state of emergency, absent justification. The absence of perfect clarity and precise guidance did not render the statute unconstitutionally vague, and it was not void on its face. Also, a declaration of voidness as applied was premature because there had not yet been any determination that the statute had been violated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment and remanded the case for examination of the company's conduct in light of a judicial interpretation of the Price-Gouging Statute.

Long v. State


NO. 2009-KA-01861-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


52 So. 3d 1188; 2011 Miss. LEXIS 41



January 20, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by, Certificate of appealability denied Long v. King, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 87812 (N.D. Miss., June 27, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/02/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT P. CHAMBERLIN.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the DeSoto County Circuit Court, Mississippi, of selling a controlled substance within 1,000 feet of a public park. He was sentenced as a habitual offender under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-83 (Rev. 2007) to life imprisonment without parole. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: A jury's verdict was not against the overwhelming weight of the evidence as surveillance video showed that a transaction took place between defendant and an agent of the narcotics division at the location alleged in the indictment. The State's closing argument reiterated the jury's duty set forth in the jury instructions and was not an improper "send-a-message" argument. There was sufficient evidence to find defendant was selling a controlled substance with 1,000 feet of a public park as the agent testified a city park was about 100 feet behind defendant's house. At the sentencing hearing, the State presented certified copies of defendant's commitment papers from another state showing that he had been convicted of 3 felonies on 2 separate occasions. Defendant admitted to the convictions. There was sufficient evidence to find that defendant had been previously convicted of 3 felonies and that at least one was for a crime of violence. Thus, he was properly sentenced as a habitual offender under § 99-19-83. His sentence as a habitual offender was not cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

115 of 603 DOCUMENTS


State v. Delaney


NO. 2009-CA-01640-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


52 So. 3d 348; 2011 Miss. LEXIS 26



January 13, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent civil proceeding at Delaney v. Miss. Dep't of Pub. Safety, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 9600 (S.D. Miss., Jan. 24, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HOLMES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/28/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JANNIE M. LEWIS.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of dismissal by the Holmes County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of the indictment of defendant police officer for one count of extortion because a probable cause hearing pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-3-28 (2007) had not been held prior to defendant's arrest.


OVERVIEW: Miss. Code Ann. § 99-3-28 provided that prior to the issuance of a warrant for the arrest of a teacher, jail officer, counselor at an adolescent offender program or law enforcement officer for criminal conduct while that person was performing official duties, a probable cause hearing had to be held before a circuit court judge. In a matter of first impression, the court concluded that § 99-3-28 (2007) did not apply once an indictment has been returned by a grand jury. The court reasoned that to require a probable cause after an indictment has been returned by a state grand jury would create an inherent conflict with the court's precedent and its rules, including Miss. Unif. Cir. & Cty. R. 6.05, which provided that a defendant who has been indicted by a grand jury shall not be entitled to a preliminary hearing. Under the constitutional concept of separation of powers, the court's rules regarding matters of judicial procedure controlled when a statute conflicted with the court's rules.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal, reinstated the indictment, and remanded the case for further proceedings.

Stewart v. Miss. Bar


NO. 2009-BR-01954-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


84 So. 3d 9; 2011 Miss. LEXIS 2



January 6, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by Stewart v. Miss. Bar, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 3 (Miss., Jan. 6, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Stewart v. Miss. Bar, 5 So. 3d 344, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 452 (Miss., 2008)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] REINSTATEMENT DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney filed a second petition for reinstatement to the practice of law and appellee, the Mississippi Bar (Bar) continued to oppose the attorney's reinstatement.


OVERVIEW: The attorney filed a second petition for reinstatement to the practice of law. He had been disbarred after he pled guilty to conspiracy to commit extortion under color of official right. Although he had made strides toward rehabilitating his character and demonstrated a changed life in many ways, he made a false statement to the Bar and failed to cooperate with the Bar during its investigation of his petition. Thus, the supreme court denied his request for reinstatement. The Bar had the right to ask the attorney if he had an expunged record, and the Bar was permitted to inquire about the underlying circumstances or offense. Because the Bar had a right to ask the attorney whether he had anything expunged, the attorney had an obligation to answer the question truthfully. Although the attorney said that his reason for not doing so was that the word "expungement" had never been used with him, the word "expunge," or some derivation thereof, was used no less than nine times between the two expungement-related orders. The attorney never claimed ignorance of having a prior offense cleared and thus, even if the word "expungement" was not communicated to him, he still knew what occurred.


OUTCOME: The request for reinstatement was denied.

 

117 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Miss. State Fedn. of Colored Women's Club Hous. for the Elderly in Clinton, Inc. v. L. R.


NO. 2009-CA-00508-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


62 So. 3d 351; 2010 Miss. LEXIS 657



December 16, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/20/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM F. COLEMAN.
Doe v. Mississippi State Fed'n of Colored Women's Club Housing for the Elderly in Clinton, Inc. (In re Minor Child), 941 So. 2d 820, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 194 (Miss. Ct. App., 2006)



DISPOSITION: ON DIRECT APPEAL: REVERSED AND REMANDED. ON CROSS APPEAL: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Parents, individually and on behalf of their eleven-year old daughter, filed an action for damages against the father's apartment owner and its management company (the apartment) after the daughter was raped and impregnated in his building. The Circuit Court of the First Judicial District of Hinds County (Mississippi), contrary to the jury's findings, assessed fault entirely to the apartment. The apartment appealed. The family cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The jury established total damages at $200,000, and allocated fault at forty percent to the apartment and sixty percent to the father. The trial court entered final judgment against the apartment for $80,000. However, following post-trial motions, the trial court assessed fault entirely to the apartment and ordered additur of $800,000, contingent upon acceptance. It then entered judgment against the apartment for $1,000,000. Neither party agreed to the additur. The trial court abused its discretion in ordering additur because it failed to make either required finding under Miss. Code Ann. § 11-1-55 (Rev. 2002). There was no finding that the jury was influenced by bias, prejudice, or passion, or that the damages awarded were contrary to the overwhelming weight of credible evidence. Even without this procedural flaw, the trial court's judgment was erroneous because evidence supported the jury's verdict and the verdict was not so unreasonable as to strike mankind at first blush as being beyond all measure, unreasonable in amount and outrageous. However, the trial court did not err in allocating 100 percent fault to the apartment because the father did not breach a defined duty.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for entry of a final judgment against the owner and the management company.

Jones v. City of Ridgeland


NO. 2009-CT-00984-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


48 So. 3d 530; 2010 Miss. LEXIS 604



November 18, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MADISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/28/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. SAMAC S. RICHARDSON.
Jones v. City of Ridgeland, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 302 (Miss., June 17, 2010)



DISPOSITION: THE JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF APPEALS IS VACATED. THE JUDGMENT OF THE MADISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT IS REINSTATED AND AFFIRMED. THE CONVICTION BY THE COUNTY COURT OF MADISON COUNTY OF DUI FIRST OFFENSE AND CARELESS DRIVING AND SENTENCE OF FORTY-EIGHT (48) HOURS IN JAIL AND A FINE OF FIFTY (50) DOLLARS, WITH CONDITIONS, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled nolo contendere in the municipal court to driving under the influence (DUI), possession of an open container of alcohol, and careless driving. Defendant appealed to the county court and was found guilty of DUI and careless driving. The circuit court affirmed. Defendant again appealed. The Court of Appeals (Mississippi) granted the City's motion to dismiss pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 11-51-81 (Rev. 2002). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to § 11-51-81, defendants aggrieved by a decision originating in justice or municipal court, who had appealed to both the county and the circuit courts, were not entitled to appeal for a third time unless the appeal involved a constitutional question and either the circuit court judge or a Mississippi Supreme Court justice allowed the appeal. However, the "three-court rule" of § 11-51-81 was unconstitutional because it contravened the constitutional mandates imposed upon the legislature and the judiciary in Miss. Const. art. 1, § 2. It was not within the purview of the legislature to determine which litigants could appeal to the Mississippi Supreme Court. Accordingly, the court of appeals erred in dismissing the appeal. On the merits, the county court did not err in denying defendant's motion to dismiss because the police officers had probable cause to stop defendant's vehicle where defendant exited a restaurant in an apparent intoxicated state, argued with another patron, entered his vehicle, nearly collided with a patrol car, made an unusually wide turn onto a public road, and failed to stop at a red light.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the court of appeals. It reinstated the circuit court's judgment and affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Fulgham v. State


NO. 2009-CA-00971-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


47 So. 3d 698; 2010 Miss. LEXIS 575



November 5, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: OKTIBBEHA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/07/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES T. KITCHENS, JR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, who had been incarcerated for capital murder, was caught furnishing a cell phone and a charger to another inmate. She pled guilty to a violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-193 (2004) and was sentenced to 8 years. She filed a timely petition for postconviction relief, arguing that § 47-5-193 was unconstitutionally vague. The Oktibbeha County Circuit Court, Mississippi denied her petition without a hearing. Petitioner sought review.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that she had waived her right to question the statute's constitutionality and that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The court found that petitioner's claim was an exception to the procedural bar at Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21(1) (2007) under the Uniform Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act as a conviction under an unconstitutionally vague statute violated the fundamental right to due process. Petitioner argued that § 47-5-193, at the time she was convicted, was facially vague as it did not define the phrase "unauthorized electronic device." The court found that the statute did not affect a constitutional right. The court concluded the cause needed to be remanded for an evidentiary hearing to determine whether petitioner had notice that a cell phone and charger constituted an "electronic device," and if so, whether she had notice that they were "unauthorized," and whether law enforcement had definite standards to avoid arbitrary enforcement. The court could not answer those questions on the record before it.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for an evidentiary hearing.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Oktibbeha County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted her of capital murder in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(e) (Rev. 2006), and sentenced her to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death for killing her husband. OVERVIEW: The supreme court granted certiorari after the appellate court affirmed defendant's capital-murder conviction and sentence and the supreme court reversed and remanded for a new trial, stating that defendant was entitled to have an instruction given to the jury that presented his theory of the case because he presented sufficient evidence to support his duress theory. Further the portion of a jury instruction requiring the jury to unanimously find beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was not guilty was improper and could not have been cured by other instructions.

Moffett v. State


NO. 2008-DP-00541-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


49 So. 3d 1073; 2010 Miss. LEXIS 477



September 16, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Moffett v. State, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 11 (Miss., Jan. 6, 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Moffett v. Mississippi, 132 S. Ct. 127, 181 L. Ed. 2d 49, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 5318 (U.S., 2011)
Post-conviction proceeding at Moffett v. State, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 643 (Miss., Aug. 31, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/26/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. SWAN YERGER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), entered on a jury's verdict convicting him of capital murder, a violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19 (Rev. 2007), and sentencing him to death by lethal injection under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101 (Rev. 2007).


OVERVIEW: Defendant savagely raped, battered, and murdered his girlfriend's five-year-old daughter. Although defendant was soon arrested and held for 250 days, he was released upon a no-bill. Defendant was not indicted for the crimes until eight years later. There was no statute of limitations for capital murder, and, therefore, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-1-5 (Rev. 2007) did not bar the prosecution. No speedy trial rights were applicable after defendant was released following his initial arrest until after he was later indicted. Weighing all factors, including that defendant never timely asserted his speedy trial right and that he failed to show actual prejudice, his speedy trial and due process rights were not violated. Pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-105(3), the case was examined with heightened scrutiny. There was no support in the record that the death sentence was imposed under the influence of passion or prejudice. Given the evidence presented, there was no doubt that a rational trier of fact could have found the aggravating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt. Further, the death penalty was not a disproportionate or excessive sentence when compared to other capital-murder cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence of death.

 

123 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Tapper v. State


NO. 2009-KA-00544-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


47 So. 3d 95; 2010 Miss. LEXIS 446



August 26, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by, En banc Tapper v. State, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 612 (Miss., Nov. 18, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/02/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT P. KREBS.
Tapper v. State, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 448 (Miss., Aug. 26, 2010)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Jackson County Circuit Court, Mississippi, convicted defendant of 2 counts of sexual battery and 5 counts of touching a child for lustful purposes. Defendant sought review, arguing that the trial court violated his fundamental right to a fair and impartial jury by failing to excuse jurors for cause, erred in denying his motion to quash the indictment, and erred by not merging the touching convictions with the sexual battery convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court failed to excuse three jurors for cause that declared that he had to prove his innocence in clear contradiction to defendant's fundamental right not to testify. Defendant used three of his peremptory challenges to strike the jurors. While the record showed defendant used all 12 of his peremptory challenges, defendant was unable to show that any of the three challenged jurors were forced upon him be sitting on the trial jury. Defendant argued that the failure of the indictment to allege more specific dates denied him the opportunity to present his defense at trial. The court found that the three-month time frame alleged by the State was sufficient to comply with the date and time requirement of Miss. Unif. Cir. & Cty. R. 7.06(5), especially as the case involved sex offenses committed upon minor children. Defendant's right against double jeopardy was not violated because his convictions of touching a child for lustful purposes did not merge with his sexual battery convictions. Sexual battery included separate events involving penetration, while the unlawful touching acts alleged did not involve penetration.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Thomas v. Bd. of Supervisors


NO. 2009-CA-00347-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


45 So. 3d 1173; 2010 Miss. LEXIS 409



August 5, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PANOLA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/10/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW C. BAKER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Panola County, Second Judicial District (Mississippi), which affirmed the decision of appellee Board of Supervisors (Board). The Board had rezoned five acres from an agricultural to an industrial classification and affirmed the special exception to operate a recycling facility/junkyard.


OVERVIEW: The property owner appealed after the circuit court had affirmed the Board's decision to rezone five acres from an agricultural to an industrial classification and had affirmed the special exception to operate a recycling facility/junkyard. The supreme court affirmed. The Board had evidence of the former industrial use of the property, the changes in the area, the high agricultural versus commercial or industrial ratio of county lands, the lack of industrially zoned land, and the varied uses of land in the area despite its agricultural zoning, among other things. The Board had substantial evidence before it to support its decision to rezone. The Board did not engage in spot-zoning because it found a public need for the rezoning and the rezoning was for the betterment of county. The Board had proof that the junkyard met the factors as listed in the county ordinance. The special exception was restricted by the Board in number, area, location, or relation to the neighborhood, and proof was provided as to the promotion of the public health, safety, welfare, morals, order, comfort, convenience, appearance, prosperity, or general welfare.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
