Wheat v. Wheat


NO. 2008-CA-00476-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


37 So. 3d 632; 2010 Miss. LEXIS 318



June 24, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/19/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAYE A. BRADLEY.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife sought review of a judgment of the Jackson County Chancery Court (Mississippi) granting appellee husband a divorce on the ground of uncondoned adultery, under Miss. Code Ann. § 93-5-1 (Rev. 2004), distributing the parties' assets, and ordering the wife to pay child support, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 43-19-101 (Rev. 2009).


OVERVIEW: First, the chancellor did not err in classifying the wife's severance package and IRA as marital property because they were distributed to her two years before the divorce. Second, the chancellor did not commit manifest error in reclassifying the husband's pension as nonmarital property because the husband showed proof that the pension was fully funded prior to the marriage. Furthermore, the wife's counsel conceded that the pension was nonmarital property. Third, the wife was procedurally barred from raising the issues of whether the husband's stock shares and IRA were marital property because she never asserted the issues in the trial court. However, the chancellor erred in ordering the wife to pay an amount of child support in excess of the statutory child-support guidelines under § 43-19-101(1). While the chancellor may have based the award on the wife's earning capacity rather than her actual earnings, no on-the-record findings were made that her earning capacity was considered. Further, on remand, the trial court was directed to revisit the issue of liability for the second mortgage or line of credit on the marital home.


OUTCOME: The court reversed those portions of the judgment that awarded child support and that ordered the wife to be responsible for the second mortgage on the marital home. It remanded the issues to the trial court. The court further stated that once the chancellor reconsidered the second mortgage issue on remand, adjustments could be made to the total distribution of assets to each party. The court affirmed the judgment in all other respects.

Angle v. Koppers, Inc.


NO. 2008-CA-02045-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


42 So. 3d 1; 2010 Miss. LEXIS 273; 70 ERC (BNA) 1910



May 27, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Angle v. Koppers, Inc., 2010 Miss. LEXIS 436 (Miss., Aug. 19, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GRENADA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/28/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOSEPH H. LOPER, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a toxic tort action, appellant claimant sought damages under theories of negligence, intentional tort, conspiracy, private conspiracy under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1985(3), strict liability, trespass, private nuisance, and failure to warn against appellee corporations. The Grenada County Circuit Court, Mississippi, found that her claims were time-barred and granted summary judgment for the corporations. The claimant sought review.


OVERVIEW: The claimant argued that the statute of limitations began to run when she discovered that her medical problems were the result of her exposure to toxic chemicals. The corporations contended that the limitations period began to run when the claimant discovered or was diagnosed with her illnesses. The court agreed that Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-35 (2003) was inapplicable as the claimant's intentional tort claim was not listed in that code section. The court concluded that the claimant's cause of action accrued when she was last diagnosed with an injury or a disease. She was last diagnosed with a medical condition that she alleged was related to exposure to toxic chemicals approximately five years before she filed her action. Thus, her claims were time-barred under Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-49(2) (2003). The claimant argued that 42 U.S.C.S. § 9658 (2006) of the Comprehensive Environmental Response, Compensation, and Liability Act preempted § 15-1-49(2). Because there was no evidence in the record to support her argument, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the claimant failed to carry her burden of showing that § 9648 preempted § 15-1-49(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Carl Ronnie Daricek Living Trust v. Hancock County


NO. 2009-IA-01513-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2009-IA-01514-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2009-IA-01515-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


34 So. 3d 587; 2010 Miss. LEXIS 238



May 13, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HANCOCK COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/31/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LAWRENCE PAUL BOURGEOIS, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In three consolidated cases, the Hancock County Circuit Court (Mississippi) held that the Seawall Act, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 65-33-1 to 65-33-71 (Rev. 2005), was constitutional, and had not been repealed or superseded by the Real Property Acquisition Policies Act (RPAPA), Miss. Code Ann. §§ 43-37-1 to Miss. Code Ann. § 43-37-13 (Rev. 2009). Appellant landowners filed interlocutory appeals.


OVERVIEW: Following Hurricane Katrina, appellee county used Miss. Code Ann. § 65-33-23 (Rev. 2005) of the Seawall Act to condemn the landowners' property for a temporary construction easement to rebuild the county seawall. The landowners failed in their burden to show beyond a reasonable doubt that the Seawall Act was unconstitutional. While the county acted under the authority granted by the Seawall Act, it conceded that the RPAPA also applied. The RPAPA did not repeal or supersede any part of the Seawall Act, and the two statutes were applied in conjunction with each other. Further, the county complied with the constitutional and statutory requirements in condemning the property. Any discrepancies between the procedures employed and the statutory requirements were harmless errors because they did not pertain to the power of the board to condemn the property, nor did they infringe on the landowners' constitutional rights. Further, the trial court did not err in finding that the landowners were entitled, upon request, to a jury trial, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 65-33-33 (Rev. 2005). Finally, the Eminent Domain Act, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 11-27-1 to 11-27-51 (Rev. 2002), was inapplicable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court and remanded the matter to that court for a jury trial, if requested by the landowners.

Long v. State


NO. 2008-KA-01877-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


33 So. 3d 1122; 2010 Miss. LEXIS 224

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of one count of possession of cocaine with intent to sell and one count of sale of cocaine in the Circuit Court of Grenada County (Mississippi). He was sentenced as a habitual offender to life imprisonment on each count. Defendant filed a post-trial motion for a new trial, which was denied. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Upon review, the court found that defendant failed to establish that the verdict was contrary to the overwhelming weight of the evidence. In deciding that a confidential informant's testimony regarding defendant's prior cocaine sales was admissible, the trial court conducted a Miss. R. The trial court's finding that there was no racial discrimination was not clearly erroneous or against the overwhelming weight of the evidence. Defendant's sentence was not disproportionate to his offenses or cruel and unusual punishment. His sentence was within the statutory range, it was mandatory under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-83 (2007), and he did not show it was grossly disproportionate to his crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Hutzel v. City of Jackson


NO. 2008-CA-02134-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


33 So. 3d 1116; 2010 Miss. LEXIS 231



May 6, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/21/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM F. COLEMAN.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for damages against appellees, City of Jackson and a construction company, alleging inverse condemnation, negligence, trespass, and nuisance arising out of the city's efforts to improve a corridor, appellant leaseholder challenged a judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted summary judgment in favor of the city.


OVERVIEW: During the course of an improvement project, the city obtained a deed from a property owner and the leaseholder, conveying interest in the property to the city in exchange for consideration. The leaseholder filed an action for damages it allegedly suffered when the construction affected its business. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the city, finding that the leaseholder had released the city from any and all claims arising from the project and that the consideration paid for the release was an accord and satisfaction of such claims. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, finding that the trial court erred in allowing the city to amend its answer two years after the action was filed. Pursuant to Miss. R. Civ. P. 8(c), the city waived its right to assert the affirmative defenses of release and accord and satisfaction 26 months after it filed its original answer; the city's filing of an answer, coupled with its participation in the discovery process, sufficiently established that it actively participated in the litigation. The record revealed no unusual or extreme circumstances that explained the city's failure to assert timely the affirmative defenses.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for a trial on the merits.

Jackson v. State


NO. 2008-CT-00074-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


2010 Miss. LEXIS 170



April 1, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 6, 2010.

As Corrected April 22, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WARREN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/04/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ISADORE W. PATRICK, JR.
Jackson v. State, 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 99 (Miss. Ct. App., Feb. 24, 2009)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of capital murder in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(e). The circuit court denied his most recent motion for post-conviction relief (PCR) under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-27. The Court of Appeals (Mississippi) affirmed, holding that the circuit court was without jurisdiction to entertain the motion absent leave of the supreme court pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-7 (Rev. 2007). Writ of certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: The current PCR motion was the fourth time in which the disposition of one of defendant's PCR motions had been appealed to the supreme court. The circuit court continued to have exclusive initial jurisdiction over defendant's PCR proceedings because defendant never directly appealed his conviction and sentence to the supreme court. The court of appeals decision that the most recent PCR motion was procedurally barred as an impermissible successive writ was in error because the supreme court incorrectly applied the procedural bar to defendant's 1999, 2002, and 2004 applications. Defendant's arguments regarding the substantive deficiencies in his indictment were excepted from the procedural bars of the Uniform Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-1 et seq., because defendant's arguments implicated fundamental due-process concerns. On the merits, defendant's indictment was fatally insufficient to charge him with capital murder or burglary because it failed to assert the underlying offense that comprised the burglary. The indictment also failed to charge him with murder or manslaughter because it omitted the phrase without the authority of law or unlawfully.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the most recent PCR motion. It also reversed defendant's conviction for capital murder and remanded the case to the circuit court without prejudice of the State's right to bring a charge against defendant founded upon a proper indictment.

Miss. Comm'n on Judicial Performance v. DeLaughter


NO. 2008-JP-00460-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


29 So. 3d 750; 2010 Miss. LEXIS 108



March 4, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Miss. Comm'n on Judicial Performance v. DeLaughter, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 117 (Miss., Mar. 4, 2010)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] REMOVED FROM OFFICE; MOTION TO DISMISS ORDER OF INTERIM SUSPENSION DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Mississippi Commission on Judicial Performance filed a motion to dismiss order of interim suspension on the ground that in exchange for the dismissal of formal complaints pending before the Commission, a circuit court judge agreed that he would not seek judicial office or otherwise serve in any judicial capacity at any time in the future.


OVERVIEW: Two judicial complaints were filed against the circuit court judge. They alleged that he committed multiple counts of judicial misconduct in two separate cases. The Commission filed a petition for interim suspension of the circuit court judge, which was granted. The circuit court judge was indicted on federal charges. He pleaded guilty to obstructing, influencing, and impeding an official federal corruption investigation and grand jury proceeding. The Commission moved to dismiss order of interim suspension. The supreme court held that the Commission exceeded its authority under Miss. Const. art. 6, § 177A. The supreme court had neither been presented with nor asked to approve any agreement between the Commission and the circuit court judge. It could not ignore the serious, willful nature of the admitted acts of criminal and judicial misconduct. The supreme court could not allow the dismissal of formal complaints in two separate cases pursuant to the circuit court judge's resignation or any mere agreement not to seek judicial office in the future. Based upon the seriousness of his admitted criminal acts and judicial misconduct, he would be removed from office.


OUTCOME: The supreme court removed the judge from office and dismissed the Commission's motion to dismiss order of interim suspension as moot.

Sauvage v. Meadowcrest Living Ctr., LLC


NO. 2008-CA-02116-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


28 So. 3d 589; 2010 Miss. LEXIS 93



February 25, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/21/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM F. COLEMAN.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff personal representatives filed a complaint against defendants, a nursing home, its administrator, and others, alleging that their decedent died as the result of inadequate medical care at a church camp where nursing home residents were taken. The personal representatives filed an almost identical action in Louisiana. The Hinds County Circuit Court, Mississippi, dismissed the complaint and the personal representatives appealed.


OVERVIEW: On the eve of Hurricane Katrina, the nursing home evacuated its elderly residents from Louisiana to a church camp in Mississippi. The complaint alleged that the decedent was one of the evacuated residents, and that she died as the result of inadequate medical care at the church camp. On appeal, the personal representatives argued that the circuit court erred by dismissing the case for lack of personal jurisdiction or forum non conveniens. Affirming, the court ruled that under Mississippi's wrongful-death statute--Miss. Code Ann. § 11-7-13 (Rev. 2004)--and interpretive caselaw, the Mississippi action was properly dismissed due to the pendency of the prior-filed Louisiana wrongful-death action. Under § 11-7-13, there was to be one suit for the same death; under Long v. McKinney, all claims had to be joined in that single action. The court held that a wrongful-death suit filed in Mississippi was subject to dismissal during the pendency of a suit for the same wrongful death in a sister state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

In re Estate of McCullough v. Yates


NO. 2009-CA-00149-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


32 So. 3d 403; 2010 Miss. LEXIS 82



February 18, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Leach v. Yates (In re Estate of McCullough), 2010 Miss. LEXIS 212 (Miss., Apr. 29, 2010)
Costs and fees proceeding at Catchings v. Estate of McCullough (In re Estate of McCullough), 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 138 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 15, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/08/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. PATRICIA D. WISE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an appeal of a decision of the Chancery Court of the First Judicial District of Hinds County (Mississippi), appellants sought a determination that they were the heirs at law of the decedent in order receive the assets of her estate through representation.


OVERVIEW: In order for appellants to inherit from the decedent, their putative aunt, through representation, they first had to establish paternity through their putative father. The putative father died in 1978, and appellants did not try to establish paternity until 2003, after the death of the decedent. Appellants failed properly to adjudicate themselves as the illegitimate children of their putative father in the time prescribed by Miss. Code Ann. § 91-1-15. As such, the petition to be determined heirs of the decedent was barred by the time provision of § 91-1-15. Additionally, § 91-1-15 did not violate the Equal Protection Clause or the Due Process Clause of the United States Constitution. Further, appellants were not deprived of either their procedural or substantive due process rights. Mississippi had a legitimate state interest in the legislation propounded in § 91-1-15, therefore, the statute did not violate any substantive due process rights. In addition, appellants had notice of the putative father's death and would have been afforded a hearing for adjudication of paternity, however, they failed to make such a petition within the statutory limits of § 91-1-15.


OUTCOME: The decision of the chancery court was affirmed.

Johnson v. State


NO. 2008-KA-01077-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


29 So. 3d 738; 2009 Miss. LEXIS 610



December 17, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Johnson v. State, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 156 (Miss., Mar. 25, 2010)
Rehearing denied by Johnson v. State, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 158 (Miss., Mar. 25, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEAKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/14/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. VERNON R. COTTEN.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of three counts of armed robbery and his sentence of forty-one years without parole entered by the Leake County Circuit Court (Mississippi).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-81 violated the Separation of Powers Doctrine; however, the instant court failed to see how the Separation of Powers Doctrine was applicable to a division of power between an individual and the Legislature. Defendant had no constitutional right to a jury trial on the issue of habitual-offender status. Although defendant alleged numerous claims of ineffective assistance, all of the claims failed. There was sufficient evidence to convict defendant of three counts of armed robbery. The jury was presented with testimony and evidence that defendant feloniously took money from three victims, against their will, by putting each man in fear of immediate injury by the exhibition of a deadly weapon, i.e., the gun. A rational jury could have found the essential elements of armed robbery beyond a reasonable doubt. As the three victims and another witness identified defendant and defendant took the stand only to say that all the witnesses were lying, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion for a new trial.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of three counts of armed robbery and sentence of forty-one years without parole or probation was affirmed.

 

137 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Aarco Oil & Gas Co. v. EOG Res., Inc.


NO. 2008-CA-01219-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


20 So. 3d 662; 2009 Miss. LEXIS 530; 171 Oil & Gas Rep. 422



October 29, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: COVINGTON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/26/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOE DALE WALKER.
Allred v. Fairchild, 785 So. 2d 1064, 2001 Miss. LEXIS 143 (Miss., 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both plaintiffs and defendants claimed ownership to the mineral rights of two tracts of land. Plaintiffs brought suit seeking to confirm and quiet title and also seeking a declaratory judgment. The Covington County Chancery Court (Mississippi) granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, finding that a 1942 tax sale was valid. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Because the lower court addressed the due process issue relating to the 1942 tax sale, the appellate court was not prohibited from considering the issue on appeal. At the time of the 1941 assessment, real property rolls were examined and equalized every two years, and the next equalization was not to occur until 1942. Ad valorem taxes were assessed for 1941 in compliance with applicable law, and the board of supervisors was under no obligation, either by statute or constitution, to equalize the land roll in that year. In addition, because the identity and whereabouts of the owners of the severed mineral interests were not readily ascertainable, publication and notice to the surface owners were sufficient to satisfy the due process requirements of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Miss. Const. art. 3, § 14. The appellate court presumed that the tax sale was properly advertised given the presumption that public officials perform their lawful duties. The tax assessor was under no obligation to comb the land records to identify individuals who might have appeared to have had an interest in the land's minerals.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of defendants.

Schmidt v. Catholic Diocese


NO. 2008-CA-00416-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


18 So. 3d 814; 2009 Miss. LEXIS 427



September 17, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by Schmidt v. Catholic Diocese of Biloxi, 2014 Miss. LEXIS 328 (Miss., July 17, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/27/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS L. ZEBERT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, former church parishioners, appealed from the holding of the Harrison County, MS, Chancery court which held in favor of defendants, a diocese, a bishop, and a reverend, on the parishioners' claims relief after the bishop closed the church, which had been damaged in Hurricane Katrina. The chancellor found that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction based on the church autonomy doctrine of the First Amendment.


OVERVIEW: The parishioners asserted, in part, that the bishop held the church property in trust for the members of the church, that any financial contributions designated for reconstruction of the church were held in trust for that particular purpose, that defendants had violated said trusts, and that the reverend had made misrepresentations in soliciting donations for the rebuilding efforts. First, the court held that the extent of the parishioners' interest in the church property, if any, was inextricably tied to their status as members of the parish. Because such church or parish no longer existed, the parishioners had no standing to assert a claim for any interest they may or may not have had in church property. Second, the court determined that the chancellor erred in dismissing the parishioners' claims that defendants improperly diverted designated funds. While churches had large, almost-unfettered discretion in their administrative decision-making, they were not entitled to violate recognized duties or standards of conduct. Thus, subject matter jurisdiction existed over a claim that a religious entity breached a fiduciary duty by improperly diverting designated funds.


OUTCOME: The instant court affirmed the chancellor's finding that subject matter jurisdiction did not exist over the parishioners' claim that the church property was held in trust. The court reversed the chancellor's dismissal of the parishioners' breach of fiduciary duty claim for the diversion of designated funds, as well as their intentional misrepresentation claim against the reverend. These claims were remanded these claims for further proceedings.

 

139 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Franklin Corp. v. Tedford


NO. 2007-CA-01454-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


18 So. 3d 215; 2009 Miss. LEXIS 426



September 10, 2009, Decided 
May 14, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CALHOUN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/26/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW K. HOWORTH.
Franklin Corp. v. Tedford, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 169 (Miss., Apr. 16, 2009)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee employees sued appellant employer alleging multiple claims for batter and intentional infliction of emotional distress that arose from injuries sustained in the course of their employment. A jury returned a verdict in favor of the employees. The Calhoun County Circuit Court (Miss.) denied the employer's motions for judgment notwithstanding the verdict (JNOV), or in the alternative for a new trial or remittitur. The employer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employer was a furniture manufacturer. The employer used a certain adhesive that contained a neurotoxin and it was necessary to have the area well ventilated. Despite the savings the employer enjoyed from using the adhesive it did not install mechanical ventilation exhausts outside the building on the glue line. The employees eventually were hospitalized because of their exposure to the neurotoxin. At issue on appeal was the application of the intentional tort exception to the Mississippi Workers' Compensation Act. Miss. Code Ann. § 71-3-1 et seq. The Supreme Court found that given the considerable amount of testimony offered by the employees and the management personnel of the employer the denial of the JNOV motion was proper. The experts' testimony was properly admitted under Miss. R. Evid. 702 because their qualifications were not legitimately questioned, and their testimony was sufficiently relevant and reliable. There was sufficient evidence to meet the "clear and convincing" standard required for punitive damages under Miss. Code Ann. § 11-1-65 and the court's determination of the employer's net worth at the time of judgment was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Modak-Truran v. Johnson


NO. 2008-CA-00104-SCT, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2008-CA-00105-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


18 So. 3d 206; 2009 Miss. LEXIS 397



August 13, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Modak-Truran v. Johnson, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 492 (Miss., Oct. 15, 2009)
Rehearing denied by Baker v. Johnson, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 493 (Miss., Oct. 15, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/04/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: BOBBY BURT DELAUGHTER.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant neighbors challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of the First Judicial District of Hinds County (Mississippi), which affirmed appellee city's council's adoption of two amendments to Jackson, Miss., Zoning Ordinance § 202.17 (2002), allowing appellee, a bed and breakfast inn, to operate a restaurant.


OVERVIEW: The inn was located in a residential district. The amendments exempted the inn from having to obtain a new use permit in order to operate a restaurant. The supreme court held that the amendments constituted illegal spot zoning. Although the city claimed that the amendments were "text amendment," the changes to the ordinance effectively rezoned residential property for the sole favor and benefit of the inn. The amendments significantly altered and expanded the activities previously allowed on residential district properties and effectively rezoned the inn from residential to commercial property. They allowed the inn to conduct highly commercial operations within an area restricted to one- and two-family dwellings. Before the amendments, the only use permits allowed in residential zones were for limited purposes. With the addition of a bed and breakfast with restaurant, the inn was granted permission to operate a general restaurant within a residential zone, an activity allowed in areas zoned commercial districts. In addition, by allowing existing bed and breakfast inns to operate restaurants "as of right," the amendments exempted the inn from having to apply for a use permit.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the circuit court's judgment affirming the amendments and rendered judgment in favor of the neighbors.

Hood v. State

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Hood v. State, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 453 (Miss., Sept. 24, 2009)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Hood v. King, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 42345 (S.D. Miss., Jan. 30, 2013)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Hood v. King, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 42094 (S.D. Miss., Jan. 15, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: YAZOO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/19/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JANNIE M. LEWIS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court of Yazoo County, Mississippi, of the crime of exploitation of children under Miss. Code Ann. §§ 97-5-31 and 97-5-33(5) (Rev. 2006). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's wife found a videotape among her husband's belonging. The tape depicted nude male children. The wife confronted defendant who made a comment about going back to California, where he could do it again. The wife contacted a police detective. On appeal, defendant presented four issues: (1) whether the marital privilege caused his wife to be incompetent to testify; (2) whether the males in the video were engaged in "sexually explicit conduct;" (3) whether the statutes were unconstitutional; (4) whether the prosecution made improper arguments. The supreme court determined that spousal incompetence was not applicable, under Miss. R. Evid. 601(a)(2) and Miss. R. Evid. 504(d), because defendant was being prosecuted for a criminal act against any child. The supreme court also adopted the Dost factors and concluded the jury was justified in its finding that the images it viewed depicted "sexually explicit conduct." Defendant's constitutional argument was procedurally barred due to his failure to assert it at the trial-court level. As to the prosecutor's comments in closing arguments, defendant did not object; therefore, the issue was waived.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Price v. Clark


NO. 2007-CA-01671-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


21 So. 3d 509; 2009 Miss. LEXIS 365



July 23, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion dismissed by, Moot Price v. Clark, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 351 (Miss., July 23, 2009)
Rehearing denied by Price v. Clark, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 601 (Miss., Dec. 3, 2009)
Rehearing denied by Price v. Clark, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 595 (Miss., Dec. 3, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: BOLIVAR COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/17/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. CHARLES E. WEBSTER.



DISPOSITION: ON DIRECT APPEAL: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART. ON CROSS-APPEAL: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice/wrongful death claim, plaintiff, the wife of a decedent, appealed a judgment of the Bolivar County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that dismissed her cause of action against defendant health care providers based upon her failure to comply with the pre-suit notice requirements under Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11 (Rev. 2002) and her failure to timely identify John Does 1-5.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the trial court properly dismissed those claims where the decedent's wife failed to provide pre-suit notice because strict compliance with the 90-day-notice requirement in Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11(1) (Rev. 2002) was required. Further, the notice of claim letters that were sent were insufficient under Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11(2) because they did not contain allegations of the nature of the negligent conduct, the time and place of alleged conduct, the names of persons involved, the damages sought, or claimant's residence. The third complaint, which substituted the names of actual physicians for the John Does, did not relate back to the original complaint under Miss. R. Civ. P. 9(h) because the wife failed to exercise due diligence to discover the identities of the John Doe physicians where she received records pertaining to the patient's treatment prior to filing suit. As to other health care providers, however, the court held that the trial court erred in holding that the wife's complaint failed to toll the statute of limitations because the complaint did have a tolling effect until the trial court issued its ruling on the motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Edmonds v. Williamson


NO. 2007-CA-00751-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


13 So. 3d 1283; 2009 Miss. LEXIS 300



June 25, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: KEMPER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/28/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LESTER F. WILLIAMSON, JR.
Williamson v. Edmonds, 880 So. 2d 310, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1031 (Miss., 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a legal malpractice case, plaintiff clients, a husband and wife, appealed summary judgment granted by the Kemper County Circuit Court (Mississippi) in favor of defendant attorneys. The clients further challenged an order of the circuit court that held that the attorneys were not required to turn over their case file to the clients but that the clients could copy the file at their own expense.


OVERVIEW: The attorneys represented the clients in products liability litigation. The representation agreement established attorney fees for the litigation, which increased as the litigation progressed. Under the agreement, if the case was settled after the discovery period expired, the attorney fee would be 45 percent of the settlement amount. After the parties settled, the attorneys withheld their fee of 45 percent. Dissatisfied with the fee withheld, the clients filed a legal malpractice claim. On review, the court affirmed summary judgment due to the enforceability of the fee agreement, which the clients did not challenge. Further, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying clients' motion to compel the attorneys to surrender their case file to the clients as being the clients' property. Rather, the trial court properly ordered that counsel make the case file available to the clients and allow the clients to copy as much of the case file as they chose at the client's expense; the trial court's order complied with Miss. R. Prof. Conduct 1.16(d) in that it required the attorneys to do what was reasonably practicable in order to protect the clients' interests.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment granted in favor of the attorneys and the trial court's order concerning the production of the case file were affirmed.

Neal v. State

SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


15 So. 3d 388; 2009 Miss. LEXIS 272

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Tallahatchie County Circuit Court, Mississippi, convicted defendant of murder and sentenced him to life in the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections. Defendant appealed.

The investigator's testimony was not hearsay. There was no ineffective assistance of counsel. Defendant was validly convicted by a jury verdict accepted and recorded in court. The evidence did not support a heat-of-passion manslaughter jury instruction. There was ample evidence to support the verdict.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Goff v. State


NO. 2006-DP-00815-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


14 So. 3d 625; 2009 Miss. LEXIS 273



May 28, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 27, 2009.
Rehearing denied by, Modified by Goff v. State, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 406 (Miss., Aug. 27, 2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Goff v. Miss., 2010 U.S. LEXIS 1251 (U.S., Feb. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GEORGE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/06/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DALE HARKEY.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the George County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that convicted him of capital murder under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19 (Rev. 2006) during the commission of a robbery under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-79 (Rev. 2006), arguing that the prosecution failed to produce evidence sufficient to convict him of the underlying felony of robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his married girlfriend were staying at a motel together. After defendant left, the body of his murdered girlfriend was found in the room they shared. On review of defendant's conviction, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of the underlying felony of robbery because defendant's possession of the murder victim's wallet created a reasonable inference that it was stolen. The State's theory of the case was that defendant went back to the motel to get back what was rightfully his--the money in the victim's wallet, and the evidence, although circumstantial, supported that theory. During the State's case-in-chief, evidence was presented to establish that, after defendant left the motel earlier in the day, the victim feared his return, and when defendant did return and was unable to access the room, a motel employee told him that the door was locked from the inside. Additional evidence was presented that defendant had received a significant amount of money from his mother for a business that he planned to start and that defendant was supporting the victim and was the source of the cash found inside her wallet.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and the capital sentence were affirmed.

Franklin Corp. v. Tedford


NO. 2007-CA-01454-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


2009 Miss. LEXIS 169



April 16, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at Franklin Corp. v. Tedford, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 426 (Miss., Sept. 10, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CALHOUN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/26/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW K. HOWORTH.
Franklin Corp. v. Tedford, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 383 (Miss., June 16, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged a judgment of the Calhoun County Circuit Court (Mississippi) denying its motion for J.N.O.V. or a new trial and awarding appellee employees compensatory and punitive damages, under Miss. Code Ann. § 11-1-65(3)(a) (2002), for battery and intentional infliction of emotional distress, as intentional-tort exceptions to the Mississippi Workmens' Compensation Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 71-3-9 (2000).


OVERVIEW: The employees alleged injuries from fumes because there was no ventilation, protective gear, or sufficient air testing. The circuit court found that the employees alleged sufficient facts to satisfy the intentional tort exception to the application of the Act. The employees sought to expand the scope of egregious conduct excluded from the Act to include acts which were substantially certain to cause injury. The employer sought to enlarge the scope of the exemption test. The court held that the Act was exclusive absent an actual intent to injure the employee. Here, the employees' injuries arose out of and in the course of employment, under Miss. Code Ann. § 71-3-3(b) (2000). The employees' claims of battery and intentional infliction of emotional distress against the employer were not precluded by the Act as a matter of law. The circuit judge properly admitted the expert testimony of the employees' experts, as their qualifications were not legitimately questioned, and their testimony was sufficiently relevant and reliable. Applying net worth of the employer at the time of trial, the circuit court properly reduced the punitive damages, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 11-1-65(3)(a)(v).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

Williams v. Skelton


NO. 2007-CT-00095-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


6 So. 3d 428; 2009 Miss. LEXIS 138



April 9, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/13/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. SWAN YERGER.
Williams v. Skelton, 6 So. 3d 433, 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 250 (Miss. Ct. App., Apr. 22, 2008)



DISPOSITION: THE JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF APPEALS IS AFFIRMED. THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR THE FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HINDS COUNTY IS AFFIRMED AND THIS CASE IS DISMISSED WITHOUT PREJUDICE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice and wrongful death action, plaintiff wrongful death beneficiary appealed a judgment of the Mississippi Court of Appeals that affirmed the dismissal of her claims against defendant doctors, arguing that the trial court erred in dismissing on the basis that she failed to comply with the 60-day notice requirement of Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-36(15) (Rev. 2003).


OVERVIEW: The wrongful death beneficiary filed a medical malpractice and wrongful death suit against the doctors following the demise of the doctors' patient. The doctors moved to dismiss, arguing that the wrongful death beneficiary failed to comply with the pre-suit notice requirements of Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-36(15) (Rev. 2003). The trial court granted the motion, and after the appellate court affirmed, the wrongful death beneficiary petitioned for certiorari, arguing that, because the doctors were not served with a copy of the summons and complaint until more than 60 days after the notice of intent was received by them, she had complied with the statutory provisions. In the alternative, she argued that, even if her cause of action had been properly dismissed, she was entitled to refile. On review, the court held that, although the appellate court decided the issue correctly, it granted certiorari to reiterate that dismissal for failure to comply with the pre-suit notice requirements of Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-36 (Rev. 2003) was to be with prejudice.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed. The judgment of the trial court was likewise affirmed, and the case was dismissed without prejudice.

City of Laurel v. Sharon Waterworks Ass'n (In re Extension of the Boundaries of the City of Laurel)


NO. 2007-AN-01547-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


17 So. 3d 529; 2009 Miss. LEXIS 4



January 15, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion dismissed by City of Laurel v. Sharon Waterworks Ass'n (In re Extension of the Boundaries of the City of Laurel), 2009 Miss. LEXIS 202 (Miss., Apr. 30, 2009)
Rehearing denied by City of Laurel v. Sharon Waterworks Ass'n (In re Extension of the Boundaries of the City of Laurel), 2009 Miss. LEXIS 200 (Miss., Apr. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JONES COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/06/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. CHARLES D. THOMAS.
In re Extension of the Boundaries of Laurel v. Sharon Waterworks Ass'n, 918 So. 2d 1269, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 493 (Miss., 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A chancellor of the Jones County Chancery Court (Mississippi) entered a final judgment that approved appellant city's application to enlarge the city's boundaries as to a southern parcel only. The city challenged whether the provision of H.B. 1730 violated Miss. Const. art. 4, § 88 and whether the chancellor's finding that it was unreasonable to annex a northern parcel was manifestly wrong.


OVERVIEW: The city claimed that H.B. 1730, § 12, contained a poison pill provision that required all or none of a utility district to be annexed. The court found that the legislation did not violate Miss. Const. art. 4, § 90--the Legislature could enact by both a general law and a local and private law. Section 12 did not offend art. 4, § 88, and was not at odds with the general laws regarding annexation. The chancellor properly considered 1) the need to expand to accommodate spillover growth, internal growth, and population growth; 2) the city's need for development land; 3) the need for planning in the annexation area; 4) increased traffic counts; 5) the need to maintain and expand the city's tax base; 6) the remaining vacant land; and 7) environmental influences. Those factors did not support the need for annexation. Annexation was not reasonable as to the other parcels that were largely rural, were not "urbanizing areas," and were not in need of municipal services. There was little evidence that better municipal services would result if annexation were allowed. The chancellor did not apply an erroneous legal standard and his findings were based on substantial, credible evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the chancellor's judgment.


 

149 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Hemba v. Miss. Dep't of Corr.


NO. 2007-CA-01777-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


998 So. 2d 1003; 2009 Miss. LEXIS 1



January 8, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/10/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM H. SINGLETARY.
Hemba v. Miss. Dep't of Corr., 848 So. 2d 909, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 567 (Miss. Ct. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hinds County Chancery Court, Mississippi, dismissed appellant employee's action for wrongful termination against appellee Mississippi Department of Corrections (MDOC). The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee argued that because HB 1279, 2004 Miss. Laws 595, § 13 (Section 13) directly amended Miss. Code Ann. § 25-9-127(1) (Rev. 2006) without any reference to it, and because the purported statutory modifications were not inserted at length into the statute, the employee argued that Section 13 ran afoul of Miss. Const. art. 4, § 61. The supreme court found that the language of Section 13 did not purport to insert any words or expressly change any of the terms of Miss. Code Ann. § 25-9-127(1) and, therefore, was not a direct amendment. It exempted the personnel decisions of a specific agency, MDOC, from State Personnel Board procedures regarding terminations for a period of one year. It qualified as an amendment by implication, which was not violative of Miss. Const. art. 4, § 61. Section 13 affected a general class of people due to a mandated reorganization of the department. Even though the legislative amendment extinguished the employee's property rights as to his job, he was not denied due process. Therefore, the employee was entitled to due process only as provided under Section 13. The employee's other claims were not presented in his complaint before the trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Hearn v. State


NO. 2007-KA-01439-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


3 So. 3d 722; 2008 Miss. LEXIS 607



December 11, 2008, Decided

Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Hearn v. Byd, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 184593 (S.D. Miss., Oct. 15, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAUDERDALE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/08/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DAVID MICHAEL ISHEE.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of intimidating a judge under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-9-55 (Rev. 2006) by the Lauderdale County Circuit Court (Mississippi), arguing that the trial court erred in failing to conduct a formal hearing to determine his competency and erred in admitting the statement's of a psychologist into evidence and arguing that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-9-55 was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. I and Miss. Const. art. 3, § 28.


OVERVIEW: While incarcerated, defendant wrote more than a hundred threatening letters to two judges. While speaking with a psychologist who treated jail inmates, defendant repeated his threats against the judges. As a result of the threats made, defendant was charged with and convicted of two counts of intimidating a judge. On review of defendant's conviction, the court concluded that, despite the trial court's failure to strictly comply with Miss. Unif. Circ. & Cty. Miss. Code Ann. § 41-21-97 (Rev. 2005) created an exception to § 73-31-29 when a patient made a threat of physical violence. Finally, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-9-55 was not unconstitutional because threatening speech was not protected speech.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Thomas v. Warden


NO. 2006-CA-01703-SCT, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2007-CA-00821-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


999 So. 2d 842; 2008 Miss. LEXIS 600



December 11, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Thomas v. Warden, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 56 (Miss., Feb. 12, 2009)
Rehearing denied by Thomas v. Miss. Baptist Med. Ctr. & Clark G. Warden, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 62 (Miss., Feb. 12, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/28/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. SWAN YERGER. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/09/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: W. SWAN YERGER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of an order from the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which dismissed their medical negligence action against defendants, a physician and a hospital.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought a medical negligence action against defendants. The hospital raised as affirmative defenses plaintiffs' failure to comply with Miss. Code Ann. § 11-1-58(1)(a) (Supp. 2008), and plaintiffs' failure to comply with conditions precedent to the initiation of litigation. The physician moved to dismiss the suit on the ground that plaintiffs failed to wait 60 days after notice before filing suit. The trial court dismissed the action. On appeal, the court found that the trial court erred in dismissing the complaint for failure to file with the complaint a certificate of compliance as required by § 11-1-58. The complaint did not need to be dismissed simply because plaintiffs failed to attach a certificate or waiver. However, the trial court properly dismissed the complaint for failure to comply with the notice requirement of Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-36(15) (Rev. 2003). Because defendants did not have 60 days' prior written notice of the intention to begin the action, the lawsuit was not lawfully filed, and it was of no legal effect. The complaint, however, should have been dismissed without prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the action for failure to file with the complaint a certificate of compliance as required by § 11-1-58. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the action for failure to comply with the notice requirements of § 15-1-36(15). The court ordered that the dismissal was to be without prejudice.

Delashmit v. State


NO. 2007-KA-02130-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


991 So. 2d 1215; 2008 Miss. LEXIS 501



October 9, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/27/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS J. GARDNER, III.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was tried and convicted by a jury in the Lee County Circuit Court, Mississippi, for the crime of enticement of a child for sexual purposes, in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-5-33 (Rev. 2006). Defendant was sentenced as a habitual offender to a term of life imprisonment without parole pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-83 (Rev. 2007). After his posttrial motions were denied, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The instant court concluded that defendant's statements to law enforcement officials were properly admitted. Defendant's statement of "I prefer a lawyer" was only an ambiguous mention of possibly speaking with an attorney and was insufficient to invoke the right to counsel. A reasonable police officer would not have understood this statement alone to be an unequivocal assertion of the right to counsel. Defendant was not entitled to a lesser included offense instruction on misdemeanor indecent exposure. Based on the overwhelming evidence, no reasonable jury could have found defendant not guilty of any element of the principal charge. Although defendant argued that the trial court erred in limiting defense counsel's closing argument with regard to reasonable doubt, defense counsel's discontinuance of his reasonable doubt argument was not trial court error but rather a choice on the part of defense counsel. Even assuming that the trial court impermissibly prohibited defense counsel's reasonable doubt argument, the error was harmless. Based on the overwhelming evidence of guilt, this error, if any, had no effect on the ultimate outcome.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and sentence was affirmed.

 

153 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Bunton v. King


NO. 2007-IA-00621-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


995 So. 2d 694; 2008 Miss. LEXIS 447



September 25, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Bunton v. King, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 692 (Miss., Dec. 11, 2008)
Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by King v. Bunton, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 162 (Miss., Mar. 25, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WARREN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/05/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ISADORE W. PATRICK, JR.
Bunton v. King, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 332 (Miss., June 14, 2007)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a negligence action stemming from an automobile collision, defendants, a governmental agency and its employee, appealed an interlocutory order of the Warren County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that denied their motion to dismiss plaintiffs' complaint based upon plaintiffs' failure to strictly comply with the 90-day notice requirement of the Mississippi Tort Claims Act at Miss. Code Ann. 11-46-11 (Rev. 2002).


OVERVIEW: After being involved in an automobile collision with defendant employee, plaintiffs served a notice of claim letter to defendant governmental agency and then filed their complaint only seven days after sending the notice letter. Defendants moved to dismiss, but the circuit court denied their motion. On review, the court held that the Mississippi Tort Claims Act at Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11(1) (Rev. 2002) established a pre-suit notice requirement that a claimant must meet in order to maintain an action against a governmental entity; specifically, a claimant was required to give a 90-day notice before filing suit. The 90-day notice requirement was a mandatory rule that Mississippi courts strictly enforced, and the notice requirement was jurisdictional in nature. Mississippi law required strict compliance with the Mississippi Tort Claims Act's 90-day notice requirement. Because plaintiffs failed to strictly comply with the requirement, the circuit court never had jurisdiction over their complaint. Therefore, the circuit court erred in denying defendants' motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court was reversed, and the case was remanded for dismissal of the cause of action.

 

154 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Caves v. Yarbrough


NO. 2006-CA-01857-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


991 So. 2d 142; 2008 Miss. LEXIS 617



September 25, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FRANKLIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/13/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FORREST A. JOHNSON, JR. MOTION FOR REHEARING FILED: 12/06/2007.
Caves v. Yarbrough, 991 So. 2d 142, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 710 (Miss., 2007)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a Mississippi Tort Claims Act, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 11-46-1 to 11-46-23 (Rev. 2002) medical-negligence suit, appellant claimants challenged the summary judgment entered by a trial court in favor of appellees, a doctor and a hospital, holding that the discovery rule did not apply because the decedent's injuries were not latent. In its original opinion, the court held that the claim was time-barred, but granted the claimant's motion for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: At issue was the application of the Act's statute of limitations. The language of § 11-46-11 required courts to look past the date of the wrongful conduct to the earliest date all the necessary elements of a tort claim were present, remembering that damages may not manifest until long after the wrongful conduct. All elements of all claims were present by April 17, 2000, when the decedent died. Since notice was not provided until February 13, 2002, the suit was time-barred, unless the discovery rule applied. The Miss. Code Ann. § 11-7-13 (Rev. 2004) wrongful-death claims matured, and the statute of limitations on those claims began to run, on April 17, 2000 because that was the first day ("if death had not ensued") that the decedent could have brought a claim. Although the Act's discovery rule was judicially created, subsequent to the court's incorrect interpretation in Barnes, § 11-46-11(3) was re-enacted without addressing or countermanding the Barnes decision; the Legislature acquiesced and tacitly approved and incorporated into the statute the Barnes' discovery rule. Because the question of whether notice was timely provided was not addressed, reversal and remand were required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment and remanded the case for a hearing on the question of whether, within a year of providing notice to defendants, the claimants knew or, by exercise of reasonable diligence, should have known of both the decedent's injury and the alleged tortious act or omission that proximately caused it.

 

155 of 603 DOCUMENTS



Wimley v. Reid


NO. 2007-CA-00593-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


991 So. 2d 135; 2008 Miss. LEXIS 456



September 18, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEFLORE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/02/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. ASHLEY HINES.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Leflore County Circuit Court, Mississippi, denied appellant daughter's motion to amend her wrongful death suit, granted appellee's motion to dismiss, and dismissed the suit with prejudice. The daughter appealed.


OVERVIEW: When filing her wrongful death complaint, the daughter included neither a certificate nor a disclosure, as required by Miss. Code Ann. § 11-1-58(1)(a) (Supp. 2007). The supreme court noted that the parties raised and briefed the issue of whether failure to attach a certificate to the complaint in compliance with § 11-1-58 should result in dismissal of the suit. The supreme court was unable to ignore the constitutional imperative that the Legislature refrain from promulgating procedural statutes which required dismissal of a complaint. A complaint, otherwise properly filed, may not be dismissed, and need not be amended, simply because the plaintiff failed to attach a certificate or waiver. The certificate did not indicate whether the daughter's attorney consulted with the expert prior to, or after, filing the complaint. If the former, then the daughter was in compliance with the enforceable portion of § 11-1-58. If the latter, then the pretrial statutory requirement was not met, and the trial court had to dismiss the complaint with prejudice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for a hearing to determine whether the presuit requirements were met.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: ADAMS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/19/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FORREST A. JOHNSON, JR.
Havard v. State, 928 So. 2d 771, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 90 (Miss., 2006)



DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate filed a request for postconviction relief after the Adams County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicted him of capital murder (murder during the commission of sexual battery) and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was found guilty of capital murder and he was sentenced to death. He filed an application for leave to proceed in the trial court and motion for other relief under the Mississippi Uniform Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-1 et seq., and more specifically, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-27 (Rev. 2007). The supreme court denied his request for postconviction relief. Even if counsel had successfully procured an independent DNA expert and that expert had testified that the inmate's DNA was not present on the rape kit samples taken from the victim, that did not exonerate the inmate of the sexual battery charge. Further, counsel's consultation with a registered nurse evidenced counsel's diligence when the request for independent pathologist funding was denied. And assuming that the inmate's counsel was deficient, the inmate failed to prove that a doctor's reports and affidavits did not contain evidence that would have created a reasonable probability that, but for counsel's deficient performance, the outcome of the inmate's trial would have been different.


OUTCOME: The supreme court denied the inmate's request for postconviction relief.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was tried and convicted in the Circuit Court of Winston County, Mississippi, on one count of armed robbery, for which he was sentenced to serve thirty years, and two counts of aggravated assault, for which he was sentenced to serve twenty years each, with the sentences to run concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victims were at their home when they heard a knock at their carport door. They opened the door to find defendant and another young male dressed in black sweatshirts and pants. OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Strickland v. State


NO. 2006-KA-01573-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


980 So. 2d 908; 2008 Miss. LEXIS 132



March 6, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Strickland v. State, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 207 (Miss., May 1, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LOWNDES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/31/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LEE J. HOWARD.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Lowndes County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicting him of armed robbery in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-79 and sentencing him to 30 years in prison as a habitual offender without the benefit of parole or probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for robbing a store clerk at gunpoint. On appeal, the court held that because no evidence was offered to the trial court to support defendant's claim of a Batson violation, the court could not conclude that the trial court clearly erred in denying the white defendant's request for a Batson hearing based on the State's using peremptory challenges against seven African-American potential jurors. The trial court did not err by allowing defendant's prior conviction of theft of property to be used by the State for impeachment purposes under Miss. R. Barbour v. State ex rel. Hood


NO. 2008-EC-00115-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


974 So. 2d 232; 2008 Miss. LEXIS 87



February 6, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Replaced February 28, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/14/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BOBBY BURT DELAUGHTER.
Barbour v. State ex rel. Hood, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 53 (Miss., Jan. 24, 2008)



DISPOSITION: ON DIRECT APPEAL: REVERSED AND RENDERED. ON CROSS-APPEAL: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hinds County Circuit Court, Mississippi, issued a memorandum opinion and order, which granted judgment against appellant Governor of Mississippi, opining that a writ of election issued by the Governor violated the U.S. and Mississippi Constitutions and the statutory laws of the state, and declaring the writ of election was a nullity, being void ab initio. The Governor appealed. Appellee Attorney General of Mississippi cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The writ of election established November 4, 2008, as the date for a special election to fill a vacancy created by a U.S. Senator's resignation. Official notice of the Senator's resignation was received on December 20, 2007. That same day, the Governor issued the writ of execution. The Attorney General alleged that the writ of election violated Miss. Code Ann. § 23-15-855 (Rev. 2007). The instant court concluded that the circuit court erred, as a matter of law, in deeming § 23-15-855 plain, clear, and unambiguous, and then finding the writ of election exceeded the Governor's constitutional and statutory authority. As portions of § 23-15-855 were ambiguous, and others silent, the writ of election, which designated November 4, 2008, as the general election day for electing a Senator to complete the term of office was not constitutionally infirm. Moreover, both the temporary appointment of a replacement Senator and the writ of election effectuated the clear intent of the legislature that no senatorial temporary appointment exceed one year and an election would be held on the date of a general congressional election, less than one year after the temporary appointment.


OUTCOME: The instant court affirmed the judgment as to the denial of the Attorney General's motion for preliminary injunctive relief and the granting of the Governor's motion to dismiss, or for judgment on the pleadings, as to the Attorney General's request for a writ of mandamus, other remedial writs, or injunctive relief of any kind, and it reversed and rendered as to the declaratory judgment entered against the Governor.

Rollins v. State


NO. 2007-KA-00282-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


970 So. 2d 716; 2007 Miss. LEXIS 707



December 13, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Rollins v. King, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 27553 (S.D. Miss., Feb. 11, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LINCOLN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/15/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL M. TAYLOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Lincoln County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of one count of sexual battery, one count of touching a child for lustful purposes, and two counts of contributing to the delinquency of a minor.


OVERVIEW: At trial, the State sought to use closed circuit television to present the testimony of minor children to the jury, pursuant to Miss. R. Evid. 617. Due to technical difficulties, the prosecutor repeated the questions to ensure that the jury heard the questions and answers. Defendant was able to hear the questions and answers, but he could not see the witnesses. Defendant unsuccessfully moved for a mistrial. The jury requested a transcript of the children's testimony, but they were told that it was a live feed only. Defendant was convicted, a motion for a new trial was denied, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the supreme court found no violation of defendant's Sixth Amendment confrontation right. Defendant waived the right to claim error in the jury's inability to hear portions of the testimony because his counsel specifically declined to object. Next, the use of closed-circuit testimony was not a violation of the Confrontation Clause. To secure a new trial, defendant was required to show that the denial of his right view the demeanor of the children prejudiced him. An assertion of error without prejudice did not trigger reversal.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Caves v. Yarbrough


NO. 2006-CA-01857-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


2007 Miss. LEXIS 710



December 6, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Later proceeding at Caves v. Yarbrough, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 161 (Miss., Apr. 3, 2008)
Later proceeding at Caves v. Yarbrough, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 166 (Miss., Apr. 3, 2008)
Rehearing granted by, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Remanded by Caves v. Yarbrough, 991 So. 2d 142, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 617 (Miss., Sept. 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FRANKLIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/13/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FORREST A. JOHNSON, JR.
Caves v. Yarbrough, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 614 (Miss., Nov. 1, 2007)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a representative for several wrongful death beneficiaries, challenged a decision from the Franklin County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee health care providers in a medical negligence lawsuit filed under the Mississippi Tort Claims Act (MTCA), Miss. Code Ann. §§ 11-46-1 to 11-46-23 (Rev. 2002). After a decision was rendered on appeal, a motion for rehearing was filed.


OVERVIEW: After the decedent's death in 2000, there was a delay in receiving an autopsy report. Notice was given to the providers in 2002, and a lawsuit was subsequently filed. A motion for summary judgment was granted, and this appeal followed. A decision was rendered in the case on appeal, but the representative filed a motion for a rehearing. It was granted. In reversing the trial court, the supreme court determined that the statute of limitations for claims filed under the MTCA began to run when all of the elements of a tort existed. That was when some damage to the representative proximately resulted from the providers' negligence. Next, the doctrine of stare decisis required the supreme court to recognize a discovery rule for MTCA claims. The statute of limitations under Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11 (Rev. 2002) did not begin to run until the representative knew, or by the exercise of reasonable diligence should have known, that a cause of action existed. A remand was necessary because this issue was not addressed by the trial court.


OUTCOME: A rehearing was granted. The previous opinions in the case were withdrawn, and a new opinion was substituted. The trial court's decision was reversed. The case was remanded for a hearing on the question of whether, within a year of providing notice to the providers, the representative knew or, by exercise of reasonable diligence, should have known of both the decedent's injury and the alleged tortious act or omission which proximately caused it.

Spicer v. State


NO. 2006-DR-00625-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


973 So. 2d 184; 2007 Miss. LEXIS 619



November 8, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Spicer v. State, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 78 (Miss., Feb. 7, 2008)
Post-conviction proceeding at Spicer v. State, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 518 (Miss., Oct. 29, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GEORGE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/01/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DALE HARKEY.
Spicer v. State, 921 So. 2d 292, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 20 (Miss., 2006)



DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF IS GRANTED IN PART AND DENIED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought postconviction relief from a judgment of the George County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicting him of capital murder and sentencing him to death by lethal injection.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted for beating the victim to death. On the inmate's petition for postconviction relief, the court held that he was entitled to an evidentiary hearing on his claim that his attorneys were ineffective for failing to investigate and present mitigating evidence of the inmate's character and childhood history during the penalty phase of his trial. The inmate contended that if his counsel had investigated, they would have uncovered at least 15 witnesses who could have provided mitigating evidence concerning his childhood, education, drug habits, and other issues related to his character and childhood history. However, the court held that counsel was not ineffective for failing to present evidence of mental impairment as a mitigating factor during the penalty phase because counsel sought a mental evaluation of defendant and attempted to acquire additional testing, but the mental evaluation revealed that the inmate was malingering. This description of the inmate, if used by the State to rebut the inmate's claims of mental problems, could have been damaging in the eyes of the jury, and therefore the decision not use the evaluation was presumed to be strategic.


OUTCOME: The inmate's petition was granted insofar as he was granted an evidentiary hearing on his claim that his attorneys were ineffective during the penalty phase for failing to investigate and introduce mitigation evidence of his social history.
