Caves v. Yarbrough


NO. 2006-CA-01857-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


2007 Miss. LEXIS 614



November 1, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
As Corrected November 2, 2007.
Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Rehearing granted by, Remanded by Caves v. Yarbrough, 991 So. 2d 142, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 710 (Miss., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FRANKLIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/13/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FORREST A. JOHNSON, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife appealed a judgment of the Franklin County Circuit Court (Mississippi) granting defendants, a hospital and a physician, summary judgment in the wife's medical malpractice action filed under the Mississippi Tort Claims Act (MTCA), Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-1 et seq. (Rev. 2002), seeking damages for her husband's death.


OVERVIEW: The wife sued defendants, alleging that they failed to properly treat her husband's septic colon, causing his death. The trial court granted defendants summary judgment on the ground that the wife's action was barred by the MTCA's one-year statute of repose because it was not filed within one year, as required by Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11(3). On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that applying § 11-46-11(3) as written, it was clear that the wife failed to commence her action within its one-year limitation, and therefore it was statutorily time-barred. The alleged tortious conduct of defendants occurred, at the latest, on April 17, 2000, the day the husband died. Notice of the claim was not provided to the hospital until February 13, 2002, and was never provided to the physician, and therefore the notice was clearly outside the MTCA's one-year limitation period. The court overruled Barnes v. Singing River Hosp., 733 So. 2d 199, 205 (Miss. 1999), and its progeny, insofar as they judicially amended the MTCA by supplying a discovery rule tolling its one-year statute of repose.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

164 of 603 DOCUMENTS


DuPree v. Carroll


NO. 2006-CA-01875-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


967 So. 2d 27; 2007 Miss. LEXIS 589



October 25, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/29/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT B. HELFRICH.
DuPree v. Carroll, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 149 (Miss., Feb. 15, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mayor sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Forrest County (Mississippi), which granted appellee council members' petition for a writ of mandamus directing the mayor to resubmit department directors for approval to the council.


OVERVIEW: In 2001, the mayor nominated department directors pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 21-8-23(2) (Rev. 2007). The council approved the directors. The mayor was reelected and began a second term in 2005. At that time, the mayor indicated he was not going to resubmit the department directors for approval to the council. Three council members sought a writ of mandamus to compel him to comply with what they perceived the law required. The trial court issued the writ. On appeal, the court found that the council members had standing to seek a writ under Miss. Code Ann. § 11-41-1 (Rev. 2002). It was undisputed that the mayor had a duty to nominate, and the council a duty to approve or disapprove, directors of municipal departments. The council members demonstrated that, by virtue of their position as the legislative check and balance on the executive power of the mayor, they had a separate interest or an interest in excess of the general public. Miss. Code Ann. § 21-8-23(2) required that the mayor resubmit directors for approval by the council at the beginning of the new term of office, even if a director was a holdover from the previous term and had been previously approved by the council.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

165 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Oxford Asset Partners, LLC v. City of Oxford


NO. 2006-CA-01712-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


970 So. 2d 116; 2007 Miss. LEXIS 575



October 18, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAFAYETTE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/21/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. HENRY L. LACKEY.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lafayette County Circuit Court, Mississippi, dismissed appellant partnership's request for a declaratory judgment that H.B. 1671, Reg. Sess. (Miss. 2006), was unconstitutional and granted summary judgment in favor of appellee city. The partnership appealed.


OVERVIEW: The partnership argued that H.B. 1671 violated Miss. Const. art. IV, § 87 by suspending multiple general laws for the benefit of a private entity. The supreme court agreed that H.B. 1671 suspended general laws. However, it benefited the city and the benefit to any private party was indirect. Having determined that the aim of H.B. 1671 was to benefit the public by facilitating the construction or acquisition of municipal parking facilities, the special law furthered the same purposes as the general law. The differences between H.B. 1671 and Miss. Code Ann. § 21-37-23 were primarily procedural and minor, as were the differences between H.B. 1671 and Miss. Code Ann. § 21-37-25. H.B. 1671 strayed too far from the general law of Miss. Code Ann. § 21-17-1 by failing to ensure that the consideration received for the conveyance of municipal property was at least equivalent to fair market value. Rendering Miss. Code Ann. § 31-7-13 inapplicable was improper. Thus, the last sentences of sections 3 and 4 of H.B. 1671 were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and rendered as to the grant of summary judgment to the city as to the last sentences of H.B. 1671 sections 3 and 4; the grant of summary judgment as to the remaining portions of H.B. 1671 was affirmed.

Loden v. State


NO. 2002-DP-00282-SCT Consolidated with NO. 2006-CA-00432-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


971 So. 2d 548; 2007 Miss. LEXIS 558



October 4, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Loden v. State, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 29 (Miss., Jan. 17, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Loden v. Mississippi, 555 U.S. 831, 129 S. Ct. 45, 172 L. Ed. 2d 51, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 6568 (Oct. 6, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at Loden v. State, 43 So. 3d 365, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 204 (Miss., Apr. 15, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by, Motion dismissed by, As moot, Certificate of appealability granted, Certificate of appealability denied Loden v. Epps, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 133538 (N.D. Miss., Sept. 18, 2013)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at, As moot Loden v. State, 2017 Miss. LEXIS 208 (Miss., May 23, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
2002-DP-00282-SCT. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: ITAWAMBA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/21/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS J. GARDNER, III.

2006-CA-00432-SCT. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: ITAWAMBA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/15/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS J. GARDNER, III.



DISPOSITION: 2002-DP-00282-SCT - AFFIRMED. 2006-CA-00432-SCT - POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an inmate, sought review of the decision of the Itawamba County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied his motion for postconviction relief. He had been convicted of capital murder, rape, and four counts of sexual battery after pleading guilty and he was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Following his arrest, the inmate was indicted for capital murder, rape, and four counts of sexual battery; he pled guilty to all six counts in the indictment. The circuit court found that all four factors required by Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101(7) (Rev. 2007) were satisfied, that sufficient aggravating circumstances existed, and that the mitigating circumstances did not outweigh the aggravating circumstances. The death penalty was imposed. The supreme court affirmed, stating that the circuit court judiciously provided the inmate with state-funded investigative assistance in developing mitigation evidence. An order authorizing a criminal defense investigator (CDI) was granted, followed by an order granting additional funds for the CDI. Additionally, the indictment charged a death-penalty eligible offense because an indictment was sufficient without listing aggravating circumstances. Anytime an individual was charged with murder, he was put on notice that the death penalty might result. The submission of the Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101(5)(d) aggravating circumstance was proper because the felony-murder aggravator genuinely narrowed the class of defendants eligible for death.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

169 of 603 DOCUMENTS



Adams v. Baptist Mem'l Hospital-Desoto, Inc.


NO. 2006-IA-00455-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


965 So. 2d 652; 2007 Miss. LEXIS 472



August 16, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Adams v. Baptist Mem'l Hosp.-Desoto, Inc., 2007 Miss. LEXIS 561 (Miss., Oct. 11, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TUNICA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/22/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KENNETH L. THOMAS.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Tunica County Circuit Court (Mississippi), plaintiff husband filed a negligence action against defendants, including a hospital and two doctors (medical defendants) and a casino where decedent wife had fallen. The trial court ordered that the action against the medical defendants, but not the casino, be transferred from the county of the casino's location to the county of the hospital's location. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: All the parties asserted that the case should not have been severed. The supreme court agreed, holding that severance of a wrongful death action was violative of Miss. Code Ann. § 11-7-13 and was also inconsistent with Miss. Code Ann. § 85-5-7 (1999). The trial court did not err in transferring the medical defendants to the county where the hospital was located because under Miss. Code Ann. § 11-11-3(3) (2004), the only proper venue for a suit against medical providers was the county in which the alleged act or omission occurred. The presence of medical providers in the action rendered inapplicable Miss. Code Ann. § 11-11-3(1)(a)(i) (2004), which more generally provided that an action was to be commenced where a substantial event that caused the injury occurred. Similarly, there was no conflict between Miss. Code Ann. § 11-11-3(3) and the more liberal venue provision of Miss. R. Civ. P. 82(c). However, it was error not to order the casino to the county of the hospital's location along with the medical defendants.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the trial court's severance order and its denial of reconsideration, and the case was remanded to the trial court with directions to transfer the entire case to the circuit court of the county of the hospital's location for further proceedings.


 

170 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Tran v. State


NO. 2004-CT-00368-SCT consolidated with NO. 2004-CT-00369-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


962 So. 2d 1237; 2007 Miss. LEXIS 475



August 16, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Tran v. Miss., 2008 U.S. LEXIS 4212 (U.S., May 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/09/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM E. CHAPMAN, III.
Tran v. State, 963 So. 2d 1, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 394 (Miss. Ct. App., 2006)



DISPOSITION: 2004-CT-00368-SCT - JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF APPEALS IS AFFIRMED. 2004-CT-00369-SCT - THE JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF APPEALS IS AFFIRMED. THE JUDGMENT OF THE RANKIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT IS REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Rankin County Circuit Court, Mississippi, convicted defendants, a driver and a passenger, of money laundering. The Mississippi Court of Appeals reversed the passenger's conviction, holding that the State did not meet its burden of connecting the passenger to the money. The court of appeals affirmed the driver's conviction. Both defendant and the State filed petitions for writ of certiorari, which were granted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the indictment was legally insufficient, and his conviction had to be reversed. The supreme court found defendant's indictment to be no more informative than a hypothetical indictment which charged a defendant with entering a conspiracy to commit "some unlawful activity." The language of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-23-101(3)(a) (Rev. 2006) required that an underlying crime be named in the indictment of a state money laundering charge. However, based on the civil forfeiture action which was filed prior to defendant's indictment, he was clearly informed that the sheriff's department deemed this money the proceeds of drug trafficking activities. The omission of the "specified unlawful activity" in the indictment was harmless error which did not render the trial fundamentally unfair. The defense had ample notice that the charge of money laundering was based on the State's claim that the money was the product of drug trafficking.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed.

Thong Le v. State


NO. 2005-DR-00523-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


967 So. 2d 627; 2007 Miss. LEXIS 452



August 16, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Replaced November 28, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Le v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 607 (Miss., Nov. 1, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Thong Le v. Mississippi, 552 U.S. 1300, 128 S. Ct. 1747, 170 L. Ed. 2d 547, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2913 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/23/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES W. BACKSTROM.
Le v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 409 (Miss., June 23, 2005)



DISPOSITION: DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi), petitioner was convicted of capital murder committed during the course of a robbery and was sentenced to death. The conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. Petitioner sought postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimed that his trial counsel erred in failing to seek a change of venue because of extensive local pretrial publicity, but the court noted that the record indicated that most of the venire was largely unaware of the case, and those who were unaware of it assured counsel and the trial court that they could be impartial. Petitioner submitted the affidavit of a psychologist who opined that petitioner was not by nature a violent person, but the court held that his culpability as an accomplice would not be reduced by this sort of argument. The court also held that: (1) although the aggravating circumstances which invoked the death penalty were not charged in the indictment, the fact that the capital murder statute listed the possible aggravating circumstances refuted the contention that petitioner had inadequate notice; (2) because the record supported no findings of error, there could be no prejudicial cumulative error; (3) use of the underlying felony as an aggravating sentencing factor did not constitute double prejudice; and (4) other issues raised on direct appeal could not be considered on collateral appeal under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21 (2000).


OUTCOME: Postconviction relief was denied.

 

172 of 603 DOCUMENTS



Montgomery v. Lowndes County Democratic Exec. Comm.


NO. 2007-EC-00863-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


969 So. 2d 1; 2007 Miss. LEXIS 329



June 7, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LOWNDES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/17/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. V. R. COTTEN.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee political party executive committee refused to certify appellant judicial candidate for the position of justice court judge on the ground the candidate did not live in the particular election subdistrict where she wished to run for office, although she was a resident of the county. The Lowndes County Circuit Court, Mississippi, declined to overturn the executive committee's decision. The candidate filed a bill of exceptions.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that the candidate was a qualified candidate for the position of justice court judge, even though she did not live within the election subdistrict. Miss. Const. art. 6, § 171, set out the only requirements for justice court judges. That provision required a justice court judge to have resided two years in the county next proceeding the judge's selection. The legislature had no authority to change the requirements for those seeking the office of justice court judge. The Mississippi Constitution was detailed in setting forth the requirements for candidates for justice court. The interaction between the residency requirements as set by the Mississippi Constitution and the districts or subdistricts within counties could only be addressed by constitutional amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the executive committee was ordered to place the candidate's name on the primary election ballot.

Foster v. State


NO. 2005-KA-01938-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


961 So. 2d 670; 2007 Miss. LEXIS 315



May 31, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Foster v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 463 (Miss., Aug. 16, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LOWNDES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/02/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LEE J. HOWARD.
Foster v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 476 (Miss., Aug. 4, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's death sentence had been previously vacated. The Circuit Court of Lowndes County, Mississippi, was directed to resentence defendant to life in prison without the possibility of parole under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-107 (Rev. 2000). The circuit court complied with that directive. On appeal, defendant challenged the applicability of § 99-19-107.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the supreme court erred in not resentencing him under the 1991 version of Mississippi's capital murder statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-21 (1991), which would require a sentence of life with the possibility of parole. Nevertheless, defendant failed to raise this issue before the supreme court before the remand for resentencing. Defendant's case was procedurally barred. The circuit court properly applied Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-107 to defendant's case. Moreover, the application of the statute in no way constituted an ex post facto punishment.


OUTCOME: The order resentencing defendant to life in prison without the possibility of parole was affirmed.

King v. State


NO. 2005-DP-00419-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


960 So. 2d 413; 2007 Miss. LEXIS 317



May 31, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc King v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 420 (Miss., Aug. 2, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by King v. Mississippi, 552 U.S. 1190, 128 S. Ct. 1223, 170 L. Ed. 2d 77, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 1244 (2008)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Application denied by King v. State, 23 So. 3d 1067, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 449 (Miss., 2009)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part, Motion dismissed by, As moot King v. Epps, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 42513 (N.D. Miss., Mar. 26, 2013)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by King v. State, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 326 (Miss., June 18, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LOWNDES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/28/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. KENNETH COLEMAN.
King v. State, 784 So. 2d 884, 2001 Miss. LEXIS 99 (Miss., 2001)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCE OF DEATH BY LETHAL INJECTION, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A federal court vacated defendant's sentence of death for a capital murder and remanded the case with instructions to return to the state court for reconsideration of the death sentence. The supreme court vacated the sentence of death and remanded the case for a new sentencing trial. The supreme court again reversed the death sentence. A jury for the Lowndes County Circuit Court (Mississippi) returned another death sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Both sides presented expert testimony and other evidence regarding defendant's mental retardation claim. After hearing all the evidence, which was substantial, the trial judge outlined the evidence that he had considered and gave his reasons for concluding that defendant was not mentally retarded. One doctor testified that defendant did not test retarded on his intelligence quotient tests. Also, an officer testified that he saw defendant write certain documents without assistance, which one doctor opined would not have been possible for a mentally retarded person to do alone. Accordingly, based on the evidence, the trial court did not err in finding that defendant was not mentally retarded. Thus, his death sentence did not violate the Eighth Amendment, which prohibited the execution of mentally retarded inmates. Additionally, the supreme court found that defendant's death sentence was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor. Furthermore, there were other factually similar cases where the death sentence was imposed. Thus, the death sentence was neither excessive or disproportionate under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-105(3).


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Oktibbeha County Hosp. v. Miss. State Dep't of Health


NO. 2006-SA-00358-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


956 So. 2d 207; 2007 Miss. LEXIS 277



May 17, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part, En banc Oktibbeha County Hosp. v. Miss. State Dep't of Health, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 299 (Miss., May 17, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital challenged a decision from the Hinds County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which entered judgment in favor of appellee applicant in a dispute over awarding a certificate of need (CON) for a magnetic resonance imaging (MRI) unit.


OVERVIEW: The applicant sought to offer MRI services under Miss. Code Ann. § 41-7-191(16) (Rev. 2005). After researching the scope of § 41-7-191(16), the application was granted. The hospital's request for a hearing on the matter was denied, and an appeal was made to the chancery court. It affirmed the decision to grant the CON, and the hospital sought further review. In affirming, the supreme court determined that, without listing a single exception or qualification, § 41-7-191(16) clearly mandated the issuance of the CON. Next, the hospital was unable to raise challenges to the statute based on Miss. Const. art. 4, § 87, Miss. Const. art. 3, § 14, and the Fourteenth Amendment. It did not comply with the service requirements of Miss. R. Civ. P. 24(d) or Miss. R. App. P. 44(a). Notice to the special assistant attorney general was insufficient in this case. Finally, no hearing was required since the Mississippi Legislature had waived all CON requirements.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Gilmer v. State


NO. 2004-KA-02236-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


955 So. 2d 829; 2007 Miss. LEXIS 258



May 10, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Gilmer v. Mississippi, 552 U.S. 1165, 128 S. Ct. 1120, 169 L. Ed. 2d 949, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 1198 (2008)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Gilmer v. Epps, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 139442 (S.D. Miss., Nov. 29, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MADISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/20/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. SAMAC S. RICHARDSON.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Madison County Circuit Court (Mississippi) found defendant guilty of five counts of photographing a person in privacy without permission under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-29-63 (Rev. 2006). Defendant filed a motion for a new trial and/or a judgment of acquittal notwithstanding the verdict (JNOV), which the trial court denied. He timely filed an appeal to the supreme court seeking reversal of that denial and of the jury verdict of guilty.


OVERVIEW: The undisputed facts were that defendant recorded the victim starting around 9:00 at night, sitting inside his vehicle, the interior of which was dark, about 87 feet away from the victim's apartment, using a camera and its zoom feature and carrying in his vehicle two sets of binoculars. The time of day, dark location, distance from the victim's apartment, and equipment for producing close-up recordings from such a distance clearly indicated an attempt by defendant to conceal his actions and elude observation or detection. Therefore, the facts showed that defendant acted secretly in recording the victim in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-29-63 (Rev. 2006). Also, without question, proof that defendant recorded the victim while she was in her apartment was equivalent to proving that she was recorded while in her private dwelling in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-29-63 (Rev. 2006). Thus, the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction under the "video voyeur" statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-29-63 (Rev. 2006). Therefore, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for directed verdict, JNOV, or a new trial.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Ross v. State


NO. 1998-DP-01038-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


954 So. 2d 968; 2007 Miss. LEXIS 235



April 26, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at Ross v. State, 22 So. 3d 400, 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 861 (Miss. Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TIPPAH COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/04/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. KENNETH COLEMAN.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of capital murder by a jury in the Circuit Court of Tippah County, Mississippi, and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed, challenging various aspects of his trial, including the trial court's denial of his new trial motion.


OVERVIEW: While troubled by the lack of substantial evidence against defendant, the supreme court could not find that the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion for a new trial. However, the supreme court did find independent, reversible error in the trial court's failure to adhere to Miss. Unif. Cir. & Cty. R. 9.04(I) in excluding the statement of the State's key witness taken by defendant's investigator. Another independent factor requiring reversal was defense counsel's failure to investigate substantial mitigating factors during sentencing. There were also other, cumulative errors that provided further justification for reversal including the State maintaining in closing argument that defendant had been seen at the crime scene when he had not, defense counsel's failure to explore the possible tainting of the venire panel, and the exclusion of the State's ballistics report from evidence. These errors were of particular concern because much of the State's case against defendant, absent the inconsistent testimony of its key witness, was indirect. In sum, the independent and cumulative errors during both the guilt and sentencing phases deprived defendant of a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed defendant's conviction and sentence and remanded the case for a new trial.

Lynch v. State


NO. 2004-DR-01085-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


951 So. 2d 549; 2007 Miss. LEXIS 34



February 15, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: BOLIVAR COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/05/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KENNETH L. THOMAS.
Lynch v. State, 877 So. 2d 1254, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 591 (Miss., 2004)



DISPOSITION: GRANTED IN PART; DENIED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, who was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death, sought leave to file a motion for postconviction relief in the Bolivar County Circuit Court, alleging claims of ineffective assistance of counsel, cruel and unusual punishment, the introduction of aggravating factors not set forth in the indictment, and the improper admission of crime scene photographs.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner's trial counsel also served as appellate counsel; thus, his claim of ineffective assistance of counsel was not procedurally barred pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. §§ 99-39-21(1) and 99-39-21(3) (2000) as it was unrealistic to expect an attorney to preserve an ineffective assistance claim as to his own performance. In addition, petitioner was entitled to a hearing on the matter as counsel's untimely disclosure of some mitigation witnesses led to their exclusion from the sentencing phase of the trial, which the trial court even characterized as ineffective assistance of counsel. In addition, counsel failed to pursue petitioner's mental retardation claim and to offer sufficient mitigating evidence. Petitioner's claims concerning cruel and unusual punishment just by being placed on death row and the alleged improper admission of photographs were procedurally barred by § 99-39-21 as they could have been raised on direct appeal. Petitioner was, however, entitled to a hearing on whether he was mentally retarded and, therefore, not competent to be executed based on the Eighth Amendment. Petitioner's IQ fell within the mildly retarded range, and further testing was required.


OUTCOME: The court granted the application as to the claims of ineffective assistance of counsel and cruel and unusual punishment insofar as that claim related to his alleged mental retardation.

Guice v. State


NO. 2004-CT-01931-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


952 So. 2d 129; 2007 Miss. LEXIS 9



January 11, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Guice v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 211 (Miss., Apr. 5, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Guice v. Mississippi, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 12594 (U.S., Nov. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/04/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WINSTON L. KIDD.
Guice v. State, 952 So. 2d 187, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 72 (Miss. Ct. App., 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of aggravated assault and sentenced as a habitual offender. The case was assigned to the Mississippi Court of Appeals, which affirmed the final judgment of conviction and sentence. Defendant's petition for writ of certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: The victim's sister testified that she answered the doorbell to find a person she did not know inquiring about her brother. Not knowing that his sister had already answered the door, the victim appeared. The stranger at the door pulled out a gun and started shooting. The sister immediately picked out the photograph of defendant as being the person who shot her brother. At trial, the sister also identified defendant as the shooter. On review, defendant requested that the supreme court reverse his conviction and discharge him, not only for the violation of the Sixth Amendment or state constitutional rights under Miss. Const. art. 3, § 26 (1890), but also for a perceived violation of Mississippi's speedy trial statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-17-1. The supreme court concluded that when the record was read in its totality, it was obvious that even the day of trial, defendant did not want a speedy trial. What defendant had demanded was a dismissal of the charge based on an alleged violation of his speedy trial rights, but defendant failed to demand a speedy trial. Moreover, part of the delay in this case was created by defendant's refusal to cooperate with his court-appointed counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed. The conviction and the sentence were affirmed.

US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Hodges v. Mississippi, 552 U.S. 1061, 128 S. Ct. 705, 169 L. Ed. 2d 552, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 12873 (2007)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part, Writ of habeas corpus denied, in part, Claim dismissed by, Motion dismissed by, As moot, Certificate of appealability denied, in part Hodges v. Epps, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 95406 (N.D. Miss., Sept. 13, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LOWNDES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT BY: MELANIE K. DOTSON THOMAS FORREST ALLGOOD. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/13/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN M. MONTGOMERY.

DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted of capital murder and was sentenced to death. After his conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal, he filed a petition for post-conviction relief in the court.


OVERVIEW: The inmate broke into the home of his ex-girlfriend, kidnaped her and her infant daughter, and killed the ex-girlfriend's brother. The inmate drove the ex-girlfriend to another state and raped her at gunpoint. The court found that the inmate raised most of his arguments in his direct appeal, and those issues were barred by res judicata pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21(3) (Supp. 2003). Those issues included prosecutorial misconduct, the introduction of prior bad acts, and jury instructions. Some claims of ineffective assistance of counsel were also barred by res judicata, but the court considered the claims in which the inmate introduced new extraneous materials. The claims were without merit. Evidence of his counsel's drug use and illness did not change the court's finding on direct appeal that the attorney provided effective assistance of counsel. The ex-girlfriend's unfair or manipulative conduct towards the inmate did not change the fact that he broke into her house and killed her brother. Even if counsel had been able to produce psychological evaluations at the time of trial, the evaluations were not that compelling, particularly in the context of a death penalty case.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for post-conviction relief.

Garrison v. State


NO. 2005-KA-01512-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


950 So. 2d 990; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 693; 33 A.L.R.6th 621



December 14, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by Garrison v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 192 (Miss., Mar. 15, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAFAYETTE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/29/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW K. HOWORTH.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of failing to register as a sex offender, in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 45-33-27. The Lafayette County Circuit Court (Mississippi) found that defendant was a habitual offender pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-83. The trial court then denied defendant's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict or, in the alternative, motion for a new trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court rejected defendant's ex post facto argument as the Mississippi statute was a civil, nonpunitive regulatory scheme. However, the claim that he lacked notice of the registration requirement, which resulted in a denial of his constitutional right to due process, had merit under federal precedent. Although ignorance of the law was generally not an excuse, in order to sustain a conviction under the applicable federal precedent, the jury had to find beyond a reasonable doubt that the State had proved that defendant had actual knowledge of the duty to register, or that the State had proved the probability of such knowledge. Since the issue of whether defendant had actual or probable knowledge of the duty to register as a sex offender was a factual issue for the jury to decide, the trial court had erred in refusing defendant's request for jury instruction requiring notice. The trial court had not improperly determined facts giving rise to defendant's lifetime habitual status where the post jury verdict hearing was relegated to proof regarding prior convictions for four separate felonies to which defendant had pled guilty.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court for a new trial.

 

182 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Creel v. State


NO. 2004-CT-01723-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


944 So. 2d 891; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 683



December 7, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/02/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT P. KREBS.
Creel v. State, 944 So. 2d 896, 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 805 (Miss. Ct. App., Nov. 1, 2005)



DISPOSITION: THE JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF APPEALS IS VACATED. THE JUDGMENT OF THE JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT IS REVERSED, AND THIS CASE IS REMANDED TO THE JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS IN ACCORDANCE WITH THIS OPINION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Jackson County Circuit Court, Mississippi, dismissed appellant's motion for post-conviction relief for lack of jurisdiction. The Mississippi Court of Appeals reversed and remanded. The State petitioned for writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that the circuit court's interpretation of Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-47(2)(a) (Rev. 2004) as pertaining to resentencing was erroneous because the statute did not pertain to resentencing; it pertained only to a suspension of the further execution of a sentence and to the placement of the convicted felon on earned probation. Because appellant's petition was filed under the Mississippi Uniform Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 99-39-1 to 27 (Supp. 2005), the circuit court erred in finding that it did not have jurisdiction and dismissing the petition. The circuit judge who ordered appellant to complete the Regimented Inmate Discipline program and then report back for possible alteration of the terms of the sentence intended that appellant should not be required to serve the remainder of his sentence as an inmate in a state penitentiary. The supreme court could not determine if, under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(1)(g), appellant's release was unlawfully revoked. Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-47(2)(a) was not relevant to the issues at hand, and both the circuit court and court of appeals erred when they applied this statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was vacated; the circuit court's dismissal of the petition was reversed, and the case remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

Arceo v. Tolliver


NO. 2005-IA-00652-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


949 So. 2d 691; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 650



November 16, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion to strike denied by, Motion to modify denied by Arceo v. Tolliver, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 157 (Miss., Feb. 22, 2007)
Decision reached on appeal by Arceo v. Tolliver, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 393 (Miss., Aug. 20, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/03/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BOBBY BURT DeLAUGHTER.
Arceo v. Tolliver, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 385 (Miss., Aug. 3, 2006)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a hospital and a doctor, appealed an interlocutory order of the Circuit Court for the First Judicial District of Hinds County (Mississippi), which refused to dismiss a medical malpractice case brought by plaintiff as a result of the death of plaintiff's daughter. Defendants had filed a motion to dismiss or alternatively a motion for summary judgment. Pending before the court was plaintiff's motion for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed that dismissal was proper because plaintiff failed to comply with the notice provisions of Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-36(15). On review, the court reversed the trial court's order and rendered judgment in favor of defendants. In considering the plain language of § 15-1-36(15), the court found that plaintiff wholly failed to provide any written notice to any medical provider concerning her intention to commence suit. Thus, the trial court erred in denying defendants' motion to dismiss defendants' motion. The court did not address the issue of the constitutionality of the statute because the issue was not raised on appeal. Although plaintiff had the constitutional right to seek redress in the state courts for the death of her daughter, she also had the responsibility to comply with § 15-1-36(15). Therefore, as a matter of law, defendants were entitled to dismissal of the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court denied plaintiff's motion for rehearing, withdrew its original opinion, and substituted the present opinion. The court reversed the trial court's order denying the defendants' motion to dismiss, or in the alternative, for summary judgment, and rendered judgment in favor of defendants, dismissing plaintiff's second amendment complaint and the present action without prejudice.

Champluvier v. State


NO. 2003-CT-02581-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


942 So. 2d 145; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 636



November 9, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Champluvier v. Riley, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 29551 (N.D. Miss., Apr. 8, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/15/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GRAY EVANS.
Champluvier v. State, 942 So. 2d 172, 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 1025 (Miss. Ct. App., 2005)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of embezzlement from a limited liability company. The Mississippi Court of Appeals affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that because she was accused of stealing from a limited liability company, she was guilty of no crime under the provisions of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-23-19, which applied only to corporations and private persons. The supreme court agreed. A limited liability company such as existed between defendant and her partner was not encompassed within the language of § 97-23-19 providing for a felony conviction upon embezzlement of certain therein described property belonging to an incorporated company or a private person. Therefore, the State did not present legally sufficient evidence to support a guilty verdict against defendant on each and every element of the crime of embezzlement as set out in § 97-23-19.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the charges were dismissed.

Brawner v. State


NO. 2004-DR-00913-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


947 So. 2d 254; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 625



October 26, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Brawner v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 107 (Miss., Feb. 8, 2007)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by, Certificate of appealability denied Brawner v. Epps, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 7487 (N.D. Miss., Jan. 27, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TATE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/12/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW C. BAKER.
Brawner v. State, 872 So. 2d 1, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 458 (Miss., 2004)



DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought post-conviction relief under Miss. Code Ann. §§ 99-39-1 to 99-39-29 from a judgment of the Tate County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicting him of four counts of capital murder and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted for shooting the four victims to death. On the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief, the court held that defense counsel's decision not to seek a change of venue was beyond its review. The inmate was not prejudiced by counsel's failure to transcribe the full record because the inmate did not claim any specific error arising from the non-transcribed sections of the record. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to present mitigating evidence at sentencing because it was the inmate's choice not to do so; the inmate was fully apprised of the consequences of his choice and he made an informed and voluntary decision not to presenting mitigating evidence. The inmate's claim that the use of the robbery aggravating factor during sentencing was inappropriate as it allowed the use of the underlying felony, which elevated the crime to capital murder, was procedurally barred under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21(1) because it could have been raised on direct appeal and was not. The inmate's claim that the use of the avoiding arrest aggravating factor without a limiting instruction was unconstitutional was also procedurally barred.


OUTCOME: The inmate's petition for post-conviction relief was denied.

Powers v. State

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Powers v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 77 (Miss., Jan. 18, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Powers v. Mississippi, 551 U.S. 1149, 127 S. Ct. 3006, 168 L. Ed. 2d 733, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 8389 (2007)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by, As moot, Motion denied by, Request denied by, As moot, Stay denied by, in part, Request granted, in part Powers v. Epps, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 33741 (S.D. Miss., Mar. 31, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/15/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. RICHARD W. McKENZIE.
Powers v. State, 883 So. 2d 20, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 850 (Miss., 2003)



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION FOR LEAVE TO FILE MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF, DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Postconviction applicant was convicted in the Forrest County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of murder and attempted rape. The applicant was sentenced to death. The applicant filed a request for leave to file a motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The applicant argued, inter alia, that counsel was ineffective for failing to obtain expert assistance. In addition to finding that the issue was procedurally barred, the supreme court found the issue to be without merit. The State called a forensic pathologist, who testified that the victim suffered defensive wounds on both arms as well as her right leg. The applicant offered an affidavit of a forensic dentist who asserted that the positioning of the victim's body was "staged" by the perpetrator for some reason other than attempted rape. The dentist was also a licensed attorney in California and a certified senior crime scene analyst. Likewise, the dentist had been the Deputy Medical Examiner for the Ventura County Coroner's Office since 1988. He had testified as an expert in the field of forensic dentistry in several states and additionally, he had published articles and textbooks on forensic dental evidence. It was doubtful that expert testimony regarding the positioning of the body would have likely resulted in a different verdict. The victim was found nude from the waist down with her shorts and underwear bunched at one ankle, as well as with five gunshot wounds to her head.


OUTCOME: The application for leave to file a motion for postconviction relief was denied.

Bayview Land, Ltd. v. State


NO. 2004-CA-01415-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


950 So. 2d 966; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 546



October 12, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Bayview Land, Ltd. v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 634 (Miss., Mar. 22, 2007)
Rehearing denied by, En banc Bayview Land, Ltd. v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 632 (Miss., Mar. 22, 2007)
Rehearing denied by, En banc Bayview Land, Ltd. v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 633 (Miss., Mar. 22, 2007)
Rehearing denied by, En banc Bayview Land, Ltd. v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 630 (Miss., Mar. 22, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/22/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DONALD B. PATTERSON.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, land companies and limited partnerships, challenged a decision of the Harrison County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which found in favor of appellee State in an ownership dispute between the parties regarding land upon which appellants had built a parking garage and hotel that consisted of 3 acres of artificial accretions.


OVERVIEW: Appellants filed a declaratory action to settle the dispute over the land, and the State claimed ownership pursuant to the Public Trust Tidelands Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 29-15-1, et seq. (Rev. 2005). The State had the burden to show that any pre-1973 accretions were not done pursuant to a constitutional legislative enactment and for a higher purpose. The court reversed and held that the State failed to meet its burden to prove that the artificial accretions above the mean high water line were not done pursuant to a constitutional legislative enactment and for a higher public purpose. Therefore, a hearing was warranted to determine the mean high water line nearest the effective date of the Coastal Wetlands Protection Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 49-27-1, et seq. Appellants' predecessor's 1928 public land patent from the State was at a time when the property at issue was being utilized, albeit by a private company, to promote the State's booming oyster industry. The chancellor erred in finding that the conveyance by the State to a predecessor of appellants was null and void for want of authority because the evidence revealed a 1943 deed to the patented area.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded.

McLendon v. State


NO. 2005-KM-01480-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


945 So. 2d 372; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 548



October 12, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by McLendon v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 83 (Miss., Jan. 18, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by McLENDON, MILTON L. v. MISSISSIPPI, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 8338 (U.S., June 25, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Wayne County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicting him of driving under the influence (DUI) in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30 (Rev. 2004).


OVERVIEW: After police officers stopped defendant at a routine roadblock, they smelled an intoxicating beverage. Defendant failed field sobriety tests and had a breath-alcohol content of 0.13 percent, and was subsequently arrested and convicted of DUI. On appeal, the court held that defendant's seizure at the roadblock was constitutional because its primary purpose was to check for driver's licenses and insurance cards and because the officers were consistently and indiscriminately stopping every vehicle coming through the roadblock. The trial court properly denied defendant's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict because there was legally sufficient evidence for the trial court to find defendant guilty of DUI. It was established that defendant had a breath-alcohol content of 0.13 percent through the testimony of an officer, a printout from a completed intoxilyzer test, and a uniform traffic ticket. A second officer testified that the field sobriety test was given on the basis of the smell of an intoxicating beverage on defendant's breath. The trial court also properly denied defendant's motion for a new trial.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

Dedeaux Util. Co. v. City of Gulfport


NO. 2005-CA-00102-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


938 So. 2d 838; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 529



September 28, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Dedeaux Util. Co. v. City of Gulfport, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 191 (Miss., Apr. 7, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY SPECIAL COURT OF EMINENT DOMAIN. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/13/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. T. LARRY WILSON.



DISPOSITION: ON DIRECT AND CROSS-APPEAL: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant private utility and appellee city challenged a judgment of the Harrison County Special Court of Eminent Domain (Mississippi) that was entered in accordance with a jury verdict, determined the value of the utility to be $ 3,634,757.00, and awarded judgment interest. The city had filed a petition for condemnation after the utility land was annexed into the city and the parties failed to agree upon the value of the utility.


OVERVIEW: The utility challenged the city's evidence, arguing that it was improperly based on data from the Public Service Commission (PSC) used to set rates and did not include the value of "contributed property" from land developers. The city challenged the value determination and the award of interest. The court held that the trial court erred in failing to strike the city's expert's testimony because "contributed property" must be included in the utility's value for condemnation purposes even though such items were not included for purposes of rate-regulation. Also the trial court erred by excluding the utility's evidence as to the value of 4 parcels of land without improvements because the value of the land upon which the utility was built should have been considered as one factor in determining just compensation. The court found that the trial court erred when it compounded the interest and made a distinction between pre- and post-judgment interest because Miss. Code Ann. § 11-27-19 was the specific eminent domain provision for interest and eminent domain judgments were not based on notes, accounts, sales or contracts; therefore Miss. Code Ann. §§ 75-17-1(1) and 75-17-7 did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment and remanded the case for a new trial.

Howard v. State


NO. 2003-DR-01881-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


945 So. 2d 326; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 531



September 28, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Howard v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 76 (Miss., Jan. 18, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Howard v. Mississippi, 552 U.S. 829, 128 S. Ct. 49, 169 L. Ed. 2d 43, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 9278 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LOWNDES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/25/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LEE J. HOWARD.
Howard v. State, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 197 (Miss., Apr. 13, 2006)



DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed an application for postconviction collateral relief after he was convicted of capital murder with the underlying felony of rape and received the death penalty in the Lowndes County Circuit Court (Mississippi).


OVERVIEW: A victim was found dead when a fire was spotted at her residence. The inmate was convicted and given the death penalty. After the conviction and sentence were affirmed, the inmate sought postconviction relief. In denying such, the supreme court determined that there were no due process violations under Brady since defendant received all exculpatory evidence. Next, defendant's Sixth Amendment right to effective assistance of counsel was not violated either. The decision to move for a change of venue was merely trial strategy. Moreover, the failure to discover perjured testimony and the failure to call witnesses for an alibi did not amount to ineffective assistance of counsel. Even though the failure to call an expert regarding the bite marks was deficient, there was no prejudice shown because the inmate did not show that he did not bite the victim. Moreover, the inmate was not entitled to formal notice of the aggravating factors used by the prosecution. Also, the circuit court did not err by denying discovery under Miss. R. App. 22 because the inmate failed to show that it was not frivolous or how it would have helped in the preparation of specific postconviction relief issues.


OUTCOME: The petition for postconviction relief was denied.

Rubenstein v. State


NO. 2000-DP-00727-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


941 So. 2d 735; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 411



August 10, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Rubenstein v. State, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 713 (Miss., Nov. 16, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PIKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/05/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KEITH STARRETT.
Rubenstein v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 789 (Miss., Dec. 1, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Pike County Circuit Court (Mississippi), of capital murder of a child while engaged in the commission of felonious child abuse the murder of his stepson, who was the child's father, and the murder of the stepson's wife under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19. Defendant was sentenced to death on the child's murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant took the victims to his cabin and left them there. Over a month later, the victims' bodies were found. The court found that testimony admitted regarding an insurance scam with defendant was properly admitted under Miss. R. Evid. 403, 404(b), and 804(b)(5) because the declarant was unavailable and because the trial court analyzed the five requirements for admission of the hearsay. Further, defendant's confrontation rights were found not violated under U.S. Const. amend. VI or Miss. Const. art. III, § 26 in the Crawford did not apply because the statements were not testimonial hearsay. Testimony of defendant's prior bad acts was not objected to and thus any errors were procedurally barred and the trial court was not required to sua sponte give a limiting instruction on the evidence. Several other issues were procedurally barred because defendant failed to object. The jury instruction defining child abuse was proper because it tracked the language of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-5-39(2)(a). However, the trial court did not, as required, instruct the jury as to the option of life without parole as provided in Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment as to the convictions and to the life sentences for the two murder convictions. The court reversed and remanded for resentencing on the capital murder charge.

Arceo v. Tolliver


NO. 2005-IA-00652-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


2006 Miss. LEXIS 385



August 3, 2006, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Arceo v. Tolliver, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 402 (Miss., Aug. 3, 2006)
Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Rehearing denied by, Judgment entered by Arceo v. Tolliver, 949 So. 2d 691, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 650 (Miss., 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/03/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BOBBY BURT DeLAUGHTER.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice suit, appellant physician and appellant hospital moved to dismiss the action due to appellee executrix's failure to give the required statutory notice. The Hinds County Circuit Court, Mississippi, denied the motion. The physician and the hospital sought interlocutory appeal, which was granted under Miss. R. App. P. 5.


OVERVIEW: The patient, who was the executrix's daughter, was seen and evaluated in the hospital's emergency room. Nevertheless, the patient died. The hospital and the physician framed the issues in this way: (1) Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-36(15) (Rev. 2003) required a 60-day notice of the intention to bring a medical malpractice suit; therefore, did noncompliance with the notice provisions require dismissal? (2) Was the action now time-barred? (3) Should leave to amend have been denied because the statute required dismissal? The executrix in the case wholly failed to provide written notice to any medical provider. Under Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-36(1) (Rev. 2003), the executrix had two years from the date of the alleged negligent act in which to commence the lawsuit against medical providers. The trial court erred in denying the motion to dismiss, or in the alternative, a motion for summary judgment. The supreme court noted that in applying the statute requiring notice, the executrix was not deprived of any constitutional right.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the trial court's judgment, and it rendered judgment in favor of the physician and the hospital.

State v. Bd. of Levee Comm'rs


NO. 2005-SA-00104-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


932 So. 2d 12; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 318



June 15, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: COAHOMA COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/20/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM G. WILLARD, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the State of Mississippi, its fiscal officer, and attorney general, sought review of an order from the Coahoma County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which entered summary judgment in favor of appellee board of levee commissioners and declared H.B. 1279, § 7(4) (Miss. 2004) (bill), requiring the board to transfer funds to the State, unconstitutional and granted an injunction to prevent its enforcement.


OVERVIEW: The board argued, among other things, that the bill was unconstitutional because it violated Miss. Const. art. XI, § 227 et seq. in that the legislature did not have the authority to require the transfer of board funds for use in a state budget contingency fund. In affirming, the court agreed, and held that the bill, in authorizing the use of board funds for non-levee purposes, plainly conflicted with the clear language of Miss. Const. art. XI, §§ 232 and 236 and was, therefore, unconstitutional. Noting that Miss. Const. art. XI, § 232 gave the board plenary authority to deal with the erection, maintenance, and repair of the levee system, the court first found that, although the board was subject to legislative control absent constitutional provision otherwise, the framers did not grant legislative authority to frustrate the purposes of any constitutionally-created organization. Next, the court found that, because the bill required board funds be converted to the budget contingency fund for use other than levee purposes, the legislature overstepped the limitation set forth in Miss. Const. art. XI, § 236, which expressly prohibited the use of board funds for non-levee purposes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that the bill was unconstitutional.

 

194 of 603 DOCUMENTS



Mayor & Bd. of Aldermen v. Homebuilders Ass'n of Miss., Inc.


NO. 2004-CC-01278-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


932 So. 2d 44; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 319



June 15, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/24/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DALE HARKEY.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a case brought by plaintiffs, a home builders association and others, challenging defendant city's adoption of development impact fees for various municipal improvements, services, equipment, and vehicles, the Jackson County Circuit Court, Mississippi, held the fees to be a void taxing measure and enjoined further collection of the fees. The city appealed the ruling.


OVERVIEW: The impact fees were to be paid in addition to any and all other applicable land-use, zoning, planning, adequate public facilities, platting, or other related fees, requirements, standards, and conditions imposed by the city. The court concluded that the impact fees constituted a tax that the city had no authority to assess. The fees did not qualify as regulatory in nature because no special benefit was conferred on the fee payer. The fees did not cover administrative expenses incurred by the city because the fees were not based on the administrative expense the city incurred in issuing a building permit. The fees constituted a tax because the fees were simply a revenue-raising measure. Because the fees constituted a tax, the city was required to have enabling legislation in order to levy and collect the tax. The state's municipal planning statutes, Miss. Code Ann. § 17-1-1 et seq., did not grant the city authority to adopt impact fees or other revenue raising mechanisms to implement its comprehensive plan. The home rule statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 21-17-5, did not authorize the city to impose a tax unless such tax was specifically authorized by another statute or state law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bennett v. State


NO. 2003-DP-00765-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


933 So. 2d 930; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 246



May 11, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Bennett v. State, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 413 (Miss., Aug. 3, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bennett v. Mississippi, 127 S. Ct. 976, 166 L. Ed. 2d 740, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 351 (U.S., 2007)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Petition granted by, in part, Petition denied by, in part Bennett v. State, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 417 (Miss., Aug. 28, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 02/28/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM E. CHAPMAN, III.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Rankin County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of capital murder and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in refusing to accept his plea to the lesser included offense of heat of passion manslaughter. The supreme court disagreed. Defendant informed the trial court that he disagreed with the factual basis for the plea. Defense counsel clarified that defendant would "admit he shook the baby, but not that he threw him to the floor." The State objected, asserting that the head injury - the cause of death - did not come from the shaking but rather from blunt force trauma. When the trial court attempted to resolve the discrepancy, defendant maintained that he found the child on the floor not breathing, and all he did was pick him up and shake him to get him to start breathing. The trial court's refusal to accept the guilty plea was not error. Defendant refused to admit that he inflicted the blunt force head trauma that caused his son's death. Considering defendant's limited admission together with the pre-trial documentary evidence, the trial court properly determined that defendant failed to admit sufficient facts to justify heat of passion manslaughter.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

196 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. AG


NO. 2004-SA-02418-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


935 So. 2d 856; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 244



May 11, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Davis v. AG, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 561 (Miss., Aug. 24, 2006)
Motion dismissed by Davis v. AG of Miss., 2006 Miss. LEXIS 562 (Miss., Aug. 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/02/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. STUART ROBINSON.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged a decision from the Hinds County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which entered summary judgment in favor of appellees, the Mississippi Attorney General and the Mississippi Department of Finance and Administration (DFA), in an action seeking a refund of taxes paid under Miss. Code Ann. § 27-73-1.


OVERVIEW: The Mississippi Tax Commission assessed the taxpayers with additional income tax, penalties, and interest for the tax years 1990 to 1995. The taxpayers failed to file an appeal from the order. Over two years later, they filed a refund claim under Miss. Code Ann. § 27-73-1. The request was denied, and the chancery court granted summary judgment to the attorney general and the DFA in a subsequent judicial action. The taxpayers then sought review. In affirming, the appellate court determined that they failed to exhaust their administrative remedies. The taxpayers had 30 days to appeal under Miss. Code Ann. § 27-7-73 (repealed 2005) after the procedures in Miss. Code Ann. § 27-7-71 (repealed 2005) were utilized. When they failed to do so, the determination became a final adjudication. The doctrines of res judicata and collateral estoppel barred any further action. This precluded the taxpayers from subsequently seeking relief under Miss. Code Ann. § 27-73-1. Even if such an action was permissible, it would have been time barred under Miss. Code Ann. § 27-73-5. Finally, the appellate court was not required to consider the constitutional arguments.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

197 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Dobbins v. Coleman


NO. 2004-CA-02365-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


930 So. 2d 1246; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 191



April 13, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Dobbins v. Coleman, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 326 (Miss., June 15, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/08/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MITCHELL M. LUNDY, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother sought review of an order from the Desoto County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which made her equally responsible with respondent father for their child's medical expenses. The father challenged an order awarding the mother reasonable attorney fees pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 93-9-45 after she brought and maintained a petition to establish paternity for filiation, child support, and other relief.


OVERVIEW: The mother gave birth to a child out of wedlock. She filed a petition to establish paternity, child support, and other relief. After establishing paternity, the trial judge ordered the father to include the child under his medical insurance. The trial judge made the parties equally responsible for the balances of the existing medical bills and required them to split all future medical bills for the child. The trial judge ordered the father to reimburse the mother for her attorney fees. On appeal, the mother claimed that the trial court erred in not making the father responsible for the full amount of the child's medical expenses. The court found that the trial judge did not declare Miss. Code Ann. § 93-9-7 unconstitutional. The trial judge merely stated that an inaccurate interpretation of the statute making the father solely responsible for all of the child's medical expenses would violate equal protection laws. The trial judge made a permissible division of the financial responsibility for medical expenses. As to the award of attorney fees pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 93-9-45, the record did not support the father's assertion that the mother's attorney fees were unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the trial court.

 

198 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Trainer v. State


NO. 2004-CA-01955-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


930 So. 2d 373; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 178



April 6, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Trainer v. State, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 308 (Miss., June 8, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WASHINGTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/05/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. RICHARD A. SMITH.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Washington County Circuit Court, Mississippi, granted appellee's, State of Mississippi, motion to dismiss appellant business owner's suit to challenge the constitutionality of the criminal statutes under which he was arrested and under which the gambling machines and money were seized. The trial court found that the machines were illegal gambling devices, and that the owner had no property rights in the contraband. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner challenged the constitutionality of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-33-7, and Miss. Code Ann. § 97-33-17. The owner claimed he was deprived of a property right in the machines, and profits from the machines, without a hearing to determine if his machines were covered by the statute or if the seizure was valid. The supreme court noted that illegal gambling machines were those that were operated by coin, token, or other consideration, and dispensed a product with the possibility of dispensing additional items at varying quantities. The U.S. Constitution applied to every statute. The owner did not meet his burden of showing that he was being deprived of his property without due process of law because the criminal statutes, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-33-7, -17, were not too broad in their description of what caused a video game to be an illegal slot machine. A person with ordinary intelligence would have little difficulty determining what exactly was prohibited. Mississippi did not extend a property right to illegal gambling machines. There was no due process rights violation and Miss. Code Ann. § 97-33-7(2) was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

199 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Havard v. State


NO. 2003-DP-00457-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


928 So. 2d 771; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 90



February 9, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Havard v. State, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 297 (Miss., May 25, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Havard v. Mississippi, 549 U.S. 1119, 127 S. Ct. 931, 166 L. Ed. 2d 716, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 153 (2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Havard v. State, 988 So. 2d 322, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 264 (Miss., 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at Havard v. State, 86 So. 3d 896, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 118 (Miss., 2012)
Post-conviction proceeding at Havard v. State, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 161 (Miss., Apr. 2, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: ADAMS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/19/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FORREST A. JOHNSON, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury for the Adams County Circuit Court (Mississippi) found defendant guilty of capital murder (murder during the commission of a sexual battery) of the six-month old victim, the same jury found that he should suffer the penalty of death. Consistent with the jury verdict, the trial court imposed the death sentence upon defendant, and it was from that final judgment that defendant appealed to the state supreme court.


OVERVIEW: In a videotaped statement two days after the victim's death, defendant denied committing sexual battery on her, but instead claimed he accidentally dropped her against the commode after bathing her, shook her in a panic, and then rubbed her down with lavender lotion before putting her to bed. Defendant argued that his representation was ineffective at several points during the trial, violating his Sixth Amendment right to effective counsel. But, the supreme court found that his counsel was not ineffective because (1) a potential juror made no indication during the extensive questioning following her objectionable comments that in any way revealed she would be unable to be fair and impartial in deciding whether defendant was guilty or not guilty, and if found guilty, in deciding the appropriate sentence; (2) the trial judge asked if any potential juror would automatically vote for or against the death penalty and, thus, defense counsel was not ineffective in failing to repeat that line of questioning; and (3) given the testimony provided in mitigation of punishment and what it did show the jury about defendant's life and tendencies, counsel's performance was not deficient.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

200 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Spicer v. State


NO. 2003-DP-02281-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


921 So. 2d 292; 2006 Miss. LEXIS 20



January 5, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Rehearing denied by Spicer v. State, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 107 (Miss., Mar. 2, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Spicer v. Mississippi, 127 S. Ct. 493, 166 L. Ed. 2d 364, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 8022 (U.S., 2006)
Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Post-conviction relief denied at, in part Spicer v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 619 (Miss., Nov. 8, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GEORGE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/1/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DALE HARKEY.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the George County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of capital murder and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction because the evidence was insufficient to sustain the underlying robbery conviction. The supreme court disagreed. Defendant elicited testimony from the owner of a convenience store in Jackson County which defendant and the victim frequented, stating that he had observed at times previous to the murder defendant driving the victim's truck alone. Defendant was attempting to prove that the victim allowed him to borrow the truck and thus he had permission to drive the truck the day he was caught in Jackson County. However, officers discovered defendant in possession of the victim's truck and a sword taken from the victim's trailer. Possession of the victim's property created a reasonable inference that the property was stolen. Therefore, a reasonable juror could have determined that defendant stole the victim's property. In addition to his possession of the property, there was testimony that defendant admitted that the truck was stolen. Accordingly, there was enough legally sufficient evidence to determine that defendant robbed the victim and to convict defendant of capital murder.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
